10102{_}807{_}"Then quick!
10102{_}808{_}Fly from this house this instant.
10102{_}809{_}If you are stopped, then use your revolver.
10102{_}810{_}Don't hesitate.
10102{_}811{_}In a moment they will be here upon you."
10102{_}812{_}"But who are they, Olinto?
10102{_}813{_}You must tell me," I cried in desperation.
10102{_}814{_}"_Dio!_ Go!
10102{_}815{_}Go!"
10102{_}816{_}he cried, pushing me violently towards the door.
10102{_}817{_}"Fly, or we shall both die--both of us!
10102{_}818{_}Run downstairs.
10102{_}819{_}I must make feint of dashing after you."
10102{_}820{_}I turned, and seeing his desperate eagerness, precipitately fled, while he ran down behind me, uttering fierce imprecations in Italian, as though I had escaped him.
10102{_}821{_}A man in the narrow dark passage attempted to trip me up as I ran, but I fired point blank at him, and gaining the door unlocked it, and an instant later found myself out in the street.
10102{_}822{_}It was the narrowest escape from death that I had ever had in all my life--surely the strangest and most remarkable adventure.
10102{_}823{_}What, I wondered, did it mean?
10102{_}824{_}Next morning I searched up and down Oxford Street for the Restaurant Milano, but could not find it.
10102{_}825{_}I asked shopkeepers, postmen, and policemen; I examined the London Directory at the bar of the Oxford Music Hall, and made every inquiry possible.
10102{_}826{_}But all was to no purpose.
10102{_}827{_}No one knew of such a place.
10102{_}828{_}There were restaurants in plenty in Oxford Street, from the Frascati down to the humble coffeeshop, but nobody had ever heard of the "Milano."
10102{_}829{_}Even Olinto had played me false!
10102{_}830{_}I was filled with chagrin, for I had trusted him as honest, upright, and industrious; and was puzzled to know the reason he had deceived me, and why he had enticed me to the very brink of the grave.
10102{_}831{_}He had told me that he himself had fallen into the trap laid by my enemies, and yet he had steadfastly refused to tell me who they were!
10102{_}832{_}The whole thing was utterly inexplicable.
10102{_}833{_}I drove over to Lambeth and wandered through the maze of mean streets off the York Road, yet for the life of me I could not decide into which house I had been taken.
10102{_}834{_}There were a dozen which seemed to me that they might be the identical house from which I had so narrowly escaped with my life.
10102{_}835{_}Gradually it became impressed upon me that my ex-servant had somehow gained knowledge that I was in London, that he had watched my exit from the club, and that all his pitiful story regarding Armida was false.
10102{_}836{_}He was the envoy of my unknown enemies, who had so ingeniously and so relentlessly plotted my destruction.
10102{_}837{_}That I had enemies I knew quite well.
10102{_}838{_}The man who believes he has not is an arrant fool.
10102{_}839{_}There is no man breathing who has not an enemy, from the pauper in the workhouse to the king in his automobile.
10102{_}840{_}But the unseen enemy is always the more dangerous; hence my deep apprehensive reflections that day as I walked those sordid back streets "over the water," as the Cockney refers to the district between those two main arteries of traffic, the Waterloo and Westminster Bridge Roads.
10102{_}841{_}My unknown enemies had secured the services of Olinto in their dastardly plot to kill me.
10102{_}842{_}With what motive?
10102{_}843{_}I wondered as I crossed Waterloo Bridge to the Strand, whether Olinto Santini would again approach me and make the promised explanation.
10102{_}844{_}I had given my word not to prejudge him until he revealed to me the truth.
10102{_}845{_}Yet I could not, in the circumstances, repose entire confidence in him.
10102{_}846{_}When one's enemies are unknown, the feeling of apprehension is always much greater, for in the imagination danger lurks in every corner, and every action of a friend covers the ruse of a suspected enemy.
10102{_}847{_}That day I did my business in the city with a distrust of everyone, not knowing whether I was not followed or whether those who sought my life were not plotting some other equally ingenious move whereby I might go innocently to my death.
10102{_}848{_}I endeavored to discover Olinto by every possible means during those stifling days that followed.
10102{_}849{_}The heat of London was, to me, more oppressive than the fiery sunshine of the old-world Tuscany, and everyone who could be out of town had left for the country or the sea.
10102{_}850{_}The only trace I found of the Italian was that he was registered at the office of the International Society of Hotel Servants, in Shaftesbury Avenue, as being employed at Gatti's Adelaide Gallery, but on inquiry there I found he had left more than a year before, and none of his fellow-waiters knew his whereabouts.
10102{_}851{_}Thus being defeated in every inquiry, and my business at last concluded in London, I went up to Dumfries on a duty visit which I paid annually to my uncle, Sir George Little.
10102{_}852{_}Having known Dumfries since my earliest boyhood, and having spent some years of my youth there, I had many friends in the vicinity, for Sir George and my aunt were very popular in the county and moved in the best set.
10102{_}853{_}Each time I returned from abroad I was always a welcome guest at Greenlaw, as their place outside the city of Burns was called, and this occasion proved no exception, for the country houses of Dumfries are always gay in August in prospect of the shooting.
10102{_}854{_}"Some new people have taken Rannoch Castle.
10102{_}855{_}Rather nice they seem," remarked my aunt as we were sitting together at luncheon the day after my arrival.
10102{_}856{_}"Their name is Leithcourt, and they've asked me to drive you over there to tennis this afternoon."
10102{_}857{_}"I'm not much of a player, you know, aunt.
10102{_}858{_}In Italy we don't believe in athletics.
10102{_}859{_}But if it's out of politeness, of course, I'll go."
10102{_}860{_}"Very well," she said.
10102{_}861{_}"Then I'll order the victoria for three."
10102{_}862{_}"There are several nice girls there, Gordon," remarked my uncle mischievously.
10102{_}863{_}"You have a good time, so don't think you are going to be bored."
10102{_}864{_}"No fear of that," was my answer.
10102{_}865{_}And at three o'clock Sir George, his wife, and myself set out for that fine old historic castle that stands high on the Bognie, overlooking the Cairn waters beyond Dunscore, one of the strongholds of the Black Douglas in those turbulent days of long ago, and now a splendid old residence with a big shoot which was sometimes let for the season at a very high rent by its aristocratic if somewhat impecunious owner.
10102{_}866{_}We could see its great round towers, standing grim and gray on the hillside commanding the whole of the valley, long before we approached it, and when we drove into the grounds we found a gay party in summer toilettes assembled on the ancient bowling-green, now transformed into a modern tennis-lawn.
10102{_}867{_}Mrs. Leithcourt and her husband, a tall, thin, gray-headed, well-dressed man, both came forward to greet us, and after a few introductions I joined a set at tennis.
10102{_}868{_}They were a merry crowd.
10102{_}869{_}The Leithcourts were entertaining a large house-party, and their hospitality was on a scale quite in keeping with the fine old place they rented.
10102{_}870{_}Tea was served on the lawn by the footmen, and afterwards, being tired of the game, I found myself strolling with Muriel Leithcourt, a bright, dark-eyed girl with tightly-bound hair, and wearing a cotton blouse and flannel tennis skirt.
10102{_}871{_}I was apologizing for my terribly bad play, explaining that I had no practice out in Italy, whereupon she said--  "I know Italy slightly.
10102{_}872{_}I was in Florence and Naples with mother last season."
10102{_}873{_}And then we began to discuss pictures and sculptures and the sights of Italy generally.
10102{_}874{_}I discerned from her remarks that she had traveled widely; indeed, she told me that both her father and mother were never happier than when moving from place to place in search of variety and distraction.
10102{_}875{_}We had entered the huge paneled hall of the Castle, and had passed up the quaint old stone staircase to the long banqueting hall with its paneled oak ceiling, which in these modern days had been transformed into a bright, pleasant drawing-room, from the windows of which was presented a marvelous view over the lovely Nithsdale and across to the heather-clad hills beyond.
10102{_}876{_}It was pleasant lounging there in the cool old room after the hot sunshine outside, and as I gazed around the place I noted how much more luxurious and tasteful it now was to what it had been in the days when I had visited its owner several years before.
10102{_}877{_}"We are awfully glad to be up here," my pretty companion was saying.
10102{_}878{_}"We had such a busy season in London."
10102{_}879{_}And then she went on to describe the Court ball, and two or three of the most notable functions about which I had read in my English paper beside the Mediterranean.
10102{_}880{_}She attracted me on account of her bright vivacity, quick wit and keen sense of humor, therefore I sat listening to her pleasant chatter.
10102{_}881{_}Exiled as I was in a foreign land, I seldom spoke English save with Hutcheson, the Consul, and even then we generally spoke Italian if there were others present, in order that our companions should understand.
10102{_}882{_}Therefore her gossip interested me, and as the golden sunset flooded the handsome old room I sat listening to her, inwardly admiring her innate grace and handsome countenance.
10102{_}883{_}I had no idea who or what her father was--whether a wealthy manufacturer, like so many who take expensive shoots and give big entertainments in order to edge their way into Society by its back door, or whether he was a gentleman of means and of good family.
10102{_}884{_}I rather guessed the latter, from his gentlemanly bearing and polished manner.
10102{_}885{_}His appearance, tall and erect, was that of a retired officer, and his clean-cut face was one of marked distinction.
10102{_}886{_}I was telling my pretty companion something of my own life, how, because I loved Italy so well, I lived in Tuscany in preference to living in England, and how each year I came home for a month or two to visit my relations and to keep in touch with things.
10102{_}887{_}Suddenly she said--  "I was once in Leghorn for a few hours.
10102{_}888{_}We were yachting in the Mediterranean.
10102{_}889{_}I love the sea--and yachting is such awfully good fun, if you only get decent weather."
10102{_}890{_}The mention of yachting brought back to my mind the visit of the _Lola_ and its mysterious sequel.
10102{_}891{_}"Your father has a yacht, then?"
10102{_}892{_}I remarked, with as little concern as I could.
10102{_}893{_}"Yes.
10102{_}894{_}The _Iris_.
10102{_}895{_}My uncle is cruising on her up the Norwegian Fiords.
10102{_}896{_}For us it is a change to be here, because we are so often afloat.
10102{_}897{_}We went across to New York in her last year and had a most delightful time--except for one bad squall which made us all a little bit nervous.
10102{_}898{_}But Moyes is such an excellent captain that I never fear.
10102{_}899{_}The crew are all North Sea fishermen--father will engage nobody else.
10102{_}900{_}I don't blame him."
10102{_}901{_}"So you must have made many long voyages, and seen many odd corners of the world, Miss Leithcourt?"
10102{_}902{_}I remarked, my interest in her increasing, for she seemed so extremely intelligent and well-informed.
10102{_}903{_}"Oh, yes.
10102{_}904{_}We've been to Mexico, and to Panama, besides Morocco, Egypt, and the West Coast of Africa."
10102{_}905{_}"And you've actually landed at Leghorn!"
10102{_}906{_}I remarked.
10102{_}907{_}"Yes, but we didn't stay there more than an hour--to send a telegram, I think it was.
10102{_}908{_}Father said there was nothing to see there.
10102{_}909{_}He and I went ashore, and I must say I was rather disappointed."
10102{_}910{_}"You are quite right.
10102{_}911{_}The town itself is ugly and uninteresting.
10102{_}912{_}But the outskirts--San Jacopo, Ardenza and Antigniano are all delightful.
10102{_}913{_}It was unfortunate that you did not see them.
10102{_}914{_}Was it long ago when you put in there?"
10102{_}915{_}"Not very long.
10102{_}916{_}I really don't recollect the exact date," was her reply.
10102{_}917{_}"We were on our way home from Alexandria."
10102{_}918{_}"Have you ever, in any of the ports you've been, seen a yacht called the _Lola_?"
10102{_}919{_}I asked eagerly, for it occurred to me that perhaps she might be able to give me information.
10102{_}920{_}"The _Lola_!"
10102{_}921{_}she gasped, and instantly her face changed.
10102{_}922{_}A flush overspread her cheeks, succeeded next moment by a death-like pallor.
10102{_}923{_}"The _Lola_!"
10102{_}924{_}she repeated in a strange, hoarse voice, at the same time endeavoring strenuously not to exhibit any apprehension.
10102{_}925{_}"No.
10102{_}926{_}I have never heard of any such a vessel.
10102{_}927{_}Is she a steam-yacht?
10102{_}928{_}Who's her owner?"
10102{_}929{_}I regarded her in amazement and suspicion, for I saw that mention of the name had aroused within her some serious misgiving.
10102{_}930{_}That look in her dark eyes as they fixed themselves upon me was one of distinct and unspeakable terror.
10102{_}931{_}What could she possibly know concerning the mysterious craft?
10102{_}932{_}"I don't know the owner's name," I said, still affecting not to have noticed her alarm and apprehension.
10102{_}933{_}"The vessel ran aground at the Meloria, a dangerous shoal outside Leghorn, and through the stupidity of her captain was very nearly lost."
10102{_}934{_}"Yes?"
10102{_}935{_}she gasped, in a half-whisper, bending to me eagerly, unable to sufficiently conceal the terrible anxiety consuming her.
10102{_}936{_}"And you--did you go aboard her?"
10102{_}937{_}"Yes," was the only word I uttered.
10102{_}938{_}A silence fell between us, and as my eyes fixed themselves upon her, I saw that from her handsome mobile countenance all the light and life had suddenly gone out, and I knew that she was in secret possession of the key to that remarkable enigma that so puzzled me.
10102{_}939{_}Of a sudden the door opened, and a voice cried gayly--  "Why, I've been looking everywhere for you, Muriel.
10102{_}940{_}Why are you hidden here?
10102{_}941{_}Aren't you coming?"
10102{_}942{_}We both turned, and as she did so a low cry of blank dismay involuntarily escaped her.
10102{_}943{_}Next instant I sprang to my feet.
10102{_}944{_}The reason of her cry was apparent, for there, in the full light of the golden sunset streaming through the long open windows, stood a broad-shouldered, fair-bearded man in tennis flannels and a Panama hat--the fugitive I knew as Philip Hornby!
10102{_}945{_}I faced him, speechless.
10102{_}946{_}CHAPTER IV  IN WHICH THE MYSTERY INCREASES   Neither of us spoke.
10102{_}947{_}Equally surprised at the unexpected encounter, we stood facing each other dumbfounded.
10102{_}948{_}Hornby started quickly as soon as his eyes fell upon me, and his face became blanched to the lips, while Muriel Leithcourt, quick to notice the sudden change in him, rose and introduced us in as calm a voice as she could command.
10102{_}949{_}"I don't think you are acquainted," she said to me with a smile.
10102{_}950{_}"This is Mr. Martin Woodroffe--Mr. Gordon Gregg."
10102{_}951{_}I bowed to him in sudden resolve to remain silent in pretense that I doubted whether the man before me was actually my host of the _Lola_.
10102{_}952{_}I intended to act as though I was not sufficiently convinced to openly express my doubt.
10102{_}953{_}Therefore we bowed, exchanging greetings as strangers, while, carefully watching, I saw how greatly the minds of both were relieved.
10102{_}954{_}They shot meaning glances at each other, and then, as though reassured that I was mystified and uncertain, the man who called himself Woodroffe explained to my companion------  "I've been over to Newton Stewart with Fred all day, and only got back a quarter of an hour ago.
10102{_}955{_}Aren't you playing any more to-day?"
10102{_}956{_}"I think not," was her reply.
10102{_}957{_}"We've been out there the whole afternoon, and I'm rather tired.
10102{_}958{_}But they're still on the lawn.
10102{_}959{_}You can surely get a game with someone."
10102{_}960{_}"If you don't play, I shan't.
10102{_}961{_}I returned to keep the promise I made this morning," he laughed, standing before the big open fireplace, holding his tennis racquet behind his back.
10102{_}962{_}I examined his countenance, and was more than ever convinced that he was actually the man who gave me the name of Hornby and the false address in Somerset.
10102{_}963{_}The pair seemed to be on familiar terms, and I wondered whether they were engaged.
10102{_}964{_}In any case, the man seemed quite at home there.
10102{_}965{_}As he chatted with the daughter of the house, he cast a quick, covert glance at me, and then darted a meaning look at her--a look of renewed confidence, as though he felt that he had successfully averted any suspicions I might have held.
10102{_}966{_}We talked of the prospects of the grouse and the salmon, and from his remarks he seemed to be as keen at sport as he had once made out himself to be at yachting.
10102{_}967{_}"My friend Leithcourt is awfully fortunate in getting such a splendid old place as this.
10102{_}968{_}On every hand I hear glowing accounts of the number of birds.
10102{_}969{_}The place has been well preserved in the past, and there's plenty of good cover."
10102{_}970{_}"Yes," I said.
10102{_}971{_}"Gilrae, the owner, is a keen sportsman, and before he became so hard up he spent a lot of money on the estate, which, I believe, has always been considered one of the very best in the southwest.
10102{_}972{_}There's salmon, they say, down in the Glen yonder--but I've never tried for any."
10102{_}973{_}"Certainly there is.
10102{_}974{_}I've seen several.
10102{_}975{_}I hope to try one of these days.
10102{_}976{_}The Glen is deep and shady--an ideal place for fish.
10102{_}977{_}The only disappointment here, as far as I can make out, is the very few head of black-game."
10102{_}978{_}"Yes, but every year they are getting rarer and rarer in this part of Scotland.
10102{_}979{_}A really fine black-cock is quite an event nowadays," I said.
10102{_}980{_}While we were talking, or rather while I was carefully watching the rapid working of his mind, Leithcourt himself entered and joined us.
10102{_}981{_}He had been playing tennis, and had come in to rest and cool.
10102{_}982{_}Host and guest were evidently on the most intimate terms.
10102{_}983{_}Leithcourt addressed him as "Martin," and began to relate a quarrel which his head-gamekeeper had had that day with one of the small farmers on the estate regarding the killing of some rabbits.
10102{_}984{_}And while they were talking Muriel suggested that we should stroll down to the tennis-courts again, an invitation which, much as I regretted leaving the two men, I was bound to accept.
10102{_}985{_}It seemed as though she wished purposely to take me away from that man's presence, fearing that by remaining there longer my suspicions might become confirmed.
10102{_}986{_}She was acting in conjunction with the man whom I had known as Hornby.
10102{_}987{_}There were still a good many people watching the game, for it was pleasant in those old-world gardens in the sunset hour.
10102{_}988{_}The dried-up moat was now transformed into a garden filled with rhododendrons and bright azaleas, while the high ancient beech-hedges, the quaint old sundial with its motto: "Each time ye shadowe turneth ys one daye nearer unto dethe," and the old stone balustrades gray with lichen, all spoke mutely of those glorious days when the fierce horsemen of the Lairds of Rannoch were feared across the Border, and when many a prisoner of the Black Douglas had pined and died in those narrow stone chambers in the grim north tower that still stood high above.
10102{_}989{_}Among the party strolling and lounging there prior to departure were quite a number of people I knew, people who had shooting-boxes in the vicinity and were my uncle's friends.
10102{_}990{_}In Scotland there is always a hearty hospitality among the sporting folk, and the laws of caste are far less rigorous than they are in England.
10102{_}991{_}I was standing chatting with two ladies who were about to take leave of their hostess, when Leithcourt returned, but alone.
10102{_}992{_}Hornby had not accompanied him.
10102{_}993{_}Was it because he feared to again meet me?
10102{_}994{_}In order to ascertain something regarding the man who had so mysteriously fled from Leghorn, I managed by the exercise of a little diplomacy to sit on the lawn with a young married woman named Tennant, wife of a cavalry captain, who was one of the house-party.
10102{_}995{_}After a little time I succeeded in turning the conversation to her fellow guests, and more particularly to the man I knew as Hornby.
10102{_}996{_}"Oh!
10102{_}997{_}Mr. Woodroffe is most amusing," declared the bright little woman.
10102{_}998{_}"He's always playing some practical joke or other.
10102{_}999{_}After dinner he is usually the life and soul of our party."
10102{_}1000{_}"Yes," I said, "I like what little I have seen of him.
10102{_}1001{_}He's a very good fellow, I should say.
10102{_}1002{_}I've heard that he's engaged to Muriel," I hazarded.
10102{_}1003{_}"Is that true?"
10102{_}1004{_}"Of course.
10102{_}1005{_}They've been engaged nearly a year, but he's been abroad until quite lately.
10102{_}1006{_}He is rather close about his own affairs, and never talks about his travels and adventures, although one day Mr. Leithcourt declared that his hairbreadth escapes would make a most exciting book if ever written."
10102{_}1007{_}"Leithcourt and he are evidently most intimate friends."
10102{_}1008{_}"Oh, quite inseparable!"
10102{_}1009{_}she laughed.
10102{_}1010{_}"And the other man who is always with them is that short, stout, red-faced old fellow standing over there with the lady in pale blue, Sir Ughtred Gardner.
10102{_}1011{_}Mr. Woodroffe has nicknamed him 'Sir Putrid.'"
10102{_}1012{_}And we both laughed.
10102{_}1013{_}"Of course, don't say I said so," she whispered.
10102{_}1014{_}"They don't call him that to his face, but it's so easy to make a mistake in his name when he's not within hearing.
10102{_}1015{_}We women don't care for him, so the nickname just fits."
10102{_}1016{_}And she gossiped on, telling me much that I desired to know regarding the new tenant of Rannoch and his friends, and more especially of that man who had first introduced himself to me in the Consulate at Leghorn.
10102{_}1017{_}Half an hour later my uncle's carriage was announced, and I left with the distinct impression that there was some deep mystery surrounding the Leithcourts.
10102{_}1018{_}What it was, however, I could not, for the life of me, make out.
10102{_}1019{_}Perhaps it was Philip Leithcourt's intimate relation with the man who had so cleverly deceived me that incited my curiosity concerning him; perhaps it was that mysterious intuition, that curious presage of evil that sometimes comes to a man as warning of impending peril.
10102{_}1020{_}Whatever the reason, I had become filled with grave apprehensions.
10102{_}1021{_}The mystery grew deeper day by day, and was inexplicable.
10102{_}1022{_}During the week that followed I sought to learn all I could regarding the new people at the castle.
10102{_}1023{_}"They are taken up everywhere," declared my aunt when I questioned her.
10102{_}1024{_}"Of course, we knew very little of them, except that they had a shoot up near Fort William two years ago, and that they have a town house in Green Street.
10102{_}1025{_}They are evidently rather smart folks.
10102{_}1026{_}Don't you think so?"
10102{_}1027{_}"Judging from their house-party, yes," I responded.
10102{_}1028{_}"They are about as gay a crowd as one could find north of Carlisle just at present."
10102{_}1029{_}"Exactly.
10102{_}1030{_}There are some well-known people among them, too," said my aunt.
10102{_}1031{_}"I've asked them over to-morrow afternoon, and they've accepted."
10102{_}1032{_}"Excellent!"
10102{_}1033{_}I exclaimed, for I wanted an opportunity for another chat with the dark-eyed girl who was engaged to the man whose alias was Hornby.
10102{_}1034{_}I particularly desired to ascertain the reason of her fear when I had mentioned the _Lola_, and whether she possessed any knowledge of Hylton Chater.
10102{_}1035{_}The opportunity came to me in due course, for next afternoon the Rannoch party drove over in two large brakes, and with other people from the neighborhood and a band from Dumfries, my aunt's grounds presented a gay and animated scene.
10102{_}1036{_}There was the usual tennis and croquet, while some of the men enjoyed a little putting on the excellent course my uncle, a golf enthusiast, had recently laid down.
10102{_}1037{_}As I expected, Woodroffe did not accompany the party.
10102{_}1038{_}Mrs. Leithcourt, a slightly fussy little woman, apologized for his absence, explaining that he had been recalled to London suddenly a few days before, but was returning to Rannoch again at the end of the week.
10102{_}1039{_}"We couldn't afford to lose him," she declared to my aunt.
10102{_}1040{_}"He is so awfully humorous--his droll sayings and antics keep us in a perfect roar each night at dinner.
10102{_}1041{_}He's such a perfect mimic."
10102{_}1042{_}I turned away and strolled with Muriel, pleading an excuse to show her my uncle's beautiful grounds, not a whit less picturesque than those of the castle, and perhaps rather better kept.
10102{_}1043{_}"I only heard yesterday of your engagement, Miss Leithcourt," I remarked presently when we were alone.
10102{_}1044{_}"Allow me to offer my best congratulations.
10102{_}1045{_}When you introduced me to Mr. Woodroffe the other day I had no idea that he was to be your husband."
10102{_}1046{_}She glanced at me quickly, and I saw in her dark eyes a look of suspicion.
10102{_}1047{_}Then she flushed slightly, and laughing uneasily said, in a blank, hard voice--  "It's very good of you, Mr. Gregg, to wish me all sorts of such pleasant things."
10102{_}1048{_}"And when is the happy event to take place?"
10102{_}1049{_}"The date is not exactly fixed--early next year, I believe," and I thought she sighed.
10102{_}1050{_}"And you will probably spend a good deal of time yachting?"
10102{_}1051{_}I suggested, my eyes fixed upon her in order to watch the result of my pointed remark.
10102{_}1052{_}But she controlled herself perfectly.
10102{_}1053{_}"I love the sea," she responded briefly, and her eyes were set straight before her.
10102{_}1054{_}"Mr. Woodroffe has gone up to town, your mother says."
10102{_}1055{_}"Yes.
10102{_}1056{_}He received a wire, and had to leave immediately.
10102{_}1057{_}It was an awful bore, for we had arranged to go for a picnic to Dundrennan Abbey yesterday."
10102{_}1058{_}"But he'll be back here again, won't he?"
10102{_}1059{_}"I really don't know.
10102{_}1060{_}It seems quite uncertain.
10102{_}1061{_}I had a letter this morning which said he might have to go over to Hamburg on business, instead of coming up to us again."
10102{_}1062{_}There was disappointment in her voice, and yet at the same time I could not fail to recognize how the man to whom she was engaged had fled from Scotland because of my presence.
10102{_}1063{_}How I longed to ask her point-blank what she really knew of the yachtsman who was shrouded in so much mystery.
10102{_}1064{_}Yet by betraying any undue anxiety I should certainly negative all my efforts to solve the puzzling enigma, therefore I was compelled to remain content with asking ingeniously disguised questions and drawing my own conclusions from her answers.
10102{_}1065{_}As we passed along those graveled walks it somehow became vividly impressed upon me that her marriage was being forced upon her by her parents.
10102{_}1066{_}Her manner was that of one who was concealing some strange and terrible secret which she feared might be revealed.
10102{_}1067{_}There was a distant look of unutterable terror in those dark eyes as though she existed in some constant and ever-present dread.
10102{_}1068{_}Of course she told me nothing of her own feelings or affections, yet I recognized in both her words and her bearing a curious apathy--a want of the real enthusiasm of affection.
10102{_}1069{_}Woodroffe, much her senior, was her father's friend, and it therefore seemed to me more than likely that Leithcourt was pressing a matrimonial alliance upon his daughter for some ulterior motive.
10102{_}1070{_}In the mad hurry for place, power, and wealth, men relentlessly sell their daughters in the matrimonial market, and ambitious mothers scheme and intrigue for their own aggrandizement at sacrifice of their daughter's happiness more often than the public ever dream.
10102{_}1071{_}Tragedy is, alas!
10102{_}1072{_}written upon the face of many a bride whose portrait appears in the fashion-papers and whose toilette is so faithfully chronicled in the paragraph beneath.
10102{_}1073{_}Indeed, the girl in Society who is allowed her own free choice in the matter of a husband is, alas!
10102{_}1074{_}nowadays the exception, for parents who want to "get on" up the social scale have found that pretty daughters are a marketable commodity, and many a man has been placed "on his legs," both financially and socially, by his son-in-law.
10102{_}1075{_}Hence the marriage of convenience is fast becoming common, while in the same ratio the divorce petitions are unfortunately on the increase.
10102{_}1076{_}I read tragedy in the dark luminous eyes of Muriel Leithcourt.
10102{_}1077{_}I knew that her young heart was over-burdened by some secret sorrow or guilty knowledge that she would reveal to me if she dared.
10102{_}1078{_}Her own words told me that she was perplexed; that she longed to confide and seek advice of someone, yet by reason of some hidden and untoward circumstance her lips were sealed.
10102{_}1079{_}I tried to question her further regarding Woodroffe, of what profession he followed and of his past.
10102{_}1080{_}But she evidently suspected me, for I had unfortunately mentioned the _Lola_.
10102{_}1081{_}She wanted to speak to me in confidence, and yet she would reveal to me nothing--absolutely nothing.
10102{_}1082{_}Martin Woodroffe did not rejoin the house-party at Rannoch.
10102{_}1083{_}Although I remained the guest of my uncle much longer than I intended, indeed right through the shooting season, in order to watch the Leithcourts, yet as far as we could judge they were extremely well-bred people and very hospitable.
10102{_}1084{_}We exchanged a good many visits and dinners, and while my uncle several times invited Leithcourt and his friends to his shoot with _al fresco_ luncheon, which the ladies joined, the tenant of Rannoch always invited us back in return.
10102{_}1085{_}Thus I gained many opportunities of talking with Muriel, and of watching her closely.
10102{_}1086{_}I had the reputation of being a confirmed bachelor, and on account of that it seemed that she was in no way averse to my companionship.
10102{_}1087{_}She could handle a rook-rifle as well as any woman, and was really a very fair shot.
10102{_}1088{_}Therefore we often found ourselves alone tramping across the wide open moorland, or along those delightful glens of the Nithsdale, glorious in the autumn tints of their luxurious foliage.
10102{_}1089{_}Her father, on the other hand, seemed to view me with considerable suspicion, and I could easily discern that I was only asked to Rannoch because it was impossible to invite my uncle without including myself.
10102{_}1090{_}Leithcourt, who perhaps thought I was courting his daughter, was ever endeavoring to avoid me, and would never allow me to walk with him alone.
10102{_}1091{_}Why?
10102{_}1092{_}I wondered.
10102{_}1093{_}Did he fear me?
10102{_}1094{_}Had Woodroffe told him of our strange encounter in Leghorn?
10102{_}1095{_}His pronounced antipathy towards me caused me to watch him surreptitiously, and more closely than perhaps I should otherwise have done.
10102{_}1096{_}He was a man of gloomy mood, and often he would leave his guests and take walks alone, musing and brooding.
10102{_}1097{_}On several occasions I followed him in secret, and found to my surprise that although he made long detours in various directions, yet he always arrived at the same spot at the same hour--five o'clock.
10102{_}1098{_}The place where he halted was on the edge of a dark wood on the brow of a hill about three miles from Rannoch--a good place to get woodpigeon, as they came to roost.
10102{_}1099{_}It was fully two miles across the hills from the high road to Moniaive, and from the break the gray wall where he was in the habit of sitting to rest and smoke, there stretched the beautiful panorama of Loch Urr and the heatherclad hills beyond.
10102{_}1100{_}Leithcourt never went direct to the place, but always so timed his walks that he arrived just at five, and remained there smoking cigarettes until half-past, as though awaiting the arrival of some person he expected.
10102{_}1101{_}Once or twice his guests suggested shooting pigeons at sundown, but he always had some excuse for opposing the proposal, and thus the party, unsuspecting the reason, were kept away from that particular lonely spot.
10102{_}1102{_}In my youth I had sat many a quiet hour there in the darkening gloom and shot many a pigeon, therefore I knew the wood well, and was able to watch the tenant of Rannoch from points where he least suspected the presence of another.
10102{_}1103{_}Once, when I was alone with Muriel, I mentioned her father's capacity for walking alone, whereupon she said--  "Oh, yes, he was always fond of walking.
10102{_}1104{_}He used to take me with him when we first came here, but he always went so far that I refused to go any more."
10102{_}1105{_}She never once mentioned Woodroffe.
10102{_}1106{_}I allowed her plenty of opportunity for doing so, chaffing her about her forthcoming marriage in order that she might again refer to him.
10102{_}1107{_}But never did his name pass her lips.
10102{_}1108{_}I understood that he had gone abroad--that was all.
10102{_}1109{_}Often when alone I reflected upon my curious adventure on that night when I met Olinto, and of my narrow escape from the hands of my unknown enemies.
10102{_}1110{_}I wondered if that ingenious and dastardly attempt upon my life had really any connection with that strange incident at Leghorn.
10102{_}1111{_}As day succeeded day, my mind became filled by increasing suspicion.
10102{_}1112{_}Mystery surrounded me on every hand.
10102{_}1113{_}Indeed, by one curious fact alone it was increased a hundredfold.
10102{_}1114{_}Late one afternoon, when I had been out shooting all day with the Rannoch party, I drove back to the castle in the Perth-cart with three other men, and found the ladies assembled in the great hall with tea ready.
10102{_}1115{_}A welcome log-fire was blazing in the huge old grate, for in October it is chilly and damp in Scotland and a fire is pleasant at evening.
10102{_}1116{_}Muriel was seated upon the high padded fender--like those one has at clubs--which always formed a cosy spot for the ladies, especially after dinner.
10102{_}1117{_}When I entered, she rose quickly and handed me my cup, exclaiming as she looked at me--  "Oh, Mr. Gregg!
10102{_}1118{_}what a state you are in!"
10102{_}1119{_}"Yes, I was after snipe, and slipped into a bog," I laughed.
10102{_}1120{_}"But it was early this morning, and the mud has dried."
10102{_}1121{_}"Come with me, and I'll get you a brush," she urged.
10102{_}1122{_}And I followed her through the long corridors and upstairs to a small sitting-room which was her own little sanctum, where she worked and read--a cosy little place with two queer old windows in the colossal wall, and a floor of polished oak, and great black beams above.
10102{_}1123{_}When the owner had occupied the house that room had been disused, but it had, I found, been now completely transformed, and was a most tasteful little nest of luxury with its bright chintzes, its Turkey rugs and its cheerful fire on the old stone hearth.
10102{_}1124{_}She laughed when I expressed admiration of her little den, and said--  "I believe it was the armory in the old days.
10102{_}1125{_}But it makes quite a comfy little boudoir.
10102{_}1126{_}I can lock myself in and be quite quiet when the party are too noisy," she added merrily.
10102{_}1127{_}But as my eyes wandered around they suddenly fell upon an object which caused me to start with profound wonder--a cabinet photograph in a frame of crimson leather.
10102{_}1128{_}The picture was that of a young girl--a duplicate of the portrait I had found torn across and flung aside on board the _Lola_!
10102{_}1129{_}The merry eyes laughed out at me as I stood staring at it in sheer bewilderment.
10102{_}1130{_}"What a pretty girl!"
10102{_}1131{_}I exclaimed quickly, concealing my surprise.
10102{_}1132{_}"Who is she?"
10102{_}1133{_}My companion was silent a moment, her dark eyes meeting mine with a strange look of inquiry.
10102{_}1134{_}"Yes," she laughed, "everyone admires her.
10102{_}1135{_}She was a schoolfellow of mine--Elma Heath."
10102{_}1136{_}"Heath!"
10102{_}1137{_}I echoed.
10102{_}1138{_}"Where was she at school with you?"
10102{_}1139{_}"At Chichester."
10102{_}1140{_}"Long ago?"
10102{_}1141{_}"A little over two years."
10102{_}1142{_}"She's very beautiful!"
10102{_}1143{_}I declared, taking up the photograph and discovering that it bore the name of the same well-known photographer in New Bond Street as that I had found on the carpet of the _Lola_ in the Mediterranean.
10102{_}1144{_}"Yes.
10102{_}1145{_}She's really prettier than her photograph.
10102{_}1146{_}It hardly does her justice."
10102{_}1147{_}"And where is she now?"
10102{_}1148{_}"Why are you so very inquisitive, Mr.
10102{_}1149{_}Gregg?"
10102{_}1150{_}laughed the handsome girl.
10102{_}1151{_}"Have you actually fallen in love with her from her picture?"
10102{_}1152{_}"I'm hardly given to that kind of thing, Miss Leithcourt," I answered with mock severity.
10102{_}1153{_}"I don't think even my worst enemy could call me a flirt, could she?"
10102{_}1154{_}"No.
10102{_}1155{_}I will give you your due," she declared.
10102{_}1156{_}"You never do flirt.
10102{_}1157{_}That is why I like you."
10102{_}1158{_}"Thanks for your candor, Miss Leithcourt," I said.
10102{_}1159{_}"Only," she added, "you seem smitten with Elma's charms."
10102{_}1160{_}"I think she's extremely pretty," I remarked, with the photograph still in my hand.
10102{_}1161{_}"Do you ever see her now?"
10102{_}1162{_}"Never," she replied.
10102{_}1163{_}"Since the day I left school we have never met.
10102{_}1164{_}She was several years younger than myself, and I heard that a week after I left Chichester her people came and took her away.
10102{_}1165{_}Where she is now I have no idea.
10102{_}1166{_}Her people lived somewhere in Durham.
10102{_}1167{_}Her father was a doctor."
10102{_}1168{_}Her reply disappointed me.
10102{_}1169{_}Yet I had, at least, retained knowledge of the name of the original of the picture, and from the photographer I might perhaps discover her address, for to me it seemed that she was somehow intimately connected with those mysterious yachtsmen.
10102{_}1170{_}What Muriel told me concerning her, I did not doubt for a single instant.
10102{_}1171{_}Yet it was certainly more than a coincidence that a copy of the picture which had created such a deep impression upon me should be preserved in her own little boudoir as a souvenir of a devoted school-friend.
10102{_}1172{_}"Then you have heard absolutely nothing as to her present position or whereabouts--whether she is married, for instance?"
10102{_}1173{_}"Ah!"
10102{_}1174{_}she cried mischievously.
10102{_}1175{_}"You betray yourself by your own words.
10102{_}1176{_}You have fallen in love with her, I really believe, Mr. Gregg.
10102{_}1177{_}If she knew, she'd be most gratified--or at least, she ought to be."
10102{_}1178{_}At which I smiled, preferring that she should adopt that theory in preference to any other.
10102{_}1179{_}She spoke frankly, as a pure honest girl would speak.
10102{_}1180{_}She was not jealous, but she nevertheless resented--as women do resent such things--that I should fall in love with a friend's photograph.
10102{_}1181{_}There was a mystery surrounding that torn picture; of that I was absolutely certain.
10102{_}1182{_}The remembrance of that memorable evening when I had dined on board the _Lola_ arose vividly before me.
10102{_}1183{_}Why had the girl's portrait been so ruthlessly destroyed and the frame turned with its face to the wall?
10102{_}1184{_}There was some reason--some distinct and serious motive in it.
10102{_}1185{_}Had Muriel told me the truth, I wondered, or was she merely seeking to shield the suspected man who was her lover?
10102{_}1186{_}Hour by hour the mystery surrounding the Leithcourts became more inscrutable, more intensely absorbing.
10102{_}1187{_}I had searched a copy of the London Directory at the Station Hotel at Carlisle, and found that no house in Green Street was registered as occupied by the tenant of Rannoch; and, further, when I came to examine the list of guests at the castle, I found that they were really persons unknown in society.
10102{_}1188{_}They were merely of that class of witty, well-dressed parasites who always cling on to the wealthy and make believe that they are smart and of the _grande monde_.
10102{_}1189{_}Rannoch was an expensive place to keep up, with all that big retinue of servants and gamekeepers, and with those nightly dinners cooked by a French _chef_; yet Leithcourt seemed to possess a long pocket and smiled upon those parasites, officers of doubtful commission and younger sprigs of the pseudo-aristocracy who surrounded him, while his wife, keen-eyed and of superb bearing, was punctilious concerning all points of etiquette, and at the same time indefatigable that her mixed set of guests should enjoy a really good time.
10102{_}1190{_}But I was not the only person who could not make them out.
10102{_}1191{_}My uncle was the first to open my eyes regarding the true character of certain of the men staying at Rannoch.
10102{_}1192{_}"I think, Gordon, that one or two of those fellows with Leithcourt are rank outsiders," he said confidentially to me one night after we had had a hard day's shooting, and were playing a hundred up at billiards before retiring.
10102{_}1193{_}"One man, who arrived yesterday, I know too well.
10102{_}1194{_}He was struck off the list at Boodle's three years ago for card-sharping--that thin-faced, fair-mustached man named Cadby.
10102{_}1195{_}I suppose Leithcourt doesn't know it, or he wouldn't have him up here among respectable folk."
10102{_}1196{_}And my uncle, chewing the end of his cigar, sniffed angrily, seeming half inclined to give his friend a gentle hint that the name Cadby was placed beyond the pale of good society.
10102{_}1197{_}"Better not say anything about it," I urged.
10102{_}1198{_}"It's Leithcourt's own affair, uncle--not ours."
10102{_}1199{_}"Yes, but if a man sets up a position in the country he mustn't be allowed to ask us to meet such fellows.
10102{_}1200{_}It's coming it a little too thick, Gordon.
10102{_}1201{_}We men can stand the women of the party, but the men--well, I tell you candidly, I shan't accept his invites to shoot again."
10102{_}1202{_}"No, no, uncle," I protested.
10102{_}1203{_}"Probably it's owing to ignorance.
10102{_}1204{_}You'll be able, a little later on, to give him valuable tips.
10102{_}1205{_}He's a good fellow, and only wants experience in Scotland to get along all right."
10102{_}1206{_}"Yes.
10102{_}1207{_}But I don't like it, my boy, I don't like it!
10102{_}1208{_}It isn't playing a fair game," declared the rigid old gentleman, coloring resentfully.
10102{_}1209{_}"I'm not going to return the invitation and ask that sharper, Cadby, to my house--and I tell you that plainly."
10102{_}1210{_}Next day I shot with the Carmichaels of Crossburn, and about four o'clock, after a good day, took leave of the party in the Black Glen, and started off alone to walk home, a distance of about six miles.
10102{_}1211{_}It was already growing dusk, and would be quite dark, I knew, before I reached my uncle's house.
10102{_}1212{_}My most direct way was to follow the river for about two miles and then strike straight across the large dense wood, and afterwards over a wide moor full of treacherous bogs and pitfalls for the unwary.
10102{_}1213{_}My gun over my shoulder, I had walked on for about three-quarters of an hour, and had nearly traversed the wood, at that hour so dark that I had considerable difficulty in finding my way, when--of a sudden--I fancied I distinguished voices.
10102{_}1214{_}I halted.
10102{_}1215{_}Yes.
10102{_}1216{_}Men were talking in low tones of confidence, and in that calm stillness of evening they appeared nearer to me than they actually were.
10102{_}1217{_}I listened, trying to distinguish the words uttered, but could make out nothing.
10102{_}1218{_}They were moving slowly together, in close vicinity to myself, for their feet stirred the dry leaves, and I could hear the boughs cracking as they forced their way through them.
10102{_}1219{_}Of a sudden, while standing there not daring to breathe lest I should betray my presence, a strange sound fell upon my eager ears.
10102{_}1220{_}Next moment I realized that I was at that place where Leithcourt so persistently kept his disappointed tryst, having approached it from within the wood.
10102{_}1221{_}The sound alarmed me, and yet it was neither an explosion of fire-arms nor a startling cry for help.
10102{_}1222{_}One word reached me in the darkness--one single word of bitter and withering reproach.
10102{_}1223{_}Heedless of the risk I ran and the peril to which I exposed myself, I dashed forward with a resolve to penetrate the mystery, until I came to the gap in the rough stone wall where Leithcourt's habit was to halt each day at sundown.
10102{_}1224{_}There, in the falling darkness, the sight that met my eyes at the spot held me rigid, appalled, stupefied.
10102{_}1225{_}In that instant I realized the truth--a truth that was surely the strangest ever revealed to any man.
10102{_}1226{_}CHAPTER V  CONTAINS CERTAIN CONFIDENCES   As I dashed forward to the gap in the boundary wall of the wood, I nearly stumbled over a form lying across the narrow path.
10102{_}1227{_}So dark was it beneath the trees that at first I could not plainly make out what it was until I bent and my hands touched the garments of a woman.
10102{_}1228{_}Her hat had fallen off, for I felt it beneath my feet, while the cloak was a thick woolen one.
10102{_}1229{_}Was she dead, I wondered?
10102{_}1230{_}That cry--that single word of reproach--sounded in my ears, and it seemed plain that she had been struck down ruthlessly after an exchange of angry words.
10102{_}1231{_}I felt in my pocket for my vestas, but unfortunately my box was empty.
10102{_}1232{_}Yet just at that moment my strained ears caught a sound--the sound of someone moving stealthily among the fallen leaves.
10102{_}1233{_}Seizing my gun, I demanded who was there.
10102{_}1234{_}There was, however, no response.
10102{_}1235{_}The instant I spoke the movement ceased.
10102{_}1236{_}As far as I could judge, the person in concealment was within the wood about ten yards from me, separated by an impenetrable thicket.
10102{_}1237{_}As, however, I stood out against the sky, my silhouette was, I knew, a well-defined mark for anyone with fire-arms.
10102{_}1238{_}It seemed evident that a tragedy had occurred, and that the victim at my feet was a woman.
10102{_}1239{_}But whom?
10102{_}1240{_}Of a sudden, while I stood hesitating, blaming myself for being without matches, I heard the movement repeated.
10102{_}1241{_}Someone was quickly receding--escaping from the spot.
10102{_}1242{_}I listened again.
10102{_}1243{_}The sound was not of the rustling of leaves or the crackling of dried sticks, but the low thuds of a man's feet racing over softer ground.
10102{_}1244{_}He had scaled the rough stone dyke and was out in the turnip-field adjacent.
10102{_}1245{_}I sprang through the gap, straining my eyes into the gloom, and as I did so could just distinguish a dark figure receding quickly beneath the wall of the wood.
10102{_}1246{_}In an instant I dashed after it.
10102{_}1247{_}But the agility of whoever the fugitive was, man or woman, was marvelous.
10102{_}1248{_}I considered myself a fairly good runner, but racing across those rough turnips and heavy, newly-plowed land in the darkness and carrying my gun soon caused me to pant and blow.
10102{_}1249{_}Yet the figure I was pursuing was so fleet of foot and so nimble in climbing the high rough walls that from the very first I was outrun.
10102{_}1250{_}Down the steep hill to the Scarwater I followed the fugitive, crossing the old footbridge near Penpont, and then up a wild winding glen towards the Cairnsmore of Deugh.
10102{_}1251{_}For a couple of miles or more I was close behind, until, at a turn in the dark wooded glen where it branched in two directions, I lost all trace of the person who flew from me.
10102{_}1252{_}Whoever it was they had very cleverly gone into hiding in the undergrowth of one or other of the two glens--which I could not decide.
10102{_}1253{_}I stood out of breath, the perspiration pouring from me, undecided how to act.
10102{_}1254{_}Was it Leithcourt himself whom I had surprised?
10102{_}1255{_}That idea somehow became impressed upon me and I suddenly resolved to go boldly across to Rannoch and ascertain for myself.
10102{_}1256{_}Therefore, with the excuse that I was belated on my walk home, I turned back down the glen, and half an hour afterward entered the great well-lighted hall of the castle where the guests, ready dressed, were assembling prior to dinner.
10102{_}1257{_}I was welcomed warmly, as I was always by the men of the party, who seeing my muddy plight at once offered me a glass of the sportsman's drink in Scotland, and while I was adding soda to it Leithcourt himself joined his guests, ready dressed in his dinner jacket, having just descended from his room.
10102{_}1258{_}"Hulloa, Gregg!"
10102{_}1259{_}he exclaimed heartily, holding out his hand.
10102{_}1260{_}"Had a long day of it, evidently.
10102{_}1261{_}Good sport with Carmichael--eh?"
10102{_}1262{_}"Very fair," I said.
10102{_}1263{_}"I remained longer with him than I ought to have done, and have got belated on my way home, so looked in for a refresher."
10102{_}1264{_}"Quite right," he laughed merrily.
10102{_}1265{_}"You're always welcome, you know.
10102{_}1266{_}I'd have been annoyed if I knew you had passed without coming in."
10102{_}1267{_}And Muriel, a pretty figure in a low-cut gown of turquoise chiffon, standing behind her father, smiled secretly at me.
10102{_}1268{_}I smiled at her in return, but it was a strange smile, I fear, for with the knowledge of that additional mystery within me--the mystery of the woman lying unconscious or perhaps dead, up in the wood--held me stupefied.
10102{_}1269{_}I had suspected Leithcourt because of his constant trysts at that spot, but I had at least proved that my suspicions were entirely without foundation.
10102{_}1270{_}He could not have got home and dressed in the time, for I had taken the nearest route to the castle while the fugitive would be compelled to make a wide detour.
10102{_}1271{_}I only remained a few minutes, then went forth into the darkness again, utterly undecided how to act.
10102{_}1272{_}My first impulse was to return to the woman's aid, for she might not be dead after all.
10102{_}1273{_}And yet when I recollected that hoarse cry that rang out in the darkness, I knew too well that she had been struck fatally.
10102{_}1274{_}It was this latter conviction that prevented me from turning back to the wood.
10102{_}1275{_}You will perhaps blame me, but the fact is I feared that if I went there suspicion might fall upon me, now that the real culprit had so ingeniously escaped.
10102{_}1276{_}If the victim were dead, what aid could I render?
10102{_}1277{_}A knife had, I believed, been used, for my foot caught against it when I had started off after the fugitive.
10102{_}1278{_}The only doubt in my own mind was whether the unfortunate woman was actually dead, for if she were not then my disinclination to return to the scene of the tragedy was culpable.
10102{_}1279{_}Whether or not I acted rightly in remaining away from the place, I leave it to you to judge in the light of the amazing truth which afterwards transpired.
10102{_}1280{_}I decided to walk straight back to my uncle's, and dinner was over before I had had my tub and dressed.
10102{_}1281{_}I therefore ate my meal alone, Davis, the grave old butler, serving me with that stateliness which always amused me.
10102{_}1282{_}I usually chatted with him when others were not present, but that night I remained silent, my mind full of that strange and startling affair of which I alone held secret knowledge.
10102{_}1283{_}Next day the body would surely be found; then the whole countryside would be filled with horror and surprise.
10102{_}1284{_}Was it possible that Leithcourt, that calm, well-groomed, distinguished-looking man, held any knowledge of the ghastly truth?
10102{_}1285{_}No.
10102{_}1286{_}His manner as he stood in the hall chatting gayly with me was surely not that of a man with a guilty secret.
10102{_}1287{_}I became firmly convinced that although the tragedy affected him very closely, and that it had occurred at the spot which he had each day visited for some mysterious purpose, yet up to the present he was in ignorance of what had transpired.
10102{_}1288{_}But who was the woman?
10102{_}1289{_}Was she young or old?
10102{_}1290{_}A thousand times I regretted bitterly that I had no matches with me so that I might examine her features.
10102{_}1291{_}One sudden thought that struck me as I sat there at table caused me to lay down my fork and pause in breathless bewilderment.
10102{_}1292{_}Was the victim that sweet-faced young girl whose photograph had been so ruthlessly cast from its frame and destroyed?
10102{_}1293{_}The theory was a weird one, but was it the truth?
10102{_}1294{_}I longed for the coming of the dawn when the Rannoch keepers would most certainly discover her.
10102{_}1295{_}Then at least I should know the truth, for I might go and see the body out of curiosity without arousing any suspicion.
10102{_}1296{_}I tried to play my usual game of billiards with my uncle, but my hand was so unsteady that the old gentleman began to chaff me.
10102{_}1297{_}"It's the gun, I suppose," I remarked.
10102{_}1298{_}"I've been carrying it all day, and am tired out.
10102{_}1299{_}I walked all the way home from Crossburn."
10102{_}1300{_}"The Carmichaels are very thick with the Leithcourts, I hear," my uncle remarked.
10102{_}1301{_}"Strange they didn't ask Leithcourt to their shoot."
10102{_}1302{_}"They did, but he'd got another engagement--over at Kenmure Castle, I think."
10102{_}1303{_}I retired to my room that night full of fevered apprehension.
10102{_}1304{_}Had I acted rightly in not returning to that lonely spot on the brow of the hill?
10102{_}1305{_}Had I done as a man should do in keeping the tragic secret to myself?
10102{_}1306{_}I opened my window and gazed away across the dark Nithsdale, where, in the distant gloom, the black line of wood loomed up against the stormy sky.
10102{_}1307{_}The stars were no longer shining and the rain clouds had gathered.
10102{_}1308{_}I stood with my face turned to the dark indistinct spot that held the secret, lost in wonderment.
10102{_}1309{_}At last I closed the window and turned in, but no sleep came to my eyes, so full was my mind of the startling events of those past few months and of that gruesome discovery I had made.
10102{_}1310{_}Had the fugitive actually recognized me?
10102{_}1311{_}Probably my voice when I had called out had betrayed me.
10102{_}1312{_}Hour after hour I lay puzzling, trying to arrive at some solution of that intricate problem which now presented itself.
10102{_}1313{_}Muriel could tell me what I wished to know.
10102{_}1314{_}Of that I was certain.
10102{_}1315{_}Yet she dared not speak.
10102{_}1316{_}Some inexpressible terror held her dumb--she was affianced to the man Martin Woodroffe.
10102{_}1317{_}Again I rose, lit the gas, and tried to read a novel.
10102{_}1318{_}But I could not concentrate my thoughts, which were ever wandering to that strange mystery of the wood.
10102{_}1319{_}At six I shaved, descended, and went out with the dogs for a short walk; but on returning I heard of nothing unusual, and was compelled to remain inactive until near mid-day.
10102{_}1320{_}I was crossing the stable-yard where I had gone to order the carriage for my aunt, when an English groom, suddenly emerging from the harness-room, touched his cap, saying--  "Have you 'eard, sir, of the awful affair up yonder?"
10102{_}1321{_}"Of what?"
10102{_}1322{_}I asked quickly.
10102{_}1323{_}"Well, sir, there seems to have been a murder last night up in Rannoch Wood," said the man quickly.
10102{_}1324{_}"Holden, the gardener, has just come back from that village and says that Mr. Leithcourt's under-gamekeeper as he was going home at five this morning came upon a dead body."
10102{_}1325{_}"A dead body!"
10102{_}1326{_}I exclaimed, feigning great surprise.
10102{_}1327{_}"Yes, sir--a youngish man.
10102{_}1328{_}He'd been stabbed to the heart."
10102{_}1329{_}"A man!"
10102{_}1330{_}"Yes, sir--so Holden says."
10102{_}1331{_}"Call Holden.
10102{_}1332{_}I'd like to know all he's heard," I said.
10102{_}1333{_}And presently, when the gardener emerged from the grape-house, I sought of him all the particulars he had gathered.
10102{_}1334{_}"I don't know very much, sir," was the man's reply.
10102{_}1335{_}"I went into the inn for a glass of beer at eleven, as I always do, and heard them talking about it.
10102{_}1336{_}A young man was murdered last night up in Rannoch Wood.
10102{_}1337{_}The gamekeeper thought at first there'd been a fight among poachers, but from the dead man's clothes they say he isn't a poacher at all, but a stranger in this district."
10102{_}1338{_}"The body was that of a man, then?"
10102{_}1339{_}I asked, trying to conceal my utter bewilderment.
10102{_}1340{_}"Yes--about thirty, they say.
10102{_}1341{_}The police have taken him to the mortuary at Dumfries, and the detectives are up there now looking at the spot, they say."
10102{_}1342{_}A man!
10102{_}1343{_}And yet the body I found was that of a woman--that I could swear.
10102{_}1344{_}After lunch I took the dog-cart and drove alone into Dumfries.
10102{_}1345{_}When I inquired of the police-constable on duty at the town mortuary to be allowed to view the body of the murdered man, he regarded me, I thought, with considerable suspicion.
10102{_}1346{_}My request was an unusual one.
10102{_}1347{_}Nevertheless, he took me up a narrow alley, unlocked a door, and I found myself in the cold, gloomy chamber of death.
10102{_}1348{_}From a small dingy window above the light fell upon an object lying upon a large slab of gray stone and covered with a soiled sheet.
10102{_}1349{_}The sight was ghastly and gruesome; the body lay there awaiting the official inquiry into the cause of death.
10102{_}1350{_}The silence of the tomb was unbroken, save for the heavy tread of the policeman, who having removed his helmet in the presence of the dead, lifted the end of the sheet, revealing to me a white, hard-set face, with closed eyes and dropped jaw.
10102{_}1351{_}I started back as my eyes fell upon the dead countenance.
10102{_}1352{_}I was entirely unprepared for such a revelation.
10102{_}1353{_}The truth staggered me.
10102{_}1354{_}The victim was the man who had acted as my friend--the Italian waiter, Olinto.
10102{_}1355{_}I advanced and peered into the thin inanimate features, scarce able to realize the actual fact.
10102{_}1356{_}But my eyes had not deceived me.
10102{_}1357{_}Though death distorts the facial expression of every man, I had no difficulty in identifying him.
10102{_}1358{_}"You recognize him, sir?"
10102{_}1359{_}remarked the officer.
10102{_}1360{_}"Who is he?
10102{_}1361{_}Our people are very anxious to know, for up to the present moment they haven't succeeded in establishing his identity."
10102{_}1362{_}I bit my lips.
10102{_}1363{_}I had been an arrant fool to betray myself before that man.
10102{_}1364{_}Yet having done so, I saw that any attempt to conceal my knowledge must of necessity reflect upon me.
10102{_}1365{_}"I will see your inspector," I answered with as much calmness as I could muster.
10102{_}1366{_}"Where has the poor fellow been wounded?"
10102{_}1367{_}"Through the heart," responded the constable, as turning the sheet further down he showed me the small knife wound which had penetrated the victim's jacket and vest full in the chest.
10102{_}1368{_}"This is the weapon," he added, taking from a shelf close by a long, thin poignard with an ivory handle, which he handed to me.
10102{_}1369{_}In an instant I recognized what it was, and how deadly.
10102{_}1370{_}It was an old Florentine _misericordia_, a long thin, triangular blade, a quarter of an inch wide at its greatest width, tapering to a needle-point, with a hilt of yellow ivory, the most deadly and fatal of all the daggers and poignards of the Middle Ages.
10102{_}1371{_}The blade being sharp on three angles produced a wound that caused internal hemorrhage and which never healed--hence the name given to it by the Florentines.
10102{_}1372{_}It was still blood-stained, but as I took the deadly thing in my hand I saw that its blade was beautifully damascened, a most elegant specimen of a medieval arm.
10102{_}1373{_}Yet surely none but an Italian would use such a weapon, or would aim so truly as to penetrate the heart.
10102{_}1374{_}And yet the person struck down was a woman, and not a man!
10102{_}1375{_}A wound from a _misericordia_ always proves fatal, because the shape of the blade cuts the flesh into little flaps which, on withdrawing the knife, close up and prevent the blood from issuing forth.
10102{_}1376{_}At the same time, however, no power can make them heal again.
10102{_}1377{_}A blow from such a weapon is as surely fatal as the poisoned poignard of the Borgia or the Medici.
10102{_}1378{_}I handed the stiletto back to the man without comment.
10102{_}1379{_}My resolve was to say as little as possible, for I had no desire to figure publicly at the inquiry, and consequently negative all my own efforts to solve the mystery of the Leithcourts and of Martin Woodroffe.
10102{_}1380{_}I returned to where the figure was lying so ghastly and motionless, and looked again for the last time upon the dead face of the man who had served me so well, and yet who had enticed me so nearly to my death.
10102{_}1381{_}In the latter incident there was a deep mystery.
10102{_}1382{_}He had relented at the last moment, just in time to save me from my secret enemies.
10102{_}1383{_}Could it be that my enemies were his?
10102{_}1384{_}Had he fallen a victim by the same hand that had attempted so ingeniously to kill me?
10102{_}1385{_}Why had Leithcourt gone so regularly up to Rannoch Wood?
10102{_}1386{_}Was it in order to meet the man who was to be entrapped and killed?
10102{_}1387{_}What was Olinto Santini doing so far from London, if he had not come expressly to meet someone in secret?
10102{_}1388{_}As I glanced down at the cold, inanimate countenance upon which mystery was written, I became seized by regret.
10102{_}1389{_}He had been a faithful and honest servant, and even though he had enticed me to that fatal house in Lambeth, yet I recollected his words, how he had done so under compulsion.
10102{_}1390{_}I remembered, too, how he had implored me not to prejudge him before I became aware of the full facts.
10102{_}1391{_}With my own hand I re-covered the face with the sheet, and inwardly resolved to avenge the dastardly crime.
10102{_}1392{_}I regretted that I was compelled to reveal the dead man's name to the police, yet I saw that to make some statement was now inevitable, and therefore I accompanied the constable to the inspector's office some distance across the town.
10102{_}1393{_}Having been introduced to the big, fair-haired man in a rough tweed suit, who was apparently directing the inquiries into the affair, he took me eagerly into a small back room and began to question me.
10102{_}1394{_}I was, however, wary not to commit myself to anything further than the identification of the body.
10102{_}1395{_}"The fact is," I said confidentially, "you must omit me from the witnesses at the inquest."
10102{_}1396{_}"Why?"
10102{_}1397{_}asked the detective suspiciously.
10102{_}1398{_}"Because if it were known that I have identified him, all chance of getting at the truth will at once vanish," I answered.
10102{_}1399{_}"I have come here to tell you in strictest confidence who the poor fellow really is."
10102{_}1400{_}"Then you know something of the affair?"
10102{_}1401{_}he said, with a strong Highland accent.
10102{_}1402{_}"I know nothing," I declared.
10102{_}1403{_}"Nothing except his name."
10102{_}1404{_}"H'm.
10102{_}1405{_}And you say he's a foreigner--an Italian--eh?"
10102{_}1406{_}"He was in my service in Leghorn for several years, and on leaving me he came to London and obtained an engagement as waiter in a restaurant.
10102{_}1407{_}His father lived in Leghorn; he was doorkeeper at the Prefecture."
10102{_}1408{_}"But why was he here, in Scotland?"
10102{_}1409{_}"How can I tell?"
10102{_}1410{_}"You know something of the affair.
10102{_}1411{_}I mean that you suspect somebody, or you would have no objection to giving evidence at the inquiry."
10102{_}1412{_}"I have no suspicions.
10102{_}1413{_}To me the affair is just as much of an enigma as to you," I hastened at once to explain.
10102{_}1414{_}"My only fear is that if the assassin knew that I had identified him he would take care not to betray himself."
10102{_}1415{_}"You therefore think he will betray himself?"
10102{_}1416{_}"I hope so."
10102{_}1417{_}"By the fact that the man was attacked with an Italian stiletto, it would seem that his assailant was a fellow-countryman," suggested the detective.
10102{_}1418{_}"The evidence certainly points to that," I replied.
10102{_}1419{_}"You don't happen to be aware of anyone--any foreigner, I mean--who was, or might be his enemy?"
10102{_}1420{_}I responded in the negative.
10102{_}1421{_}"Ah," he went on, "these foreigners are always fighting among themselves and using knives.
10102{_}1422{_}I did ten years' service in Edinburgh and made lots of arrests for stabbing affrays.
10102{_}1423{_}Italians, like Greeks, are a dangerous lot when their blood is up."
10102{_}1424{_}Then he added: "Personally, it seems to me that the murdered man was enticed from London to that spot and coolly done away with--from some motive of revenge, most probably."
10102{_}1425{_}"Most probably," I said.
10102{_}1426{_}"A vendetta, perhaps.
10102{_}1427{_}I live in Italy, and therefore know the Italians well," I added.
10102{_}1428{_}I had given him my card, and told him with whom I was staying.
10102{_}1429{_}"Where were you yesterday, sir?"
10102{_}1430{_}he inquired presently.
10102{_}1431{_}"I was shooting--on the other side of the Nithsdale," I answered, and then went on to explain my movements, without, however, mentioning my visit to Rannoch.
10102{_}1432{_}"And although you know the murdered man so intimately, you have no suspicion of anyone in this district who was acquainted with him?"
10102{_}1433{_}"I know no one who knew him.
10102{_}1434{_}When he left my service he had never been in England."
10102{_}1435{_}"You say he was engaged in service in London?"
10102{_}1436{_}"Yes, at a restaurant in Oxford Street, I believe.
10102{_}1437{_}I met him accidentally in Pall Mall one evening, and he told me so."
10102{_}1438{_}"You don't know the name of the restaurant?"
10102{_}1439{_}"He did tell me, but unfortunately I have forgotten."
10102{_}1440{_}The detective drew a deep breath of regret.
10102{_}1441{_}"Someone who waited for him on the edge of that wood stepped out and killed him--that's evident," he said.
10102{_}1442{_}"Without a doubt."
10102{_}1443{_}"And my belief is that it was an Italian.
10102{_}1444{_}There were two foreigners who slept at a common lodging-house two nights ago and went on tramp towards Glasgow.
10102{_}1445{_}We have telegraphed after them, and hope we shall find them.
10102{_}1446{_}Scotsmen or Englishmen never use a knife of that pattern."
10102{_}1447{_}With his latter remark I entirely coincided.
10102{_}1448{_}In my own mind that was the strongest argument in favor of Leithcourt's innocence.
10102{_}1449{_}That the tenant of Rannoch had kept that secret tryst in daily patience I knew from my own observations, yet to me it scarcely seemed feasible that he would use a weapon so peculiarly Italian and yet so terribly deadly.
10102{_}1450{_}And then when I reflected further, recollecting that the body I had discovered was that of a woman and not a man, I stood staggered and bewildered by the utterly inexplicable enigma.
10102{_}1451{_}I promised the burly detective that in exchange for his secrecy regarding my statement that I would assist him in every manner possible in the solution of the problem.
10102{_}1452{_}"The real name of the murdered man must be at all costs withheld," I urged.
10102{_}1453{_}"It must not appear in the papers, for I feel confident that only by the pretense that he is unknown can we arrive at the truth.
10102{_}1454{_}If his name is given at the inquiry, then the assassin will certainly know that I have identified him."
10102{_}1455{_}"And what then?"
10102{_}1456{_}"Well," I said with some hesitation, "while I am believed to be in ignorance we shall have opportunity for obtaining the truth."
10102{_}1457{_}"Then you do really suspect?"
10102{_}1458{_}he said, again looking at me with those cold, blue eyes.
10102{_}1459{_}"I know not whom to suspect," I declared.
10102{_}1460{_}"It is a mystery why the man who was once my faithful servant should be enticed to that wood and stabbed to the heart."
10102{_}1461{_}"There is no one in the vicinity who knew him?"
10102{_}1462{_}"Not to my knowledge."
10102{_}1463{_}"We might obtain his address in London through his father in Leghorn," suggested the officer.
10102{_}1464{_}"I will write to-day if you so desire," I said readily.
10102{_}1465{_}"Indeed, I will get my friend the British Consul to go round and see the old man and telegraph the address if he obtains it."
10102{_}1466{_}"Capital!"
10102{_}1467{_}he declared.
10102{_}1468{_}"If you will do us this favor we shall be greatly indebted to you.
10102{_}1469{_}It is fortunate that we have established the victim's identity--otherwise we might be entirely in the dark.
10102{_}1470{_}A murdered foreigner is always more or less of a mystery."
10102{_}1471{_}Therefore, then and there, I took a sheet of paper and wrote to my old friend Hutcheson at Leghorn, asking him to make immediate inquiry of Olinto's father as to his son's address in London.
10102{_}1472{_}I said nothing to the police of that strange adventure of mine over in Lambeth, or of how the man now dead had saved my life.
10102{_}1473{_}That his enemies were my own he had most distinctly told me, therefore I felt some apprehension that I myself was not safe.
10102{_}1474{_}Yet in my hip pocket I always carried my revolver--just as I did in Italy--and I rather prided myself on my ability to shoot straight.
10102{_}1475{_}We sat for a long time discussing the strange affair.
10102{_}1476{_}In order to betray no eagerness to get away, I offered the big Highlander a cigar from my case, and we smoked together.
10102{_}1477{_}The inquiry would be held on the morrow, he told me, but as far as the public was concerned the body would remain as that of some person "unknown."
10102{_}1478{_}"And you had better not come to my uncle's house, or send anyone," I said.
10102{_}1479{_}"If you desire to see me, send me a line and I will meet you here in Dumfries.
10102{_}1480{_}It will be safer."
10102{_}1481{_}The officer looked at me with those keen eyes of his, and said:  "Really, Mr. Gregg, I can't quite make you out, I confess.
10102{_}1482{_}You seem to be apprehensive of your own safety.
10102{_}1483{_}Why?"
10102{_}1484{_}"Italians are a very curious people," I responded quickly.
10102{_}1485{_}"Their vendetta extends widely sometimes."
10102{_}1486{_}"Then you have reason to believe that the enemy of this poor fellow Santini may be your enemy also?"
10102{_}1487{_}"One never knows whom one offends when living in Italy," I laughed, as lightly as I could, endeavoring to allay his suspicion.
10102{_}1488{_}"He may have fallen beneath the assassin's knife by giving quite a small and possibly innocent offense to somebody.
10102{_}1489{_}Italian methods are not English, you know."
10102{_}1490{_}"By Jove, sir, and I'm jolly glad they're not!"
10102{_}1491{_}he said.
10102{_}1492{_}"I shouldn't think a police officer's life is a very safe one among all those secret murder societies I've read about."
10102{_}1493{_}"Ah!
10102{_}1494{_}what you read about them is often very much exaggerated," I assured him.
10102{_}1495{_}"It is the vendetta which is such a stain upon the character of the modern Italian; and depend upon it this affair in Rannoch Wood is the outcome of some revenge or other--probably over a love affair."
10102{_}1496{_}"But you will assist us, sir?"
10102{_}1497{_}he urged.
10102{_}1498{_}"You know the Italian language, which will be of great advantage; besides, the victim was your servant."
10102{_}1499{_}"Be discreet," I said.
10102{_}1500{_}"And in return I will do my very utmost to assist you in hunting down the assassin."
10102{_}1501{_}And thus we made our compact.
10102{_}1502{_}Half-an-hour after I was driving in the dog-cart through the pouring rain up the hill out of gray old Dumfries to my uncle's house.
10102{_}1503{_}As I descended from the cart and gave it over to a groom, old Davis, the butler, came forward, saying in a low voice:  "There's Miss Leithcourt waiting to see you, Mr. Gordon.
10102{_}1504{_}She's in the morning-room, and been there an hour.
10102{_}1505{_}She asked me not to tell anyone else she's here, sir."
10102{_}1506{_}"Then my aunt has not seen her?"
10102{_}1507{_}I exclaimed, scenting mystery in this unexpected visit.
10102{_}1508{_}"No, sir.
10102{_}1509{_}She wishes to see you alone, sir."
10102{_}1510{_}I walked across the big hall and along the corridor to the room the old man had indicated.
10102{_}1511{_}And as I opened the door and Muriel Leithcourt in plain black rose to meet me, I plainly saw from her white, haggard countenance that something had happened--that she had been forced by circumstances to come to me in strictest confidence.
10102{_}1512{_}Was she, I wondered, about to reveal to me the truth?
10102{_}1513{_}CHAPTER VI  THE GATHERING OF THE CLOUDS   "Mr. Gregg," exclaimed the girl with agitation, as she put forth her black-gloved hand, "I--I suppose you know--you've heard all about the discovery to-day up at the wood?
10102{_}1514{_}I need not tell you anything about it"  "Yes, Miss Leithcourt, I only wish you would tell me about it," I said gravely, inviting her to a chair and seating myself.
10102{_}1515{_}"I've heard some extraordinary story about a man being found dead, but I've been in Dumfries nearly all day.
10102{_}1516{_}Who is the man?"
10102{_}1517{_}"Ah!
10102{_}1518{_}that we don't know," she replied, pale-faced and anxious.
10102{_}1519{_}Her attitude was as though she wished to confide in me and yet still hesitated to do so.
10102{_}1520{_}"You've been waiting for me quite a long time, Davis tells me.
10102{_}1521{_}I regret that you should have done this.
10102{_}1522{_}If you had left word that you wished to see me, I would have come over to you at once."
10102{_}1523{_}"No.
10102{_}1524{_}I wanted to see you alone--that's the reason I am here.
10102{_}1525{_}They must not know at home that I've been over here, so I purposely asked the man not to announce me to your aunt."
10102{_}1526{_}"You want to see me privately," I said in a low, earnest voice.
10102{_}1527{_}"Why?
10102{_}1528{_}Is there any service I can render you?"
10102{_}1529{_}"Yes.
10102{_}1530{_}A very great one," she responded with quick eagerness, "I--well--the fact is, I have summoned courage to come to you and beg of you to help me.
10102{_}1531{_}I am in great distress--and I have not a single friend whom I can trust--in whom I can confide."
10102{_}1532{_}"I shall esteem it the highest honor if you will trust me," I said in deep earnestness.
10102{_}1533{_}"I can only assure you that I will remain loyal to your interests and to yourself."
10102{_}1534{_}"Ah!
10102{_}1535{_}I believe you will, Mr.
10102{_}1536{_}Gregg!"
10102{_}1537{_}she declared with enthusiasm, her large, dark eyes turned upon me--the eyes of a woman in sheer and bitter despair.
10102{_}1538{_}Her face was perfect, one of the most handsome I had ever gazed upon.
10102{_}1539{_}The more I saw of her the greater was the fascination she held over me.
10102{_}1540{_}A silence fell between us as she sat with her gloved hands lying idly in her lap.
10102{_}1541{_}Her lips moved nervously, but no sound came from them, so agitated was she, so eager to tell me something; and yet at the same time reluctant to take me into her confidence.
10102{_}1542{_}"Well?"
10102{_}1543{_}I asked at last in a low voice.
10102{_}1544{_}"I am quite ready to render you any service, if you will only command me."
10102{_}1545{_}"Ah!
10102{_}1546{_}But I fear what I require will strike you as so unusual--you will hesitate to act when I explain what service I require of you," she said doubtfully.
10102{_}1547{_}"I cannot tell you until I hear your wishes," I said, smiling, and yet puzzled at her attitude.
10102{_}1548{_}"It concerns the terrible discovery made up in Rannoch Wood," she said in a hoarse, nervous voice at last.
10102{_}1549{_}"That unknown man was murdered--stabbed to the heart."
10102{_}1550{_}"Well?"
10102{_}1551{_}"Well," she said, scarcely above a whisper, "I have suspicions."
10102{_}1552{_}"Of the murdered man's identity?"
10102{_}1553{_}"No.
10102{_}1554{_}Of the assassin."
10102{_}1555{_}I glanced at her sharply and saw the intense look in her dark, wide-open eyes.
10102{_}1556{_}"You believe you know who dealt the blow?"
10102{_}1557{_}"I have a suspicion--that is all.
10102{_}1558{_}Only I want you to help me, if you will."
10102{_}1559{_}"Most certainly," I responded.
10102{_}1560{_}"But if you believe you know the assassin you probably know something of the victim?"
10102{_}1561{_}"Only that he looked like a foreigner."
10102{_}1562{_}"Then you have seen him?"
10102{_}1563{_}I exclaimed, much surprised.
10102{_}1564{_}My remark caused her to hold her breath for an instant.
