10102{_}1565{_}Then she answered, rather lamely, it seemed to me:  "I saw him when the keepers brought the body to the castle."
10102{_}1566{_}Now, according to the account I had heard, the police had conveyed the dead man direct from the wood into Dumfries.
10102{_}1567{_}Was it possible, therefore, that she had seen Olinto before he met with his sudden end?
10102{_}1568{_}I feared to press her for an explanation at that moment, but, nevertheless, the admission that she had seen him struck me as a very peculiar fact.
10102{_}1569{_}"You judge him to be a foreigner?"
10102{_}1570{_}I remarked as casually as I could.
10102{_}1571{_}"From his features and complexion I guessed him to be Italian," she responded quickly, at which I pretended to express surprise.
10102{_}1572{_}"I saw him after the keepers had found him."
10102{_}1573{_}"Besides," she went on, "the stiletto was evidently an Italian one, which would almost make it appear that a foreigner was the assassin."
10102{_}1574{_}"Is that your own suspicion?"
10102{_}1575{_}"No."
10102{_}1576{_}"Why?"
10102{_}1577{_}She hesitated a moment, then in a low, eager voice she said:  "Because I have already seen that three-edged knife in another person's possession."
10102{_}1578{_}"That's pretty strong evidence," I declared.
10102{_}1579{_}"The person in question will have to prove that he was not in Rannoch Wood last evening at nightfall."
10102{_}1580{_}"How do you know it was done at nightfall?"
10102{_}1581{_}she asked quickly with some surprise, half-rising from her chair.
10102{_}1582{_}"I merely surmised that it was," I responded, inwardly blaming myself for my ill-timed admission.
10102{_}1583{_}"Ah!"
10102{_}1584{_}she said with a slight sigh, "there is more mystery in this affair than we have yet discovered, Mr. Gregg.
10102{_}1585{_}What, I wonder, brought the unfortunate young man up into our wood?"
10102{_}1586{_}"An appointment, without a doubt.
10102{_}1587{_}But with whom?"
10102{_}1588{_}She shook her head, saying:  "My father often goes to that spot to shoot pigeon in the evening.
10102{_}1589{_}He told us so at luncheon to-day.
10102{_}1590{_}How fortunate he was not there last night, or he might be suspected."
10102{_}1591{_}"Yes," I said.
10102{_}1592{_}"It is a very fortunate circumstance, for it cannot be a pleasant experience to be under suspicion of being an assassin.
10102{_}1593{_}He was at home last night, was he?"
10102{_}1594{_}I added casually.
10102{_}1595{_}"Of course.
10102{_}1596{_}Don't you recollect that when you called he chatted with you?
10102{_}1597{_}I did some typewriting for him in the study, and we were together all the afternoon--or at least till nearly five o'clock, when we went out into the hall to tea."
10102{_}1598{_}"Then what is your theory regarding the affair?"
10102{_}1599{_}I inquired, rather puzzled why she should so decisively prove an alibi for her father.
10102{_}1600{_}"It seems certain that the poor fellow went to the wood by appointment, and was killed.
10102{_}1601{_}But have you been up to the spot since the finding of the body?"
10102{_}1602{_}"No.
10102{_}1603{_}Have you?"
10102{_}1604{_}"Yes.
10102{_}1605{_}The affair interested me, and as soon as I recognized the old Italian knife in the hand of the keeper, I went up there and looked about.
10102{_}1606{_}I am glad I did so, for I found something which seems to have escaped the notice of the detectives."
10102{_}1607{_}"And what's that?"
10102{_}1608{_}I asked eagerly.
10102{_}1609{_}"Why, about three yards from the pool of blood where the unfortunate foreigner was found is another small pool of blood where the grass and ferns around are all crushed down as though there had been a struggle there."
10102{_}1610{_}"There may have been a struggle at that spot, and the man may have staggered some distance before he fell dead."
10102{_}1611{_}"Not if he had been struck in the heart, as they say.
10102{_}1612{_}He would fall, would he not?"
10102{_}1613{_}she suggested.
10102{_}1614{_}"No.
10102{_}1615{_}The police seem very dense, and this plain fact has not yet occurred to them.
10102{_}1616{_}Their theory is the same as what you suggest, but my own is something quite different, Mr. Gregg.
10102{_}1617{_}I believe that a second person also fell a victim," she added in a low, distinct tone.
10102{_}1618{_}I gazed at her open-mouthed.
10102{_}1619{_}Did she, I wondered, know the actual truth?
10102{_}1620{_}Was she aware that the woman who had fallen there had disappeared?
10102{_}1621{_}"A second person!"
10102{_}1622{_}I echoed, as though in surprise.
10102{_}1623{_}"Then do you believe that a double murder was committed?"
10102{_}1624{_}"I draw my conclusion from the fact that the young man, on being struck in the heart, could not have gone such a distance as that which separates the one mark from the other."
10102{_}1625{_}"But he might have been slightly wounded--on the hand, or in the face--at first, and then at the spot where he was found struck fatally," I suggested.
10102{_}1626{_}She shook her head dubiously, but made no reply to my argument.
10102{_}1627{_}Her confidence in her own surmises made it quite apparent that by some unknown means she was aware of the second victim.
10102{_}1628{_}Indeed, a few moments later she said to me:  "It is for this reason, Mr. Gregg, that I have sought you in confidence.
10102{_}1629{_}Nobody must know that I have come here to you, or they would suspect; and if suspicion fell upon me it would bring upon me a fate worse than death.
10102{_}1630{_}Remember, therefore, that my future is entirely in your hands."
10102{_}1631{_}"I don't quite understand," I said, rising and standing before her in the fading twilight, while the rain drove upon the old diamond window panes.
10102{_}1632{_}"But I can only assure you that whatever confidence you repose in me, I shall never abuse, Miss Leithcourt."
10102{_}1633{_}"I know, I know!"
10102{_}1634{_}she said quickly.
10102{_}1635{_}"I trust you in this matter implicitly.
10102{_}1636{_}I have come to you for many reasons, chief of them being that if a second victim has fallen beneath the hand of the assassin, it is, I know, a woman."
10102{_}1637{_}"A woman!
10102{_}1638{_}Whom?"
10102{_}1639{_}"At present I cannot tell you.
10102{_}1640{_}I must first establish the true facts.
10102{_}1641{_}If this woman were really stricken down, then her body lies concealed somewhere in the vicinity.
10102{_}1642{_}We must find it and bring home the crime to the guilty one."
10102{_}1643{_}"But if we succeed in finding it, could we place our hand upon the assassin?"
10102{_}1644{_}I asked, looking straight at her.
10102{_}1645{_}"If we find it, the crime would then tell its own tale--it would convict the person in whose hand I have seen that fatal weapon," was her clear, bold answer.
10102{_}1646{_}"Then you wish me to assist you in this search, Miss Leithcourt?"
10102{_}1647{_}I said, wondering if her suspicions rested upon that mysterious yachtsman, Philip Hornby, the man to whom she was engaged.
10102{_}1648{_}"Yes, I would beg of you to do your utmost in secret to endeavor to discover the body of the second victim.
10102{_}1649{_}It is a woman--of that I am certain.
10102{_}1650{_}Find her, and we shall then be able to bring the crime home to the assassin."
10102{_}1651{_}"But my search may bring suspicion upon me," I remarked.
10102{_}1652{_}"It will be difficult to examine the whole wood without arousing the curiosity of somebody--the keeper or the police."
10102{_}1653{_}"I have already thought of that," she said.
10102{_}1654{_}"I will pretend to-morrow to lose this watch-bracelet in the wood," and she held up her slim wrist to show me the little enameled watch set in her bracelet.
10102{_}1655{_}"Then you and I will search for it diligently, and the police will never suspect the real reason of our investigation.
10102{_}1656{_}To-morrow I shall write to you telling you about my loss, and you will come over to Rannoch and offer to help me."
10102{_}1657{_}I was silent for a moment.
10102{_}1658{_}"Is Mr. Woodroffe back at the castle?
10102{_}1659{_}I heard he was to return to-day."
10102{_}1660{_}"No.
10102{_}1661{_}I had a letter from him from Bordeaux a week ago.
10102{_}1662{_}He is still on the Continent.
10102{_}1663{_}I believe, indeed, he has gone to Russia, where he sometimes has business."
10102{_}1664{_}"I asked you the question, Miss Muriel, because I thought if Mr. Woodroffe were here, he might object to our searching in company," I explained, smiling.
10102{_}1665{_}Her cheeks flushed slightly, as though confused at my reference to her engagement, and she said mischievously:  "I don't see why he should object in the least.
10102{_}1666{_}If you are good enough to assist me to search for my bracelet, he surely ought to be much obliged to you."
10102{_}1667{_}It was on the tip of my tongue to explain to that dark-eyed, handsome girl the circumstances in which I had met her lover on the sunny Mediterranean shore, yet prudence forbade me to refer to the matter, and I at once gladly accepted her invitation to investigate the curious disappearance of the body of poor Olinto's fellow-victim.
10102{_}1668{_}What secret knowledge could be possessed by that smart, handsome girl before me?
10102{_}1669{_}That her suspicions were in the right direction I felt confident, yet if the dead woman had been removed and hidden by the assassin it must have been after the discovery made by me.
10102{_}1670{_}The fellow must have actually dared to return to the spot and carry off the victim.
10102{_}1671{_}Yet if he had actually done that, why did he allow the corpse of the Italian to remain and await discovery?
10102{_}1672{_}He might perhaps have been disturbed and compelled to make good his escape.
10102{_}1673{_}"If the woman was really removed the assassin must surely have had some assistance," I pointed out.
10102{_}1674{_}"He could not have carried the body very far unaided."
10102{_}1675{_}She agreed with me, but expressed a belief that the double crime had been committed alone and unaided.
10102{_}1676{_}"Have you any idea as to the motive?"
10102{_}1677{_}I asked her, eager to hear her reply.
10102{_}1678{_}"Well," she answered hesitatingly, "if the woman has fallen a victim, the motive will become plain; but if not, then the matter must remain a complete mystery."
10102{_}1679{_}"You tell me, Miss Muriel, that you suspect the truth, and yet you deny all knowledge of the murdered man!"
10102{_}1680{_}I exclaimed in a tone of slight reproach.
10102{_}1681{_}"Until we have cleared up the mystery of the woman I can say nothing," was her answer.
10102{_}1682{_}"I can only tell you, Mr. Gregg, that if what I suspect is true, then the affair will be found to be one of the strangest, most startling and most ingenious plots ever devised by one man against the life of another."
10102{_}1683{_}"Then a man is the assassin, you think?"
10102{_}1684{_}I exclaimed quickly.
10102{_}1685{_}"I believe so.
10102{_}1686{_}But even of that I am not at all sure.
10102{_}1687{_}We must first find the woman."
10102{_}1688{_}She seemed so positive that a woman had also fallen beneath that deadly _misericordia_ that I fell to wondering whether she, like myself, had discovered the body, and was therefore certain that a second crime had been committed.
10102{_}1689{_}But I did not seek to question her further, lest her own suspicions might become aroused.
10102{_}1690{_}My own policy was to remain silent and to wait.
10102{_}1691{_}The woman sitting before me was herself a mystery.
10102{_}1692{_}Then, when the rain had abated, I told Davis to send her trap a little way up the high-road, so that my aunt and uncle should not see her departing; and after helping her on with her loose driving-coat, we left by one of the servants' entrances, and I saw her into her high dog-cart and stood bareheaded in the muddy high-road as she drove away into the gloom.
10102{_}1693{_}*       *       *       *       *  Rannoch Wood was already in its gold-brown glory of autumn, and as I stood with Muriel Leithcourt on the edge of it, near the spot where Olinto Santini had fallen, the morning sun was shining in a cloudless sky.
10102{_}1694{_}True to her promise, she had sent me a note by one of the grooms asking me to help search for her bracelet, and I had driven over at once to Rannoch and found her alone awaiting me.
10102{_}1695{_}The shooting party had gone over to a distant part of the estate, therefore we were able to stroll together up the hill and commence our investigations without let or hindrance.
10102{_}1696{_}She was sensibly dressed in a short tweed skirt, high shooting-boots and a tam-o'-shanter hat, while I also had on an old shooting-suit and carried a thick serviceable stick with which I could prod likely spots.
10102{_}1697{_}On arrival at the wood I asked her opinion which was the most likely corner, but she replied:  "I know so little of this place, Mr. Gregg.
10102{_}1698{_}You have known it for years, while this is only my first season here."
10102{_}1699{_}"Very well," I answered.
10102{_}1700{_}"Let us place ourselves in the position of the murderer, who probably knew the wood and wished to conceal a body in the vicinity without risk of conveying it far.
10102{_}1701{_}On this, the left side, the wood has been thinned out for nearly half a mile, and therefore affords but little cover, while here, to the right, it slopes down gently to the valley and is very thick and partly impenetrable.
10102{_}1702{_}There can therefore have been no two courses open to him.
10102{_}1703{_}He would look for a likely place to the right.
10102{_}1704{_}Let us start here, and first take a small circle, examining every bush carefully.
10102{_}1705{_}The body may have easily been pushed in beneath a thicket and well escape observation."
10102{_}1706{_}And so together, after taking our bearings, we started off, working our way into the thick undergrowth, beating with our sticks, and making minute examination of every bush or heap of dead leaves.
10102{_}1707{_}In parts, the great spreading trees shut out the light, rendering our investigations very difficult; but we kept on, my companion advancing with an eagerness which showed that the fact of the woman's body being there was no mere surmise.
10102{_}1708{_}All through the morning we walked on, our hands badly torn by brambles.
10102{_}1709{_}Even Muriel's thick gloves did not wholly protect her, and once when she received a nasty scratch across the cheek, she stopped and laughingly exclaimed:  "Now what untruth must I invent to account for that?"
10102{_}1710{_}My own coat was badly torn, and more than once I was compelled to scramble through almost impassable thickets; yet we found no trace of any previous intruder, and having completed our circle were compelled to admit that the gruesome evidence of the second crime did not exist at that spot.
10102{_}1711{_}More than once I felt half inclined to tell her how I had actually discovered the body of the woman, yet on reflection I foresaw that in such circumstances silence was best.
10102{_}1712{_}If I desired to solve the strange complicated enigma which had thus culminated in a double crime, it would be necessary for me to keep my own counsel and remain patient and watchful.
10102{_}1713{_}When Hutcheson replied from Leghorn, and when I discovered where Olinto was employed, I might perhaps follow up the clues from that end.
10102{_}1714{_}I might find his wife Armida and learn something of importance from her.
10102{_}1715{_}So I was hopeful, and by reason of that hope remained silent.
10102{_}1716{_}Muriel was untiring in her activity.
10102{_}1717{_}Hither and thither she went, beating down the high bracken and tangles of weeds, poking with her stick into every hole and corner, and going further and further into the wood in the certainty that the body was therein concealed.
10102{_}1718{_}For my own part, however, I was not too sanguine of success.
10102{_}1719{_}The portion of the wood which we had already exhausted seemed to be the most likely point.
10102{_}1720{_}To carry the body far would require assistance, and in my own mind I believed the crime to have been the work of one person.
10102{_}1721{_}There was no path in the wood in that direction, but soon we came to a deep wooded ravine of the existence of which I was in ignorance.
10102{_}1722{_}It was a kind of small glen through which a rivulet flowed, but the banks were covered with a thick impenetrable undergrowth out of which sprang many fine old trees, a place that had apparently existed for centuries undisturbed, for here and there a giant trunk that had decayed and fallen lay across the bank, or had rolled into the rocky bed far below.
10102{_}1723{_}"This is a most likely place," declared my dainty little companion as we approached it.
10102{_}1724{_}"Anything could easily be concealed in that high bracken down there.
10102{_}1725{_}Let us search the whole glen from end to end," she cried with enthusiasm.
10102{_}1726{_}Acting upon her suggestion and without thought of luncheon, we made a descent of the steep bank until we reached the rocky bed of the stream, and then by springing from stone to stone--sometimes slipping into the water, be it said--we commenced to beat the bracken and carefully examine every bush.
10102{_}1727{_}Progress was not swift.
10102{_}1728{_}Once the girl, lithe and athletic as she was, slipped off a mossy stone into a hole where the water was up to her knees.
10102{_}1729{_}But she only laughed gayly at the accident, and wringing out her wet skirt, said:  "It doesn't matter in the least, if we only find what we're in search of."
10102{_}1730{_}And then, undaunted, she went on, springing from stone to stone and steadying herself with her stick.
10102{_}1731{_}If we could only discover the body of the dead woman, then the rest would be clear, she declared.
10102{_}1732{_}She would openly denounce the assassin.
10102{_}1733{_}As we went on I revolved within my mind all the curious circumstances in connection with the amazing affair, and recollected my old friend Jack Durnford's words when we stood upon the quarter-deck of the _Bulwark_ and I had related to him the visit of the mysterious yacht.
10102{_}1734{_}I too had left one effort untried, and I blamed myself for overlooking it.
10102{_}1735{_}I had not sought of that Bond Street photographer the name and address of the original of the photograph that had been mutilated and destroyed--that girl with the magnificent eyes that had so attracted me.
10102{_}1736{_}The afternoon passed, and yet we were not successful.
10102{_}1737{_}I was faint with hunger and thirst, yet my companion did not once complain.
10102{_}1738{_}Her energy was marvelous--and yet was she not hunting down a criminal?
10102{_}1739{_}was she not determined to obtain such evidence as would enable her to speak the truth fearlessly, and with confidence that it would have the effect of convicting the guilty one?
10102{_}1740{_}Slowly we toiled on up the picturesque little glen for nearly a mile and a half.
10102{_}1741{_}Its beauties were extraordinary, and the silence was unbroken save for the musical ripple of the water over the stones.
10102{_}1742{_}Hidden there in the center of that great wood, no one had visited it perhaps for years, not even the keepers, for no path led there, and by reason of the tangle of briars and bush it was utterly ungetatable.
10102{_}1743{_}Indeed, it had ruined our clothes to search there, and as we went on with so many windings and turns we became utterly out of our bearings.
10102{_}1744{_}We knew ourselves to be in the center of the wood, but that was all.
10102{_}1745{_}The sun had set, and the sky above showed the crimson of the distant afterglow, warning us that it was time we began to think of how to make our exit.
10102{_}1746{_}We were passing around a sharp bend in the glen where the boulders were so thickly moss-grown that our feet fell noiselessly, when I thought I heard a voice, and raising my hand we both halted suddenly.
10102{_}1747{_}"Someone is there," I whispered quickly.
10102{_}1748{_}"Behind that rock."
10102{_}1749{_}She nodded in the affirmative, for she, too, had heard the voice.
10102{_}1750{_}We listened, but the sound was not repeated.
10102{_}1751{_}That someone was on the other side of the rock I knew, for in a tree in the vicinity a thrush was hopping from twig to twig, sounding its alarm-cry and objecting to being disturbed.
10102{_}1752{_}Therefore we crept silently forward together to ascertain who were the intruders.
10102{_}1753{_}The only manner, however, in which to get a view beyond the huge rock that, having fallen across the stream centuries ago, had diverted its channel, was to clamber up its mossy sides to the summit.
10102{_}1754{_}This we did eagerly and breathlessly, without betraying our presence by the utterance of a single word.
10102{_}1755{_}To reach the side of the boulder we were compelled to walk through the shallow water, but Muriel, quite undaunted, sprang lithely along at my side, and with one accord we swarmed up the steep rock, gripping its slippery face with our hands and laying ourselves flat as we came to its summit.
10102{_}1756{_}Then together we peered over, just, however, in time to see two dark figures of men disappearing into the thicket on the opposite side of the glen.
10102{_}1757{_}"Who are they, I wonder?"
10102{_}1758{_}I asked.
10102{_}1759{_}"Do you recognize them?"
10102{_}1760{_}"No.
10102{_}1761{_}They are entire strangers to me," was her answer.
10102{_}1762{_}"But they seem fairly well dressed.
10102{_}1763{_}Perhaps two sportsmen from some shooting-party in the neighborhood.
10102{_}1764{_}They've lost their way most probably."
10102{_}1765{_}"But I don't think they carried guns," I said.
10102{_}1766{_}"One of them had something over his shoulder?"
10102{_}1767{_}"Wasn't it a gun?
10102{_}1768{_}I thought it was."
10102{_}1769{_}"No, he wasn't carrying it like he'd carry a gun.
10102{_}1770{_}It was short--and seemed more like a spade."
10102{_}1771{_}"A spade!"
10102{_}1772{_}she gasped quickly in a low voice.
10102{_}1773{_}"A spade!
10102{_}1774{_}Are you certain of that?"
10102{_}1775{_}"No, not at all certain.
10102{_}1776{_}We only had an instantaneous glance of them.
10102{_}1777{_}We were unfortunately too late to see them face to face."
10102{_}1778{_}"The back of one of the men, the tall fellow in the brown suit, was broad and square--the back of someone who is familiar to me, only for the moment I can't recollect whose it resembles."
10102{_}1779{_}She only spoke in a whisper, fearing lest we should be discovered.
10102{_}1780{_}I longed to scramble down and rush after the intruders, only the belief that one of them carried a spade and the other an iron bar struck me as curious, while at the same moment my eye caught sight of a portion of the ground below us at the base of the rock which had evidently been recently disturbed.
10102{_}1781{_}"It is a spade the man is carrying!"
10102{_}1782{_}I cried excitedly.
10102{_}1783{_}"Look down there!
10102{_}1784{_}They've just been burying something!"
10102{_}1785{_}Her quick eyes followed the direction I indicated, and she answered:  "I really believe they have concealed something!"
10102{_}1786{_}Then when we had allowed the men to get beyond hearing, we both slipped down to the other side of the boulder and there discovered many signs that the earth had been hurriedly excavated and only just replaced.
10102{_}1787{_}Quicker than it takes to describe the exciting incident which followed, we broke down the branch of a tree and with it commenced moving the freshly disturbed earth, which was still soft and easily removed.
10102{_}1788{_}Muriel found a dead branch in the vicinity, and both of us set to work with a will, eager to ascertain what was hidden there.
10102{_}1789{_}That something had certainly been concealed was, to us, quite evident, but what it really was we could not surmise.
10102{_}1790{_}The hole they had dug did not seem large enough to admit a human body, yet leaves had been carefully strewn over the place which, if approached from any other point than the high-up one whence we had seen it, would arouse no suspicion that the ground had ever been interfered with.
10102{_}1791{_}Digging with a piece of wood was hard and laborious work and it was a long time before we removed sufficient earth to make a hole of any size.
10102{_}1792{_}But Muriel exerted all her energy, and both of us worked on in dogged silence full of wonder and anticipation.
10102{_}1793{_}With a spade we should have soon been able to investigate, but the earth having apparently been stamped down hard prior to the last covering being put upon it, our progress was very slow and difficult.
10102{_}1794{_}At last, a quarter of an hour or so after we had commenced, Muriel, standing in the hole and having dug her stake deeply into the ground, suddenly cried:  "Look!
10102{_}1795{_}Look, Mr. Gregg!
10102{_}1796{_}Why--whatever is that?"
10102{_}1797{_}I bent forward as she indicated, and my eyes met an object so unexpected that I was held dumb and motionless.
10102{_}1798{_}By what we had succeeded in discovering, the mystery was increased rather than diminished.
10102{_}1799{_}I gave vent to an ejaculation of complete bewilderment, and looked blankly into my companion's face.
10102{_}1800{_}The amazing enigma was surely complete!
10102{_}1801{_}CHAPTER VII  CONTAINS A SURPRISE   The first object brought to light, about two feet beneath the surface, was a piece of dark gray woolen stuff which, when the mold was removed, proved to be part of a woman's skirt.
10102{_}1802{_}With frantic eagerness I got into the hole we had made and removed the soil with my hands, until I suddenly touched something hard.
10102{_}1803{_}A body lay there, doubled up and crushed into the well-like hole the men had dug.
10102{_}1804{_}Together we pulled it out, when, to my surprise, on wiping away the dirt from the hard waxen features, I recognized it as the body of Armida, the woman who had been my servant in Leghorn and who had afterwards married Olinto.
10102{_}1805{_}Both had been assassinated!
10102{_}1806{_}When Muriel gazed upon the dead woman's face she gave vent to an expression of surprise.
10102{_}1807{_}The body was evidently not that of the person she had expected to find.
10102{_}1808{_}"Who is she, I wonder?"
10102{_}1809{_}my companion ejaculated.
10102{_}1810{_}"Not a lady, evidently, by her dress and hands."
10102{_}1811{_}"Evidently not," was my response, for I still deemed it best to keep my own counsel.
10102{_}1812{_}I recollected the story Olinto had told me about his wife; of her illness and her longing to return to Italy.
10102{_}1813{_}Yet the dead woman's countenance must have been healthy enough in life, although her hands were rough and hard, showing that she had been doing manual labor.
10102{_}1814{_}Armida had been a particularly good housemaid, a black-haired, black-eyed Tuscan, quick, cleanly, and full of a keen sense of humor.
10102{_}1815{_}It was a great shock to me to find her lying there dead.
10102{_}1816{_}The breast of her dress was stained with dried blood, which, on examination, I found had issued from a deep and fatal wound beneath the ear where she had been struck an unerring blow that had severed the artery.
10102{_}1817{_}"Those men--those men who buried her!
10102{_}1818{_}I wonder who they were?"
10102{_}1819{_}my companion exclaimed in a hushed voice.
10102{_}1820{_}"We must follow them and ascertain.
10102{_}1821{_}They are certainly the murderers who have returned in secret and concealed the evidence of this second crime."
10102{_}1822{_}"Yes," I said.
10102{_}1823{_}"Let us go after them.
10102{_}1824{_}They must not escape us."
10102{_}1825{_}Then, leaving the exhumed body beneath a tree, I caught Muriel by the waist and waded across the deep channel worn by the stream at that point, after which we both ascended the steep bank where the pair had disappeared in the darkness of the wood.
10102{_}1826{_}I blamed myself a thousand times for not following them, yet my suspicions had not been aroused until after they had disappeared.
10102{_}1827{_}The back of the man in a snuff-colored suit was, she felt confident, familiar to her.
10102{_}1828{_}She repeated what she had already told me, yet she could not remember where she had seen a similar figure before.
10102{_}1829{_}We went on through the gloomy forest, for the light had faded and evening was now creeping on.
10102{_}1830{_}From time to time we halted and listened.
10102{_}1831{_}But there was a dead silence, broken only by the shrill cry of a night bird and the low rustling of the leaves in the autumn wind.
10102{_}1832{_}The men knew their way, it seemed, even though the wood was trackless.
10102{_}1833{_}Yet they had nearly twenty minutes start of us, and in that time they might be already out in the open country.
10102{_}1834{_}Would they succeed in evading us?
10102{_}1835{_}Yet even if they did, I could describe the dress of one of them, while that of his companion was, as far as I made out, dark blue, of a somewhat nautical cut.
10102{_}1836{_}He wore also a flat cap, with a peak.
10102{_}1837{_}We went on, striking straight for the open moorland which we knew bounded the woods in that direction, and before the light had entirely faded we found ourselves out amongst the heather with the distant hills looming dark against the horizon.
10102{_}1838{_}But we saw no sign of the men who had so secretly concealed the body of their victim.
10102{_}1839{_}"I will take you back to the castle, Miss Leithcourt," I said.
10102{_}1840{_}"And then I'll drive on into Dumfries and see the police.
10102{_}1841{_}These men must be arrested."
10102{_}1842{_}"Yes, do," she urged.
10102{_}1843{_}"I will get into the house by the stable-yard, for they must not see me in this terrible plight."
10102{_}1844{_}It was rough walking, therefore at my invitation she took my arm, and as she did so I felt that she was shivering.
10102{_}1845{_}"You are very wet," I remarked.
10102{_}1846{_}"I hope you won't take cold."
10102{_}1847{_}"Oh!
10102{_}1848{_}I'm used to getting wet.
10102{_}1849{_}I drive and cycle a lot, you know, and very often get drenched," was her reply.
10102{_}1850{_}Then after a pause she said: "We must discover who that woman was.
10102{_}1851{_}She seems, from her complexion and her hair, to be a foreigner, like the man."
10102{_}1852{_}"Yes, I think so," was my reply.
10102{_}1853{_}"I will tell the police all that we have found out, and they will go there presently and recover the body."
10102{_}1854{_}"If they can only find those two men, then we should know the truth," she declared.
10102{_}1855{_}"One of them--the one in brown--was unusually broad-shouldered, and seemed to walk with a slight stoop."
10102{_}1856{_}"You expected to discover another woman, did you not, Miss Leithcourt?"
10102{_}1857{_}I asked presently, as we walked across the moor.
10102{_}1858{_}"Yes," she answered.
10102{_}1859{_}"I expected to find an entirely different person."
10102{_}1860{_}"And if you had found her it would have proved the guilt of someone with whom you are acquainted?"
10102{_}1861{_}She nodded in the affirmative.
10102{_}1862{_}"Then what we have found this evening does not convey to you the identity of the assassins?"
10102{_}1863{_}"No, unfortunately it does not.
10102{_}1864{_}We must for the present leave the matter in the hands of the police."
10102{_}1865{_}"But if the identity of the dead woman is established?"
10102{_}1866{_}I asked.
10102{_}1867{_}"It might furnish me with a clue," she exclaimed quickly.
10102{_}1868{_}"Yes, try and discover who she is."
10102{_}1869{_}"Who was the woman you expected to find?"
10102{_}1870{_}"A friend--a very dear friend."
10102{_}1871{_}"Will you not tell me her name?"
10102{_}1872{_}I inquired.
10102{_}1873{_}"No, it would be unfair to her," she responded decisively, an answer which to me was particularly tantalizing.
10102{_}1874{_}On we plodded in silence, our thoughts too full for words.
10102{_}1875{_}Was it not strange that the mysterious yachtsman should be her lover, and stranger still that on recognizing me he should have escaped, not only from Scotland, but away to the Continent?
10102{_}1876{_}Was not that, in itself, evidence of guilt and fear?
10102{_}1877{_}It was quite dark when I took leave of my bright little companion, who, tired out and yet uncomplaining, pressed my hand and wished me good fortune in my investigations.
10102{_}1878{_}"I shall await you to-morrow afternoon.
10102{_}1879{_}Call and tell me everything, won't you?"
10102{_}1880{_}I promised, and then she disappeared into the great stable-yard behind the castle, while I went on down the dark road and then struck across the open fields to my uncle's house.
10102{_}1881{_}At half-past nine that night I pulled up the dog-cart before the chief police-station in Dumfries, and alighting at once sought the big fair Highlander, Mackenzie, with whom I had had the consultation on the previous day.
10102{_}1882{_}When we were seated in his room beneath the hissing gas-jet, I related my adventure and the result of my investigation.
10102{_}1883{_}"What?"
10102{_}1884{_}he cried, jumping up.
10102{_}1885{_}"You've unearthed another body--a woman's?"
10102{_}1886{_}"I have.
10102{_}1887{_}And what is more, I can identify her," I replied.
10102{_}1888{_}"Her name is Armida, and she was wife of the murdered man Olinto Santini."
10102{_}1889{_}"Then both husband and wife were killed?"
10102{_}1890{_}"Without a doubt--a double tragedy."
10102{_}1891{_}"But the two men who concealed the body!
10102{_}1892{_}Will you describe them?"
10102{_}1893{_}I did so, and he wrote at my dictation, afterwards remarking--  "We must find them."
10102{_}1894{_}And calling in one of his sub-inspectors, he gave him instructions for the immediate circulation of the description to all the police-stations in the county, saying the two men were wanted on a charge of willful murder.
10102{_}1895{_}When the official had gone out again and we were alone, Mackenzie turned to me and asked--  "What induced you to search the wood?
10102{_}1896{_}Why did you suspect a second crime?"
10102{_}1897{_}His question nonplused me for the moment.
10102{_}1898{_}"Well, you see, I had identified the young man Olinto, and knowing him to be married and devoted to his wife, I suspected that she had accompanied him here.
10102{_}1899{_}It was entirely a vague surmise.
10102{_}1900{_}I wondered whether, if the poor fellow had fallen a victim to his enemies, she had not also been struck down."
10102{_}1901{_}His lips were pressed together in distinct dissatisfaction.
10102{_}1902{_}I knew my explanation to be a very lame one, but at all hazards I could not import Muriel's name into the affair.
10102{_}1903{_}I had given her my promise, and I intended to keep it.
10102{_}1904{_}"Then the body is still in the glen, where you left it?"
10102{_}1905{_}"Yes.
10102{_}1906{_}If you wish, I will take you to the spot.
10102{_}1907{_}I can drive you and your assistant up there."
10102{_}1908{_}"Certainly.
10102{_}1909{_}Let us go," he exclaimed, rising at once and ringing his bell.
10102{_}1910{_}"Get three good lanterns and some matches, and put them in this gentleman's trap outside," he said to the constable who answered his summons.
10102{_}1911{_}"And tell Gilbert Campbell that I want him to go with me up to Rannoch Wood."
10102{_}1912{_}"Yes, sir," answered the man; and the door again closed.
10102{_}1913{_}"It's a pity--a thousand pities, Mr. Gregg, that you didn't stop those two men who buried the body."
10102{_}1914{_}"They were already across the stream, and disappearing into the thicket before I mounted the rock," I explained.
10102{_}1915{_}"Besides, at the moment I had no suspicion of what they'd been doing.
10102{_}1916{_}I believed them to be stragglers from a neighboring shooting-party who had lost their way."
10102{_}1917{_}"Ah, most unfortunate!"
10102{_}1918{_}he said.
10102{_}1919{_}"I hope they don't escape us.
10102{_}1920{_}If they're foreigners, they are not likely to get away.
10102{_}1921{_}But if they're English or Scots, then I fear there's but little chance of us coming up with them.
10102{_}1922{_}Yesterday at the inquest the identity of the murdered man was strictly preserved, and the inquiry was adjourned for a fortnight."
10102{_}1923{_}"Of course my name was not mentioned?"
10102{_}1924{_}I said.
10102{_}1925{_}"Of course not," was the detective's reply.
10102{_}1926{_}Then he asked: "When do you expect to get a telegram from your friend, the Consul at Leghorn?
10102{_}1927{_}I am anxious for that, in order that we may commence inquiries in London."
10102{_}1928{_}"The day after to-morrow, I hope.
10102{_}1929{_}He will certainly reply at once, providing the dead man's father can still be found."
10102{_}1930{_}And at that moment a tall, thin man, who proved to be Detective Campbell, entered, and five minutes later we were all three driving over the uneven cobbles of Dumfries and out in the darkness towards Rannoch.
10102{_}1931{_}It was cloudy and starless, with a chill mist hanging over the valley; but my uncle's cob was a swift one, and we soon began to ascend the hill up past the castle, and then, turning to the left, drove along a steep, rough by-road which led to the south of the wood and out across the moor.
10102{_}1932{_}When we reached the latter we all descended, and I led the horse, for owing to the many treacherous bogs it was unsafe to drive further.
10102{_}1933{_}So, with Mackenzie and Campbell carrying lanterns, we walked on carefully, skirting the wood for nearly a mile until we came to the rough wall over which I had clambered with Muriel.
10102{_}1934{_}I recognized the spot, and having tied up the cob we all three plunged into the pitch-darkness of the wood, keeping straight on in the direction of the glen, and halting every now and then to listen for the rippling of the stream.
10102{_}1935{_}At last, after some difficulty, we discovered it, and searching along the bank with our three powerful lights, I presently detected the huge moss-grown boulder whereon I had stood when the pair of fugitives had disappeared.
10102{_}1936{_}"Look!"
10102{_}1937{_}I cried.
10102{_}1938{_}"There's the spot!"
10102{_}1939{_}And quickly we clambered down the steep bank, lowering ourselves by the branches of the trees until we came to the water into which I waded, being followed closely by my two companions.
10102{_}1940{_}On gaining the opposite side I clambered up to the base of the boulder and lowered my lantern to reveal to them the gruesome evidence of the second crime, but the next instant I cried--  "Why!
10102{_}1941{_}It's gone!"
10102{_}1942{_}"Gone!"
10102{_}1943{_}gasped the two men.
10102{_}1944{_}"Yes.
10102{_}1945{_}It was here.
10102{_}1946{_}Look!
10102{_}1947{_}this is the hole where they buried it!
10102{_}1948{_}But they evidently returned, and finding it exhumed, they've retaken possession of it and carried it away!"
10102{_}1949{_}The two detectives gazed down to where I indicated, and then looked at each other without exchanging a word.
10102{_}1950{_}As we stood there dumbfounded at the disappearance of the body, the Highlander's quick glance caught something, and stooping he picked it up and examined the little object by the aid of his lantern.
10102{_}1951{_}Within his palm I saw lying a tiny little gold cross, about an inch long, enameled in red, while in the center was a circular miniature of a kneeling saint, an elegant and beautifully executed little trinket which might have adorned a lady's bracelet.
10102{_}1952{_}"This is a pretty little thing!"
10102{_}1953{_}remarked the detective.
10102{_}1954{_}"It may possibly lead us to something.
10102{_}1955{_}But, Mr. Gregg," he added, turning to me, "are you quite certain you left the body here?"
10102{_}1956{_}"Certain?"
10102{_}1957{_}I echoed.
10102{_}1958{_}"Why, look at the hole I made.
10102{_}1959{_}You don't think I have any interest in leading you here on a fool's errand, do you?"
10102{_}1960{_}"Not at all," he said apologetically.
10102{_}1961{_}"Only the whole affair seems so very inconceivable--I mean that the men, having once got rid of the evidence of their crime, would hardly return to the spot and re-obtain possession of it."
10102{_}1962{_}"Unless they watched me exhume it, and feared the consequences if it fell into your hands," I suggested.
10102{_}1963{_}"Of course they might have watched you from behind the trees, and when you had gone they came and carried it away somewhere else," he remarked dubiously; "but even if they did, it must be in this wood.
10102{_}1964{_}They would never risk carrying a body very far, and here is surely the best place of concealment in the whole country."
10102{_}1965{_}"The only thing remaining is to search the wood at daylight," I suggested.
10102{_}1966{_}"If the two men came back here during my absence they may still be on the watch in the vicinity."
10102{_}1967{_}"Most probably they are.
10102{_}1968{_}We must take every precaution," he said decisively.
10102{_}1969{_}And then, with our lanterns lowered, we made an examination of the vicinity, without, however, discovering anything else to furnish us with a clew.
10102{_}1970{_}While I had been absent the body of the unfortunate Armida had disappeared--a fact which, knowing all that I did, was doubly mysterious.
10102{_}1971{_}The pair had, without doubt, watched Muriel and myself, and as soon as we had gone they had returned and carried off the ghastly remains of the poor woman who had been so foully done to death.
10102{_}1972{_}But who were the men--the fellow with the broad shoulders whom Muriel recognized, and the slim seafarer in his pilot-coat and peaked cap?
10102{_}1973{_}The enigma each hour became more and more inscrutable.
10102{_}1974{_}At dawn Mackenzie, with four of his men, made a thorough examination of the wood, but although they continued until dusk they discovered nothing, neither was anything heard of the mysterious seafarer and his companion in brown tweeds.
10102{_}1975{_}I called on Muriel as arranged, and explained how the body had so suddenly disappeared, whereupon she stared at me pale-faced, saying--  "The assassins must have watched us!
10102{_}1976{_}They are aware, then, that we have knowledge of their crime?"
10102{_}1977{_}"Of course," I said.
10102{_}1978{_}"Ah!"
10102{_}1979{_}she cried hoarsely.
10102{_}1980{_}"Then we are both in deadly peril--peril of our own lives!
10102{_}1981{_}These people will hesitate at nothing.
10102{_}1982{_}Both you and I are marked down by them, without a doubt.
10102{_}1983{_}We must both be wary not to fall into any trap they may lay for us."
10102{_}1984{_}Her very words seemed an admission that she was aware of the identity of the conspirators, and yet she would give me no clue to them.
10102{_}1985{_}We went out and up the drive together to the kennels, where her father, a tall, imposing figure in his shooting-kit, was giving orders to the keepers.
10102{_}1986{_}"Hulloa, Gregg!"
10102{_}1987{_}he cried merrily, extending his hand.
10102{_}1988{_}"You'll make one of a party to Glenlea to-morrow, won't you?
10102{_}1989{_}Paton and Phillips are coming.
10102{_}1990{_}Ten sharp here, and the ladies are coming out to lunch with us."
10102{_}1991{_}"Thanks," I said, accepting with pleasure, for by so doing I saw that I might be afforded an opportunity of being near Muriel.
10102{_}1992{_}The fact that the assassins were aware of our knowledge seemed to have caused her the greatest apprehension lest evil should befall us.
10102{_}1993{_}Then, as we turned away to go back to the house, Leithcourt said to me--  "You know all about the discovery up at the wood the other day!
10102{_}1994{_}Horrible affair--a young foreigner found murdered."
10102{_}1995{_}"Yes.
10102{_}1996{_}I've heard about it," I responded.
10102{_}1997{_}"And the police are worse than useless," he declared with disgust.
10102{_}1998{_}"They haven't discovered who the fellow is yet.
10102{_}1999{_}Why, if it had happened anywhere else but in Scotland, they'd have arrested the assassin before this."
10102{_}2000{_}"He's an entire stranger, I hear," I remarked.
10102{_}2001{_}And then added: "You often go up to the wood of an evening after pigeons.
10102{_}2002{_}It's fortunate you were not there that evening, eh?"
10102{_}2003{_}He glanced at me quickly with his brows slightly contracted, as though he did not exactly comprehend me.
10102{_}2004{_}In an instant I saw that my remark had caused him quick apprehension.
10102{_}2005{_}"Yes," he answered with a sickly smile which he intended should convey to me utter unconcern.
10102{_}2006{_}"They might have suspected me."
10102{_}2007{_}"It certainly is a disagreeable affair to happen on one's property."
10102{_}2008{_}I said, still watching him narrowly.
10102{_}2009{_}And then Muriel at his side managed with her feminine ingenuity to divert the conversation into a different channel.
10102{_}2010{_}Next day I accompanied the party over to Glenlea, about five miles distant, and at noon at a spot previously arranged, we found the ladies awaiting us with luncheon spread under the trees.
10102{_}2011{_}As soon as we approached Muriel came forward quickly, handing me a telegram, saying that it had been sent over by one of my uncle's grooms at the moment they were leaving the castle.
10102{_}2012{_}I tore it open eagerly, and read its contents.
10102{_}2013{_}Then, turning to my companions, said in as quiet a voice as I could command--  "I must go up to London to-night," whereat the men, one and all, expressed hope that I should soon return.
10102{_}2014{_}Leithcourt's party were a friendly set, and at heart I was sorry to leave Scotland.
10102{_}2015{_}Yet the telegram made it imperative, for it was from Frank Hutcheson in Leghorn, and read--  _"Made inquiries.
10102{_}2016{_}Olinto Santini married your servant Armida at Italian Consulate-General in London about a year ago.
10102{_}2017{_}They live 64B, Albany Road, Camberwell: he is employed waiter Ferrari's Restaurant, Westbourne Grove.--British Consulate, Leghorn"_  The lunch was a merry one, as shooting luncheons usually are, and while we ate the keepers packed our morning bag--a considerable one--into the Perth-cart in waiting.
10102{_}2018{_}Then, when we could wander away alone together, I explained to Muriel that the reason of my sudden journey to London was in order to continue my investigations regarding the mysterious affair.
10102{_}2019{_}This puzzled her, for I had not, of course, revealed to her that I had identified Olinto.
10102{_}2020{_}Yet I managed to make such excuses and promises to return that I think allayed all her suspicions, and that night, after calling upon the detective Mackenzie, I took the sleeping-car express to Euston.
10102{_}2021{_}The restaurant which Hutcheson had indicated was, I found, situated about half-way up Westbourne Grove, nearly opposite Whiteley's, a small place where confectionery and sweets were displayed in the window, together with long-necked flasks of Italian chianti, chump-chops, small joints and tomatoes.
10102{_}2022{_}It was soon after nine o'clock when I entered the long shop with its rows of marble-topped tables and greasy lounges of red plush.
10102{_}2023{_}An unhealthy-looking lad was sweeping out the place with wet saw-dust, and a big, dark-bearded, flabby-faced man in shirt-sleeves stood behind the small counter polishing some forks.
10102{_}2024{_}"I wish to see Signor Ferrari," I said, addressing him.
10102{_}2025{_}"There is no Ferrari, he is dead," responded the man in broken English.
10102{_}2026{_}"My name is Odinzoff.
10102{_}2027{_}I bought the place from madame."
10102{_}2028{_}"You are Russian, I presume?"
10102{_}2029{_}"Polish, m'sieur--from Varsovie."
10102{_}2030{_}I had seen from the first moment we had met that he was no Italian.
10102{_}2031{_}He was too bulky, and his face too broad and flat.
10102{_}2032{_}"I have come to inquire after a waiter you have in your service, an Italian named Santini.
10102{_}2033{_}He was my servant for some years, and I naturally take an interest in him."
10102{_}2034{_}"Santini?"
10102{_}2035{_}he repeated.
10102{_}2036{_}"Oh I you mean Olinto?
10102{_}2037{_}He is not here yet.
10102{_}2038{_}He comes at ten o'clock."
10102{_}2039{_}This reply surprised me.
10102{_}2040{_}I had expected the restaurant-keeper to express regret at his disappearance, yet he spoke as though he had been at work as usual on the previous day.
10102{_}2041{_}"May I have a liqueur brandy?"
10102{_}2042{_}I asked, seeing that I would be compelled to take something.
10102{_}2043{_}"Perhaps you will have one with me?"
10102{_}2044{_}"Ach no!
10102{_}2045{_}But a kuemmel--yes, I will have a kuemmel!"
10102{_}2046{_}And he filled our glasses, and tossed off his own at a single gulp, smacking his lips after it, for the average Russian dearly loves his national decoction of caraway seeds.
10102{_}2047{_}"You find Olinto a good servant, I suppose?"
10102{_}2048{_}I said, for want of something else to say.
10102{_}2049{_}"Excellent.
10102{_}2050{_}The Italians are the best waiters in the world.
10102{_}2051{_}I am Russian, but dare not employ a Russian waiter.
10102{_}2052{_}These English would not come to my shop if I did."
10102{_}2053{_}I looked around, and it struck me that the trade of the place mainly consisted in chops and steaks for chance customers at mid-day, and tea and cake for those swarms of women who each afternoon buzz around that long line of windows of the "world's provider."
10102{_}2054{_}I could see that his was a cheap trade, as revealed by the printed notice stuck upon one of the long fly-blown mirrors: "Ices _4d_ and _6d_."
10102{_}2055{_}"How long has Olinto been with you?"
10102{_}2056{_}I inquired.
10102{_}2057{_}"About a year--perhaps a little more.
10102{_}2058{_}I trust him implicitly, and I leave him in charge when I go away for holidays.
10102{_}2059{_}He does not get along very well with the cook--who is Milanese.
10102{_}2060{_}These Italians from different provinces always quarrel," he added, laughing.
10102{_}2061{_}"If you live in Italy you know that, no doubt."
10102{_}2062{_}I laughed in chorus, and then glancing at my watch, said: "I'll wait for him, if he will be here at ten.
10102{_}2063{_}I'd much like to see him again."
10102{_}2064{_}The Russian was by no means nonplused, but merely remarked--  "He is late sometimes, but not often.
10102{_}2065{_}He lives on the other side of London--over at Camberwell."
10102{_}2066{_}His confidence that the waiter would return struck me as extremely curious; nevertheless I possessed myself in patience, strolled up and down the restaurant, and then stood watching the traffic in the Grove outside.
10102{_}2067{_}The man Odinzoff seemed a quick, hard-working fellow with a keen eye to business, for he fell to polishing the top of the marble tables with a pail and brush, at the same time directing the work of the pallid-looking youth.
10102{_}2068{_}Suddenly a side door opened, and the cook put his head in to speak with his master in French.
10102{_}2069{_}He was a typical Italian, about forty, with dark mustaches turned upwards, and an easy-going, careless manner.
10102{_}2070{_}Seeing me, however, and believing me to be a customer, he turned and closed the door quickly.
10102{_}2071{_}In that instant I noticed the high broadness of his shoulders, and his back struck me as strangely similar to that of the man in brown whom we had seen disappearing in Rannoch Wood.
10102{_}2072{_}The suspicion held me breathless.
10102{_}2073{_}Was this Russian endeavoring to deceive me when he declared that Olinto would arrive in a few minutes?
10102{_}2074{_}It seemed curious, for the man now dead must, I reflected, have been away at least four days.
10102{_}2075{_}Surely his absence from work had caused the proprietor considerable inconvenience?
10102{_}2076{_}"That was your cook, wasn't it?
10102{_}2077{_}The Milanese who is quarrelsome?"
10102{_}2078{_}I laughed, when the side door had closed.
10102{_}2079{_}"Yes, m'sieur.
10102{_}2080{_}But Emilio is a very good workman--and very honest, even though I had constantly to complain that he uses too much oil in his cooking.
10102{_}2081{_}These English do not like the oil."
10102{_}2082{_}I stood in the doorway again watching the busy throng passing outside towards Royal Oak.
10102{_}2083{_}Ten o'clock struck from a neighboring church, and I still waited, knowing only too well that I waited in vain for a man whose body had already been committed to the grave outside that far-away old Scotch town.
10102{_}2084{_}But I waited in order to ascertain the motive of the bearded Russian in leading me to believe that the young fellow would really return.
10102{_}2085{_}Presently Odinzoff went outside, carrying with him two boards upon which the menu of the "Eight-penny Luncheon!
10102{_}2086{_}This Day!"
10102{_}2087{_}was written in scrawly characters, and proceeded to affix them to the shop-front.
10102{_}2088{_}This was my opportunity, and quick as thought I moved towards where the unhealthy youth was at work, and whispered:  "I'll give you half-a-sovereign if you'll answer my questions truthfully.
10102{_}2089{_}Now, tell me, was the cook, the man I've just seen, here yesterday?"
10102{_}2090{_}"Yes, sir."
10102{_}2091{_}"Was he here the day before?"
10102{_}2092{_}"No, sir.
10102{_}2093{_}He's been away ill for four days."
10102{_}2094{_}"And your master?"
10102{_}2095{_}"He's been away too, sir."
10102{_}2096{_}I had no time to put any further question, for the Russian re-entered at that moment, and the youth busied himself rubbing the front of the counter in pretense that I had not spoken to him.
10102{_}2097{_}Indeed, I had some difficulty in slipping the promised coin into his hand at a moment when his master was not looking.
10102{_}2098{_}Then I paced up and down the restaurant, waiting patiently and wondering whether the absence of Emilio had any connection with the tragedy up in Rannoch Wood.
10102{_}2099{_}While I stood there a rather thin, respectably-dressed man entered, and seating himself upon one of the plush lounges at the further end, removed his bowler hat and ordered from the proprietor a chop and a pot of tea.
10102{_}2100{_}Then, taking a newspaper from his pocket, he settled himself to read, apparently oblivious to his surroundings.
10102{_}2101{_}And yet as I watched I saw that over the top of his paper he was carefully taking in the general appearance of the place, and his eyes were keenly following the Russian's movements.
10102{_}2102{_}The latter shouted--in French--the order for the chop through the speaking-tube to the man Emilio, and then returning to his customer he spread out a napkin and placed a small cruet, with knife, fork, and bread before him.
10102{_}2103{_}But the customer seemed immersed in his paper, and never looked up until after the Russian's back was turned.
10102{_}2104{_}Then so deep was his interest in the place, and so keen those dark eyes of his, that the truth suddenly dawned upon me.
10102{_}2105{_}Mackenzie had telegraphed to Scotland Yard, and the customer sitting there was a detective who had come to investigate.
10102{_}2106{_}I had advanced to the counter to chat again with the proprietor, when a quick step behind me caused me to turn.
10102{_}2107{_}Before me stood the slim figure of a man in a straw hat and rather seedy black jacket.
10102{_}2108{_}"_Dio Signor Padrone!_" he cried.
10102{_}2109{_}I staggered as though I had received a blow.
10102{_}2110{_}Olinto Santini in the flesh, smiling and well, stood there before me!
10102{_}2111{_}CHAPTER VIII  LIFE'S COUNTER-CLAIM   No words of mine can express my absolute and abject amazement when I faced the man, whom I had seen lying cold and dead upon that gray stone slab in the mortuary at Dumfries.
10102{_}2112{_}My eye caught the customer who, on the entry of Olinto, had dropped his paper and sat staring at him in wonderment.
10102{_}2113{_}The detective had evidently been furnished with a photograph of the dead man, and now, like myself, discovered him alive and living.
10102{_}2114{_}"Signor Padrone!"
10102{_}2115{_}cried the man whose appearance was so absolutely bewildering.
10102{_}2116{_}"How did you find me here?
10102{_}2117{_}I admit that I deceived you when I told you I worked at the Milano," he went on rapidly in Italian.
10102{_}2118{_}"But it was under compulsion--my actions that night were not my own--but those of others."
10102{_}2119{_}"Yes, I understand," I said.
10102{_}2120{_}"But come out into the street.
10102{_}2121{_}I don't wish to speak before these people.
10102{_}2122{_}Your padrone knows Italian, no doubt."
10102{_}2123{_}"Ah!
10102{_}2124{_}only a very little," he answered, smiling.
10102{_}2125{_}"Have no fear of him."
10102{_}2126{_}"But there is Emilio, the cook?"
10102{_}2127{_}"Then you have met him!"
10102{_}2128{_}he exclaimed quickly, with a strange look of apprehension.
10102{_}2129{_}"He is an undesirable person, signore."
10102{_}2130{_}"So I gather," I answered.
10102{_}2131{_}"But I desire to speak to you outside--not here."
10102{_}2132{_}And then turning with a smile to the Pole, I apologized for taking away his servant for a few minutes.
10102{_}2133{_}"Recollect, I am his old master, I added."
10102{_}2134{_}"Of course, m'sieur," answered the Pole, bowing politely.
10102{_}2135{_}"Speak with him where and how long you will.
10102{_}2136{_}He is entirely at your service."
10102{_}2137{_}And when we were outside in Westbourne Grove, Olinto walking by my side in wonderment, I asked suddenly:  "Tell me.
10102{_}2138{_}Have you ever been in Scotland--at Dumfries?"
10102{_}2139{_}"Never, signore, in my life.
10102{_}2140{_}Why?"
10102{_}2141{_}"Answer me another question," I said quickly.
10102{_}2142{_}"You married Armida at the Italian Consulate.
10102{_}2143{_}Where is she now--where is she this morning?"
10102{_}2144{_}He turned pale, and I saw a complete change in his countenance.
10102{_}2145{_}"Ah, signore!"
10102{_}2146{_}he responded, "I only wish I could tell."
10102{_}2147{_}"It is untrue that she is an invalid," I went on, "or that you live in Lambeth.
10102{_}2148{_}Your address is in Albany Road, Camberwell.
10102{_}2149{_}You can't deny these facts."
10102{_}2150{_}"I do not deny them, Signor Commendatore.
10102{_}2151{_}But how did you learn this?"
10102{_}2152{_}"The authorities in Italy know everything," I answered.
10102{_}2153{_}"Like that of all your countrymen, your record is written down at the Commune."
10102{_}2154{_}"It is a clean one, at any rate, signore," he declared with some slight warmth.
10102{_}2155{_}"I have a permesso to carry a revolver, which is in itself sufficient proof that I am a man of spotless character."
10102{_}2156{_}"I cast no reflection whatever upon you, Olinto," I answered.
10102{_}2157{_}"I have merely inquired after your wife, and you do not give me a direct reply."
10102{_}2158{_}We had walked to the Royal Oak, and stood talking on the curb outside.
10102{_}2159{_}"I give you no reply, because I can't," he said in Italian.
10102{_}2160{_}"Armida--my poor Armida--has left home."
10102{_}2161{_}"Why did you tell me such a tale of distress regarding her?"
10102{_}2162{_}"As I have already explained, signore, I was not then master of my own actions.
10102{_}2163{_}I was ruled by others.
10102{_}2164{_}But I saved your life at risk of my own.
10102{_}2165{_}Some day, when it is safe, I will reveal to you everything."
10102{_}2166{_}"Let us allow the past to remain," I said.
10102{_}2167{_}"Where is your wife now?"
10102{_}2168{_}He hesitated a moment, looking straight into my face.
10102{_}2169{_}"Well, Signor Commendatore, to tell the truth, she has disappeared."
10102{_}2170{_}"Disappeared!"
10102{_}2171{_}I echoed.
10102{_}2172{_}"And have you not made any report to the police?"
10102{_}2173{_}"No."
10102{_}2174{_}"Why not?"
10102{_}2175{_}"For reasons known only to myself I did not wish the police to pry into my private affairs."
10102{_}2176{_}"I know.
10102{_}2177{_}Because you were once convicted at Lucca of using a knife--eh?
10102{_}2178{_}I recollect quite well that affair--a love affair, was it not?"
10102{_}2179{_}"Yes, Signor Commendatore.
10102{_}2180{_}But I was a youth then--a mere boy."
10102{_}2181{_}"Then tell me the circumstances In which Armida has disappeared," I urged, for I saw quite plainly that his sudden meeting with me had upset him, and that he was trying to hold back from me some story which he was bursting to tell.
10102{_}2182{_}"Well, signore," he said at last in a low tone of confidence, "I don't like to trouble you with my private affairs after those untruths I told you when we last met."
10102{_}2183{_}"Go on," I said.
10102{_}2184{_}"Tell me the truth."
10102{_}2185{_}After the exciting incidents of our last meeting, I was half inclined to doubt him.
10102{_}2186{_}"The truth is, Signor Commendatore, that my wife has mysteriously disappeared.
10102{_}2187{_}Last Saturday, at eleven o'clock, she was talking over the garden wall with a neighbor and was then dressed to go out.
10102{_}2188{_}She apparently went out, but from that moment no one has seen or heard of her."
10102{_}2189{_}It was on the tip of my tongue to tell him the ghastly truth, yet so strange was the circumstance that his own double, even to the mole upon his face, should be lying dead and buried in Scotland that I hesitated to relate what I knew.
10102{_}2190{_}"She spoke English, I suppose?"
10102{_}2191{_}"She could make herself understood very well," he said with a sigh, and I saw a heavy, thoughtful look upon his brow.
10102{_}2192{_}That he was really devoted to her, I knew.
10102{_}2193{_}With the Italian of whatever station in life, love is all-consuming--it is either perfect love or genuine hatred.
10102{_}2194{_}The Tuscan character is one of two extremes.
10102{_}2195{_}I glanced across the road, and saw that the detective who had ordered his chop and coffee had stopped to light his pipe and was watching us.
10102{_}2196{_}"Have you any idea where your wife is, or what has induced her to go away from home?
10102{_}2197{_}Perhaps you had some words!"
10102{_}2198{_}"Words, signore!"
10102{_}2199{_}he echoed.
10102{_}2200{_}"Why, we were the happiest pair in all London.
10102{_}2201{_}No unkind word ever passed between us.
10102{_}2202{_}There seems absolutely no reason whatever why she should go away without wishing me a word of farewell."
10102{_}2203{_}"But why haven't you told the police?"
10102{_}2204{_}"For reasons that I have already stated.
10102{_}2205{_}I prefer to make inquiries for myself."
10102{_}2206{_}"And in what have your inquiries resulted?"
10102{_}2207{_}"Nothing--absolutely nothing," he said gravely.
10102{_}2208{_}"You do not suspect any plot?
10102{_}2209{_}I recollect that night in Lambeth you told me that you had enemies?"
10102{_}2210{_}"Ah!
10102{_}2211{_}so I have, signore--and so have you!"
10102{_}2212{_}he exclaimed hoarsely.
10102{_}2213{_}"Yes, my poor Armida may have been entrapped by them."
10102{_}2214{_}"And if entrapped, what then?"
10102{_}2215{_}"Then they would kill her with as little compunction as they would a fly," he said.
10102{_}2216{_}"Ah!
10102{_}2217{_}you do not know the callousness of those people.
10102{_}2218{_}I only hope and pray that she may have escaped and is in hiding somewhere, and will arrive unexpectedly and give me a startling surprise.
10102{_}2219{_}She delights in startling me," he added with a laugh.
10102{_}2220{_}Poor fellow, I thought, she would never again be able to startle him.
10102{_}2221{_}She had actually fallen a victim just as he dreaded.
10102{_}2222{_}"Then you think she must have been called away from home by some urgent message?"
10102{_}2223{_}I suggested.
10102{_}2224{_}"By the manner in which she left things, it seemed as though she went away hurriedly.
10102{_}2225{_}There were five sovereigns in a drawer that we had saved for the rent, and she took them with her."
10102{_}2226{_}I paused again, hesitating whether to tell him the terrible truth.
10102{_}2227{_}I recollected that the body had disappeared, therefore what proof had I of my allegation that she had been murdered?
10102{_}2228{_}"Tell me, Olinto," I said as we moved forward again in the direction of Paddington Station, "have you any knowledge of a man named Leithcourt?"
10102{_}2229{_}He started suddenly and looked at me.
10102{_}2230{_}"I have heard of him," he answered very lamely.
10102{_}2231{_}"And of his daughter--Muriel?"
10102{_}2232{_}"And also of her.
10102{_}2233{_}But I am not acquainted with them--nor, to tell the truth, do I wish to be."
10102{_}2234{_}"Why?"
10102{_}2235{_}"Because they are enemies of mine--bitter enemies."
10102{_}2236{_}His declaration was strange, for it threw some light upon the tragedy in Rannoch Wood.
10102{_}2237{_}"And of your wife also?"
10102{_}2238{_}"I do not know that," he responded.
10102{_}2239{_}"My enemies are my wife's also, I suppose."
10102{_}2240{_}"You have not told me the secret of that dastardly attempt upon me when we last met," I said in a low voice.
10102{_}2241{_}"Why not tell me the truth?
10102{_}2242{_}I surely ought to know who my enemies really are, so as to be warned against any future plot."
10102{_}2243{_}"You shall know some day, signore.
10102{_}2244{_}I dare not tell you now."
10102{_}2245{_}"You said that before," I exclaimed with dissatisfaction.
10102{_}2246{_}"If you are faithful to me, you ought at least to tell me the reason they wished to kill me in secret."
10102{_}2247{_}"Because they fear you," was his answer.
10102{_}2248{_}"Why should they fear me?"
10102{_}2249{_}But he shrugged his shoulders, and made a gesture with his hands indicative of utter ignorance.
10102{_}2250{_}"I ask you one question.
10102{_}2251{_}Answer yes or no.
10102{_}2252{_}Is the man Leithcourt my enemy?"
10102{_}2253{_}The young Italian paused, and then answered:  "He is not your friend.
10102{_}2254{_}I am quite well aware of that."
10102{_}2255{_}"And his daughter?
10102{_}2256{_}She is engaged, I hear."
10102{_}2257{_}"I think so."
10102{_}2258{_}"Where did you first meet Leithcourt?"
10102{_}2259{_}"I have known him several years.
10102{_}2260{_}When we first met he was poor."
10102{_}2261{_}"Suddenly became rich--eh?"
10102{_}2262{_}"Bought a fine house in the country; lives mostly at the Carlton when he and his wife and daughter are in London--although I believe they now have a house somewhere in the West End--and he often makes long cruises on his steam-yacht."
10102{_}2263{_}"And how did he make his money?"
10102{_}2264{_}Again Olinto elevated his shoulders, without replying.
10102{_}2265{_}If he would only betray to me the reason he had been induced to entice me to that house, I might then be able to form some conclusion regarding the tenants of Rannoch and their friends.
10102{_}2266{_}Who was the man who, having represented the man now before me, had been struck dead by an unerring hand?
10102{_}2267{_}Was it possible that Armida had been called by telegram to meet her husband, and recognizing the fraud perpetrated upon her threatened to disclose it and, for that reason, shared the same fate as the masquerader?
10102{_}2268{_}This was the first theory that occurred to me; one which I believed to be the correct one.
10102{_}2269{_}The motive was a mystery, yet the facts seemed to me plain enough.
10102{_}2270{_}As the young Italian had refused to give any satisfactory explanation, I resolved within myself to wait until the unfortunate woman's body was recovered before revealing to him the ghastly truth.
10102{_}2271{_}Without doubt he had some reason in withholding from me the true facts, either because he feared that I might become unduly alarmed, or else he himself had been deeply implicated in the plot.
10102{_}2272{_}Of the two suggestions, I was inclined to believe in the latter.
10102{_}2273{_}He walked with me as far as the end of Bishop's Road, endeavoring with all the Italian's exquisite diplomacy to obtain from me what I knew concerning the Leithcourts.
10102{_}2274{_}But I told him nothing, nor did I reveal that I had only that morning returned from Scotland.
10102{_}2275{_}Then at last we parted, and he retraced his steps to the little restaurant in Westbourne Grove, while I entered a hansom and drove to the well-known photographer's in New Bond Street, whose name had been upon the torn photograph of the young girl in the white pique blouse and her hair fastened with a bow of black ribbon, the picture that I had found on board the _Lola_ on that memorable night in the Mediterranean, and a duplicate of which I had seen in Muriel's cosy little room up at Rannoch.
10102{_}2276{_}I recollected that she had told me the name of the original was Elma Heath, and that she had been a schoolfellow of hers at Chichester.
10102{_}2277{_}Therefore I inquired of the photographer's lady-clerk whether she could supply me with a print of the negative.
10102{_}2278{_}For a considerable time she searched in her books for the name, and at last discovered it.
10102{_}2279{_}Then she said:  "I regret, sir, that we can't give you a print, for the customer purchased the negative at the time."
10102{_}2280{_}"Ah, I'm very sorry for that," I said.
10102{_}2281{_}"To what address did you send it?"
10102{_}2282{_}"The customer who ordered it was apparently a foreigner," she said, at the same time turning round the ledger so that I could read.
10102{_}2283{_}And I saw that the entry was: "Heath--Miss Elma--3 dozen cabinets and negative.
10102{_}2284{_}Address: Baron Xavier Oberg, Vosnesenski Prospect 48, St. Petersburg, Russia."
10102{_}2285{_}"Did this gentleman come with the young lady when her portrait was taken?"
10102{_}2286{_}I inquired.
10102{_}2287{_}"I can't tell, sir," she replied.
10102{_}2288{_}"I've only been here a year, and you see the date--over two years ago."
10102{_}2289{_}"The photographer would know, perhaps?"
10102{_}2290{_}"He's a new man, sir.
10102{_}2291{_}He only came a month ago.
10102{_}2292{_}In fact, the business changed hands a year ago, and none of the previous employees have remained."
10102{_}2293{_}"Ah!
10102{_}2294{_}that's unfortunate," I said, greatly disappointed; and having copied the address to which the negative and prints had been sent, I thanked her and left.
10102{_}2295{_}Who, I wondered, was this Baron Oberg, and what relation was he to Elma Heath?
10102{_}2296{_}The picture of the girl in the white blouse somehow exercised a strange attraction for me.
10102{_}2297{_}Have you never experienced the fascination of a photograph, inexplicable and yet forcible--a kind of magnetism from which you cannot release yourself?
10102{_}2298{_}Perhaps it was the curious fact that some person had taken it from its frame on board the _Lola_ and destroyed it that first aroused my interest; or it might have been the discovery of it in Muriel's room at Rannoch.
10102{_}2299{_}Anyhow, it had for me an absorbing interest, for I often wondered whether the unknown girl who had secretly gone ashore from the yacht when I had left it was not Elma Heath herself.
10102{_}2300{_}Who was this Baron Oberg?
10102{_}2301{_}The name was German undoubtedly, yet he lived in the Russian capital.
10102{_}2302{_}From London to Petersburg is a far cry, yet I resolved that if it were necessary I would travel there and investigate.
10102{_}2303{_}At the German Embassy, in Carlton House Terrace, I found my friend Captain Nieberding, the second secretary, of whom I inquired whether the name of Baron Oberg was known, but having referred to a number of German books in his Excellency's library, he returned and told me that the name did not appear in the lists of the German nobility.
10102{_}2304{_}"He may be Russian--Polish most probably," added the captain, a tall, fair fellow in gold spectacles, whom I had known when he was third secretary of Embassy at Rome.
10102{_}2305{_}His opinion was that it was not a German name, for there was a little place called Oberg, he said, on the railway between Lodz and Lowicz.
10102{_}2306{_}Then, after luncheon, I went to Albany Road, one of those dreary, old-fashioned streets that were pleasant back in the early Victorian days when Camberwell was a suburb and Walworth Common was still an open waste.
10102{_}2307{_}I found the house where Olinto lived--a small, smoke-blackened, semi-detached place standing back in a tiny strip of weedy garden, with a wooden veranda before the first floor windows.
10102{_}2308{_}The house, according to the woman who kept a general shop at the corner, was occupied by two families.
10102{_}2309{_}The "Eye-talians," as she termed them, lived above, while the Gibbonses rented the ground floor.
10102{_}2310{_}"Oh, yes, sir.
10102{_}2311{_}The foreigners are respectable enough.
10102{_}2312{_}Always pays me ready money for everythink, except the milk.
10102{_}2313{_}That they pays for weekly."
10102{_}2314{_}"I understand that the wife has disappeared.
10102{_}2315{_}What have you heard about that?"
10102{_}2316{_}"They do say, sir, that they 'ad some words together the other day, and that the woman's took herself off in a tantrum.
10102{_}2317{_}Only you can't believe all you 'ear, you know."
10102{_}2318{_}"Did they often quarrel?"
10102{_}2319{_}"Not to my knowledge, sir.
10102{_}2320{_}They were really very quiet, respectable persons for foreigners."
10102{_}2321{_}I repassed the house of the dead woman, and then regaining the busy Camberwell Road I took an omnibus back to the Hotel Cecil in the Strand where I had put up, tired and disappointed.
10102{_}2322{_}Next day I ran down to Chichester, and after some difficulty found the Cheverton College for Ladies, a big old-fashioned house about half-a-mile out of the town on the Drayton Road.
10102{_}2323{_}The seminary was evidently a first-class one, for when I entered I noticed how well everything was kept.
10102{_}2324{_}To the principal, an elderly lady of a somewhat severe aspect, I said:  "I regret, madam, to trouble you, but I am in search of information you can supply.
10102{_}2325{_}It is with regard to a certain Elma Heath whom you had as pupil here, and who left, I believe, about two years ago.
10102{_}2326{_}Her parents lived in Durham."
10102{_}2327{_}"I remember her perfectly," was the woman's response as she sat behind the big desk, having apparently at first expected that I had a daughter to put to school.
10102{_}2328{_}"Well," I said, "there has been some little friction in the family, and I am making inquiries on behalf of another branch of it--an aunt who desires to ascertain the girl's whereabouts."
10102{_}2329{_}"Ah, I regret, sir, that I cannot tell you that.
10102{_}2330{_}The Baron, her uncle, came here one day and took her away suddenly--abroad, I think."
10102{_}2331{_}"Had she no school-friend to whom she would probably write?"
10102{_}2332{_}"There was a girl named Leithcourt--Muriel Leithcourt--who was her friend, but who has also left."
10102{_}2333{_}"And no one else?"
10102{_}2334{_}I asked.
10102{_}2335{_}"Girls often write to each other after leaving school, until they get married, and then the correspondence usually ceases."
10102{_}2336{_}The principal was silent and reflective.
10102{_}2337{_}"Well," she said at last, "there was another pupil who was also on friendly terms with Elma--a girl named Lydia Moreton.
10102{_}2338{_}She may have written to her.
10102{_}2339{_}If you really desire to know, sir, I dare say I could find her address.
10102{_}2340{_}She left us about nine months after Elma."
10102{_}2341{_}"I should esteem it a great favor if you would give me that young lady's address," I said, whereupon she unlocked a drawer in her writing-table and took therefrom a thick, leather-bound book which she consulted for a few minutes, at last exclaiming:  "Yes, here it is--'Lydia Moreton, daughter of Sir Hamilton Moreton, K.C.M.G., Whiston Grange, Doncaster.'"
10102{_}2342{_}And she scribbled it in pencil upon an envelope, and handing it to me, said:  "Elma Heath was, I fear, somewhat neglected by her parents.
10102{_}2343{_}She remained here for five years, and had no holidays like the other girls.
10102{_}2344{_}Her uncle, the Baron, came to see her several times, but on each occasion after he had left I found her crying in secret.
10102{_}2345{_}He was mean and unkind to her.
10102{_}2346{_}Now that I recollect, I remember that Lydia had said she had received a letter from her, therefore she might be able to give you some information."
10102{_}2347{_}And with that I took my leave, thanking her, and returned to London.
10102{_}2348{_}Could Lydia Moreton furnish any information?
10102{_}2349{_}If so, I might find this girl whose photograph had aroused the irate jealousy of the mysterious unknown.
10102{_}2350{_}The ten o'clock Edinburgh express from King's Cross next morning took me up to Doncaster, and hiring a musty old fly at the station, I drove three miles out of the town on the Rotherham Road, finding Whiston Grange to be a fine old Elizabethan mansion in the center of a great park, with tall old twisted chimneys, and beautifully-kept gardens.
10102{_}2351{_}When I descended at the door and rang, the footman was not aware whether Miss Lydia was in.
10102{_}2352{_}He looked at me somewhat suspiciously, I thought, until I gave my card and impressed upon him meaningly that I had come from London purposely to see his young mistress upon a very important matter.
10102{_}2353{_}"Tell her," I said, "that I wish to see her regarding her friend, Miss Elma Heath."
10102{_}2354{_}"Miss Elma 'Eath," repeated the man.
10102{_}2355{_}"Very well, sir.
10102{_}2356{_}Will you walk this way?"
10102{_}2357{_}And then I followed him across the big old oak-paneled hall, filled with trophies of the chase and arms of the civil wars, into a small paneled room on the left, the deep-set window with its diamond panes giving out upon the old bowling-green and the flower-garden beyond.
10102{_}2358{_}Presently the door opened, and a tall dark-haired girl in white entered with an enquiring expression upon her face as she halted and bowed to me.
10102{_}2359{_}"Miss Lydia Moreton, I believe?"
10102{_}2360{_}I commenced, and as she replied in the affirmative I went on: "I have first to apologize for coming to you, but Miss Sotheby, the principal of the school at Chichester, referred me to you for information as to the present whereabouts of Miss Elma Heath, who, I believe, was one of your most intimate friends at school."
10102{_}2361{_}And I added a lie, saying: "I am trying, on behalf of an aunt of hers, to discover her."
10102{_}2362{_}"Well," responded the girl, "I have had only one or two letters.
10102{_}2363{_}She's in her uncle's hands, I believe, and he won't let her write, poor girl.
10102{_}2364{_}She dreaded leaving us."
10102{_}2365{_}"Why?"
10102{_}2366{_}"Ah!
10102{_}2367{_}she would never say.
10102{_}2368{_}She had some deep-rooted terror of her uncle, Baron Oberg, who lived in St. Petersburg, and who came over at long intervals to see her.
10102{_}2369{_}But possibly you know the whole story?"
10102{_}2370{_}"I know nothing," I cried eagerly.
10102{_}2371{_}"You will be furthering her interests, as well as doing me a great personal favor, if you will tell me what you know."
