10102{_}4696{_}"I haven't exactly deserted it," I said.
10102{_}4697{_}"But I really don't love it like he does."
10102{_}4698{_}"No.
10102{_}4699{_}A year or two of the Mediterranean blue is quite sufficient to last any fellow his lifetime.
10102{_}4700{_}I shouldn't live in Leghorn if I had my choice.
10102{_}4701{_}I'd prefer somewhere up in the mountains, beyond Pisa, or outside Florence, where you can have a good time in winter."
10102{_}4702{_}Then a silence fell between us, and I sat eating on until the end of the meal, wondering how to broach the question I so desired to put to him.
10102{_}4703{_}"I shall try if I can get on recruiting service at home for a bit," he said presently.
10102{_}4704{_}"There's an appointment up in Glasgow vacant, and I shall try for it.
10102{_}4705{_}It'll be better, at any rate, than China or the Pacific."
10102{_}4706{_}I was just about to turn the conversation to the visit of the mysterious _Lola_ to Leghorn, when two men he knew entered the dining-room, and, recognizing him, came across to give him a welcome home.
10102{_}4707{_}One of the newcomers was Major Bartlett, whom I at once recollected as having been a guest of Leithcourt's up at Rannoch, and the other a younger man whom Durnford introduced to me as Captain Hanbury.
10102{_}4708{_}"Oh, Major!"
10102{_}4709{_}I cried, rising and grasping his hand.
10102{_}4710{_}"I haven't seen you since Scotland, and the extraordinary ending to your house-party."
10102{_}4711{_}"No," he laughed.
10102{_}4712{_}"It was an amazing affair, wasn't it?
10102{_}4713{_}After the Leithcourts left it was like pandemonium let loose; the guests collared everything they could lay their hands upon!
10102{_}4714{_}It's a wonder to me the disgraceful affair didn't get into the papers."
10102{_}4715{_}"But where's Leithcourt now?"
10102{_}4716{_}I asked anxiously.
10102{_}4717{_}"Haven't the ghost of an idea," replied the Major, standing astride with his hands in his pockets.
10102{_}4718{_}"Young Paget of ours told me the other day that he saw Muriel driving in the Terminus Road at Eastbourne, but she didn't notice him.
10102{_}4719{_}They were a queerish lot, those Leithcourts," he added.
10102{_}4720{_}"Hulloa!
10102{_}4721{_}What are you saying about the Leithcourts, Charley?"
10102{_}4722{_}exclaimed Durnford, turning quickly from Hanbury.
10102{_}4723{_}"I know some people of that name--Philip Leithcourt, who has a daughter named Muriel."
10102{_}4724{_}"Well, they sound much the same.
10102{_}4725{_}But if you know them, my dear old chap, I really don't envy you your friends," declared the Major with a laugh.
10102{_}4726{_}"Why not?"
10102{_}4727{_}"Well, Gregg will tell you," he said.
10102{_}4728{_}"He knows, perhaps, more than I do.
10102{_}4729{_}But," he added, "they may not, of course, be the same people."
10102{_}4730{_}"I first met them yachting over at Algiers," Jack said.
10102{_}4731{_}"And then again at Malta, where they seemed to have quite a lot of friends.
10102{_}4732{_}They had a steam-yacht, the _Iris_, and were often up and down the Mediterranean."
10102{_}4733{_}"Must be the same people," declared the Major.
10102{_}4734{_}"Leithcourt spoke once or twice of his yacht, but we all put it down as a non-existent vessel, because he was always drawing the long bow about his adventures."
10102{_}4735{_}"And how did you first come to know him?"
10102{_}4736{_}I asked of the Major eagerly.
10102{_}4737{_}"Oh, I don't know.
10102{_}4738{_}Somebody brought him to mess, and we struck up an acquaintance across the table.
10102{_}4739{_}He seemed a good chap, and when he asked me to shoot I accepted.
10102{_}4740{_}On arrival up at Rannoch, however, one thing struck me as jolly strange, and that was that among the people I was asked to meet was one of the very worst blacklegs about town.
10102{_}4741{_}He called himself Martin Woodroffe up there--although I'd known him at the old Corinthian Club as Dick Archer.
10102{_}4742{_}He was believed then to be one of a clever gang of international thieves."
10102{_}4743{_}"When I first met him he gave me the name of Hornby," I said.
10102{_}4744{_}"It was in Leghorn, where he was on board a yacht called the _Lola_, of which he represented himself as owner."
10102{_}4745{_}"He left Rannoch very suddenly," remarked Bartlett.
10102{_}4746{_}"We understood that he was engaged to marry Muriel.
10102{_}4747{_}If so, I'm sorry for her, poor girl."
10102{_}4748{_}"What!"
10102{_}4749{_}cried Durnford, starting up.
10102{_}4750{_}"That man to marry Muriel Leithcourt?"
10102{_}4751{_}"Yes," I said.
10102{_}4752{_}"Why?"
10102{_}4753{_}But his countenance had turned pale, and he gave no answer to my question.
10102{_}4754{_}"If these same Leithcourts are really friends of yours, Durnford, old fellow, I'm sorry I've said anything against them," the Major exclaimed in an apologetic tone.
10102{_}4755{_}"Only the end of my visit was so abrupt and so extraordinary, and the company such a mixed one, that--well, to tell you the truth, the people are a mysterious lot altogether."
10102{_}4756{_}"Perhaps our Leithcourts are not the same as those Jack knows," I remarked, in order to escape from a rather difficult situation; whereupon Durnford, as though eager to conceal his surprise, said with a forced laugh, "Oh!
10102{_}4757{_}probably not," and reseated himself at table.
10102{_}4758{_}Then the Major quickly changed the topic of conversation, and afterwards he and his friend passed along to their table and sat down to eat.
10102{_}4759{_}I could not help noticing that Jack Durnford was upset at what he had learnt, yet I hesitated just then to put any question to him.
10102{_}4760{_}I resolved to approach the subject later, so as to allow him time to question me if he wished to do so.
10102{_}4761{_}After smoking an hour we went across to the Empire, where we spent the evening in the grand circle, meeting many men we knew and having a rather pleasant time among old acquaintances.
10102{_}4762{_}If a man who had lived the club life of London returns from abroad, he can always run across someone he knows in the circle of the Empire about ten o'clock at night.
10102{_}4763{_}Jack was, however, not his old self that he had been before dinner.
10102{_}4764{_}His brow was now heavy and thoughtful, and he appeared deeply immersed in some intricate problem, for his eyes were fixed vacantly when opportunity was afforded him to think, and he appeared to desire to avoid his friends rather than to greet them.
10102{_}4765{_}After the theater I induced him to come round to the Cecil, and in the wicker chair in the big portico before the entrance we sat to smoke our final cigars.
10102{_}4766{_}It is a favorite spot of mine when in London, for at afternoon, when the string band plays and the Americans and other cosmopolitans drink tea, there is a continual coming and going, a little panorama of life that to a student of men like myself is intensely interesting.
10102{_}4767{_}And at night it is just as amusing to sit there in the shadow and watch the people returning from the theaters or dances and to speculate as to whom and what they are.
10102{_}4768{_}At that one little corner of London just off the Strand you see more variety of men and women than perhaps at any other spot.
10102{_}4769{_}All grades pass before you, from the pushful American commercial man interested in a patent medicine, to the proud Indian Rajah with his turbaned suite; from the variety actress to the daughter of a peer, or the wife of a millionaire pork-butcher doing Europe.
10102{_}4770{_}"You've been a bit down in the mouth to-night, Jack," I said presently, after we had been watching the cabs coming up, depositing the home-coming revelers from the Savoy or the Carlton.
10102{_}4771{_}"Yes," he sighed.
10102{_}4772{_}"And surely I have enough to cause me--after what I've heard from Bartlett."
10102{_}4773{_}"What!
10102{_}4774{_}Did the facts he told us convey any bad news to you?"
10102{_}4775{_}I inquired with pretended ignorance.
10102{_}4776{_}"Yes," he said hoarsely, after a brief pause.
10102{_}4777{_}Then he added: "Bartlett said you could tell me what happened up in Scotland, where Leithcourt had shooting.
10102{_}4778{_}Tell me everything," he added with the air of a man in whom all hope is dead.
10102{_}4779{_}"Well," I began, "the Leithcourts took Rannoch Castle, close to my uncle's place, near Dumfries.
10102{_}4780{_}I got to know them, of course, and often shot with his party.
10102{_}4781{_}One day, however, I was amazed to notice in one of the rooms the photograph of a lady, the exact counterpart of that picture which, I recollect, I told you when in Leghorn I had found torn up on board the _Lola_.
10102{_}4782{_}You recollect what I narrated about my strange adventure, don't you?"
10102{_}4783{_}"I remember every word," was his answer.
10102{_}4784{_}"Go on.
10102{_}4785{_}What did you do?"
10102{_}4786{_}"Nothing.
10102{_}4787{_}I held my tongue.
10102{_}4788{_}But when I discovered that the fellow who called himself Woodroffe--the man who had represented himself as the owner of the _Lola_, and who, no doubt, had had a hand in breaking open Hutcheson's safe in the Consulate--was engaged to Muriel, I became full of suspicion."
10102{_}4789{_}"Well?"
10102{_}4790{_}"Woodroffe, after meeting me, disappeared--went to Hamburg, they said, on business.
10102{_}4791{_}Then other things occurred.
10102{_}4792{_}A man and woman were found murdered up in the wood about a mile and a half from the castle.
10102{_}4793{_}The man was made up to represent my man Olinto--I believe you've seen him in Leghorn?"
10102{_}4794{_}"What!
10102{_}4795{_}They've killed Olinto?"
10102{_}4796{_}he gasped, starting from his chair.
10102{_}4797{_}"No.
10102{_}4798{_}The fellow was made up very much like him.
10102{_}4799{_}But his wife Armida was killed."
10102{_}4800{_}"They killed the woman, and believed they had also killed her husband, eh?"
10102{_}4801{_}he said bitterly through his teeth, and I saw that his strong hands grasped the arms of his chair firmly.
10102{_}4802{_}"And Martin Woodroffe is engaged to Muriel Leithcourt.
10102{_}4803{_}Are you certain of this?"
10102{_}4804{_}"Yes; quite certain."
10102{_}4805{_}"And is there no suspicion as to who is the assassin of the woman Santini and this mysterious man who posed as her husband?"
10102{_}4806{_}"None whatever."
10102{_}4807{_}For some time Jack Durnford smoked in silence, and I could just distinguish his white, hard face in the faint light, for it was now late, and the big electric lamps had been turned out and we were in semi-darkness.
10102{_}4808{_}"That fellow shall never marry Muriel," he declared in a fierce, hoarse voice.
10102{_}4809{_}"What you have just told me reveals the truth.
10102{_}4810{_}Did you meet Chater?"
10102{_}4811{_}"He appeared suddenly at Rannoch, and the Leithcourts fled precipitately and have not since been heard of."
10102{_}4812{_}"Ah, no wonder!"
10102{_}4813{_}he remarked with a dry laugh.
10102{_}4814{_}"No wonder!
10102{_}4815{_}But look here, Gordon, I'm not going to stand by and let that scoundrel Woodroffe marry Muriel."
10102{_}4816{_}"You love her, perhaps?"
10102{_}4817{_}I hazarded.
10102{_}4818{_}"Yes, I do love her," he admitted.
10102{_}4819{_}"And, by heaven!"
10102{_}4820{_}he cried, "I will tell the truth and crush the whole of their ingenious plot.
10102{_}4821{_}Have you met Elma Heath?"
10102{_}4822{_}he asked.
10102{_}4823{_}"Yes," I said in quick anxiety.
10102{_}4824{_}"Then listen," he said in a low, earnest voice.
10102{_}4825{_}"Listen, and I'll tell you something.
10102{_}4826{_}"There is a greater mystery surrounding that yacht, the _Lola_, than you have ever imagined, my dear old chap," declared Jack Durnford, looking me straight in the face.
10102{_}4827{_}"When you told me about it on the quarter-deck that day outside Leghorn, I was half a mind to tell you what I knew.
10102{_}4828{_}Only one fact prevented me--my disinclination to reveal my own secrets.
10102{_}4829{_}I loved Muriel Leithcourt, yet, afloat as I was, I could never see her--I could not obtain from her own lips the explanation I desired.
10102{_}4830{_}Yet I would not prejudge her--no, and I won't now!"
10102{_}4831{_}he added with a fierce resolution.
10102{_}4832{_}"I love her," he went on, "and she reciprocates my love.
10102{_}4833{_}Ours is a secret engagement made in Malta two years ago, and yet you tell me that she has pledged herself to that fellow Woodroffe--the man known here in London as Dick Archer.
10102{_}4834{_}I can't believe it--I really can't, old fellow.
10102{_}4835{_}She could never write to me as she has done, urging patience and secrecy until my return."
10102{_}4836{_}"Unless, of course, she desired to gain time," I suggested.
10102{_}4837{_}But my friend was silent; his brows were deep knit.
10102{_}4838{_}"Woodroffe is at the present moment in Petersburg," I said.
10102{_}4839{_}"I've just come back from there."
10102{_}4840{_}"In St.
10102{_}4841{_}Petersburg!"
10102{_}4842{_}he gasped, surprised.
10102{_}4843{_}"Then he is with that villainous official, Baron Oberg, the Governor-General of Finland."
10102{_}4844{_}"No; Oberg is living shut up in his palace at Helsingfors, fearing to go out lest he shall be assassinated," was my answer.
10102{_}4845{_}"And Elma?
10102{_}4846{_}What has become of her?"
10102{_}4847{_}"She is in hiding in Petersburg, awaiting such time as I can get her safely out of Russia," and then, continuing, I explained how she had been maimed and rendered deaf and dumb.
10102{_}4848{_}"What!"
10102{_}4849{_}he cried fiercely.
10102{_}4850{_}"Have they actually done that to the poor girl?
10102{_}4851{_}Then they feared that she should reveal the nature of their plot, for she had seen and heard."
10102{_}4852{_}"Seen and heard what?"
10102{_}4853{_}"Be patient; we will elucidate this mystery, and the motive of this terrible infliction upon her.
10102{_}4854{_}Muriel wrote to me saying that poor Elma, her friend, had disappeared, and she feared that some evil had also happened to her.
10102{_}4855{_}So Oberg had sent her to his fortress--his own private Bastille--the place to which, on pretended charges of conspiracy against Russia, he sends those who thwart him to a living tomb."
10102{_}4856{_}"I have seen him, and I have defied him," I said.
10102{_}4857{_}"You have!
10102{_}4858{_}Man alive!
10102{_}4859{_}be careful.
10102{_}4860{_}He's not a fellow who sticks at trifles," said Jack warningly.
10102{_}4861{_}"I don't fear," I replied.
10102{_}4862{_}"Elma's enemies are also mine."
10102{_}4863{_}"Then I take it, old fellow, that notwithstanding her affliction, you are actually in love with her?"
10102{_}4864{_}"I intend to rescue, and to marry her," I answered quite frankly.
10102{_}4865{_}"But first we must tear aside this veil of mystery and ascertain all the facts concerning her," he said.
10102{_}4866{_}"At present I only know one or two very vague details.
10102{_}4867{_}The baron is certainly not her uncle, as he represents himself to be, but it seems certain that she is the daughter of Anglo-Russian parents, and was born in Russia and brought to England when a child."
10102{_}4868{_}"But from whom do you expect I can obtain the true facts concerning her, and the reason of the baron's desire to keep her silent?"
10102{_}4869{_}"Ah!"
10102{_}4870{_}he said, twisting his mustache thoughtfully.
10102{_}4871{_}"That's just the question.
10102{_}4872{_}For a solution of the problem we must first fathom the motive of the Leithcourts and the reason they fled in fear before that fellow Chater.
10102{_}4873{_}That Muriel is innocent of any complicity in their plot, whatever it may be, I feel convinced.
10102{_}4874{_}She may be the victim of that blackleg Woodroffe, who, as Bartlett has told you, is one of the most expert swindlers in London, and who has already done two terms of penal servitude."
10102{_}4875{_}"But what was the motive in breaking open the Consul's safe, if not to obtain the Foreign Office or Admiralty ciphers?
10102{_}4876{_}Perhaps they wanted to steal them and sell them to a foreign government?"
10102{_}4877{_}"No; that was not their object.
10102{_}4878{_}I've thought over it many, many times since you told me, and I feel convinced that Woodroffe is too shrewd a fellow not to have known that no Consul goes away on leave and allows his ciphers to remain behind.
10102{_}4879{_}When he leaves his post he always deposits those precious books either at the Foreign Office here or with his Consul-General, or with a Consul at another port.
10102{_}4880{_}They'd surely ascertain all that before they made the raid, you bet.
10102{_}4881{_}The affair was a risky one, and Dick Archer is known as a man of many precautions."
10102{_}4882{_}"But he is on extremely friendly terms with Elma.
10102{_}4883{_}It was he who succeeded in finding her in Finland, and taking her beyond Oberg's sphere of influence to Petersburg."
10102{_}4884{_}"Then it is certainly only an affected friendship, with some sinister motive underlying it."
10102{_}4885{_}"She wrote a letter from her island prison to an old schoolfellow named Lydia Moreton, asking her to see Woodroffe at his rooms in Cork Street, and tell him that through all she was suffering she had kept her promise to him, and that the secret was still safe."
10102{_}4886{_}"Exactly.
10102{_}4887{_}And now the fellow fears that as you are so actively searching out the truth, she may yield to your demands and explain.
10102{_}4888{_}He therefore intends to silence her."
10102{_}4889{_}"What!
10102{_}4890{_}to kill her, you mean?"
10102{_}4891{_}I gasped, in quick apprehension.
10102{_}4892{_}"Well, he might do so, in order to save himself, you see," Jack replied, adding: "He certainly would have no compunction if he thought that it would not be brought home to him.
10102{_}4893{_}Only he, no doubt, fears you, because you have found her, and are in love with her."
10102{_}4894{_}I admitted the force of his argument, but recollected that my dear one was safe in concealment, and that the Princess was our friend, even though I, as an Englishman, had no sympathy with the doctrine of the bomb and the knife.
10102{_}4895{_}I tried to get from him all that he knew concerning Elma, but he seemed, for some curious reason, disinclined to tell.
10102{_}4896{_}All I could gather was that Leithcourt was in league with Chater and Woodroffe, and that Muriel had acted as an entirely innocent agent.
10102{_}4897{_}What the conspiracy was, or what was its motive, I could not discern.
10102{_}4898{_}I was as far off the solution of the problem as ever.
10102{_}4899{_}"We must first find Muriel," he declared, when I pressed him to tell me everything he knew.
10102{_}4900{_}"There are facts you have told me which negative my own theories, and only from her can we obtain the real truth."
10102{_}4901{_}"But surely you know where she is?
10102{_}4902{_}She writes to you," I said.
10102{_}4903{_}"The last letter, which I received at Gib.
10102{_}4904{_}ten days ago, was from the Hotel Bristol, at Botzen, in the Tyrol, yet Bartlett says she has been seen down at Eastbourne."
10102{_}4905{_}"But you have an address where you always write to her, I suppose?"
10102{_}4906{_}"Yes, a secret one.
10102{_}4907{_}I have written and made an appointment, but she has not kept it.
10102{_}4908{_}She has been prevented, of course.
10102{_}4909{_}She may be with her parents, and unable to come to London."
10102{_}4910{_}"You did not know that they had fled, and were in hiding?"
10102{_}4911{_}"Of course not.
10102{_}4912{_}What I've heard to-night is news to me--amazing news."
10102{_}4913{_}"And does it not convey to you the truth?"
10102{_}4914{_}"It does--a ghastly truth concerning Elma Heath," he answered in a low voice, as though speaking to himself.
10102{_}4915{_}"Tell me.
10102{_}4916{_}What?
10102{_}4917{_}I'm dying, Jack, to know everything concerning her.
10102{_}4918{_}Who is that fellow Oberg?"
10102{_}4919{_}"Her enemy.
10102{_}4920{_}She, by mere accident, learned his secret and Woodroffe's, and they now both live in deadly fear of her."
10102{_}4921{_}"And for that reason she was taken to Siena, where some villainous Italian doctor was bribed to render her deaf and dumb."
10102{_}4922{_}He nodded in the affirmative.
10102{_}4923{_}"But Chater?"
10102{_}4924{_}"I know very little concerning him.
10102{_}4925{_}He may have conspired with them, or he may be innocent.
10102{_}4926{_}It seems as though he were antagonistic to their schemes, if Leithcourt and his family really fled from him."
10102{_}4927{_}"And yet he was on board the _Lola_.
10102{_}4928{_}Indeed, he may have helped to commit the burglary at the Consulate," I said.
10102{_}4929{_}"Quite likely," he answered.
10102{_}4930{_}"But our first object must be to rediscover Muriel.
10102{_}4931{_}Paget says she is in Eastbourne.
10102{_}4932{_}If she is there, we shall easily find her.
10102{_}4933{_}They publish visitors' lists in the papers, don't they, like they do at Hastings?"
10102{_}4934{_}Then he added: "Visitors' lists are most annoying when you find your name printed in them when you are supposed officially to be somewhere else.
10102{_}4935{_}I was had once like that by the Bournemouth papers, when I was supposed to be on duty over at Queenstown.
10102{_}4936{_}I narrowly escaped a terrible wigging."
10102{_}4937{_}"Shall we go to Eastbourne?"
10102{_}4938{_}I suggested eagerly.
10102{_}4939{_}"I'll go there with you in the morning."
10102{_}4940{_}"Or would it not be best to send an urgent wire to the address where I always write?
10102{_}4941{_}She would then reply here, no doubt.
10102{_}4942{_}If she's in Eastbourne, there may be reasons why she cannot come up to town.
10102{_}4943{_}If her people are in hiding, of course she won't come.
10102{_}4944{_}But she'll make an appointment with me, no doubt."
10102{_}4945{_}"Very well.
10102{_}4946{_}Send a wire," I said.
10102{_}4947{_}"And make it urgent.
10102{_}4948{_}It will then be forwarded.
10102{_}4949{_}But as regards Olinto?
10102{_}4950{_}Would you like to see him?
10102{_}4951{_}He might tell you more than he has told me."
10102{_}4952{_}"No; by no means.
10102{_}4953{_}He must not know that I have returned to London," declared my friend quickly.
10102{_}4954{_}"You had better not see him--you understand."
10102{_}4955{_}"Then his interests are--well, not exactly our own?"
10102{_}4956{_}"No."
10102{_}4957{_}"But why don't you tell me more about Elma?"
10102{_}4958{_}I urged, for I was eager to learn all he knew.
10102{_}4959{_}"Come, do tell me!"
10102{_}4960{_}I implored.
10102{_}4961{_}"I've told you practically everything, my dear old fellow," was his response.
10102{_}4962{_}"The revelation of the true facts of the affair can be made only by Muriel.
10102{_}4963{_}I tell you, we must find her."
10102{_}4964{_}"Yes, we must--at all hazards," I said.
10102{_}4965{_}"Let's go across to the telegraph office opposite Charing Cross.
10102{_}4966{_}It's open always."
10102{_}4967{_}And we rose and walked out along the Strand, now nearly deserted, and despatched an urgent message to Muriel at an address in Hurlingham Road, Fulham.
10102{_}4968{_}Afterwards we stood outside on the curb, still talking, I loth to part from him, when there passed by in the shadow two men in dark overcoats, who crossed the road behind us to the front of Charing Cross station, and then continued on towards Trafalgar Square.
10102{_}4969{_}As the light of the street lamp fell upon them, I thought I recognized the face of one as that of a person I had seen before, yet I was not at all certain, and my failure to remember whom the passer-by resembled prevented me from saying anything further to Jack than:  "A fellow I know has just gone by, I think."
10102{_}4970{_}"We seem to be meeting hosts of friends to-night," he laughed.
10102{_}4971{_}"After all, old chap, it does one good to come back to our dear, dirty old town again.
10102{_}4972{_}We abuse it when we are here, and talk of the life in Paris, and Vienna, and Brussels, but when we are away there is no place on earth so dear to us, for it is 'home.'
10102{_}4973{_}But there!"
10102{_}4974{_}he laughed, "I'm actually growing romantic.
10102{_}4975{_}Ah!
10102{_}4976{_}if we could only find Muriel!
10102{_}4977{_}But we must to-morrow.
10102{_}4978{_}Ta-ta!
10102{_}4979{_}I shall go around to the club and sleep, for I haven't fixed on any diggings yet.
10102{_}4980{_}Come in at ten to-morrow, and we will decide upon some plan.
10102{_}4981{_}One thing is plainly certain; Elma must at once be got out of Russia.
10102{_}4982{_}She's in deadly peril of her life there."
10102{_}4983{_}"Yes," I said.
10102{_}4984{_}"And you will help me?"
10102{_}4985{_}"With all my heart, old fellow," answered my friend, warmly grasping my hand, and then we parted, he strolling along towards the National Gallery on his way back to the "Junior," while I returned to the _Cecil_ alone.
10102{_}4986{_}CHAPTER XVI  MARKED MEN   "Captain Durnford?"
10102{_}4987{_}I inquired of the hall-porter of the club next morning.
10102{_}4988{_}"Not here, sir."
10102{_}4989{_}"But he slept here last night," I remarked.
10102{_}4990{_}"I have an appointment with him."
10102{_}4991{_}The man consulted the big book before him, and answered:  "Captain Durnford went out at 9:27 last night, sir, but has not returned."
10102{_}4992{_}Strange, I thought, but although I waited in the club nearly an hour, he did not put in an appearance.
10102{_}4993{_}I called again at noon, and he had not come in, and again at two o'clock, but he had not even then made his appearance.
10102{_}4994{_}Then I began to be anxious.
10102{_}4995{_}I returned to the hotel, resolved to wait for a few hours longer.
10102{_}4996{_}He might have altered his mind and gone to Eastbourne in search of Muriel; yet, had he done so, he would surely have telegraphed to me.
10102{_}4997{_}About four o'clock, as I was passing through the big hall of the hotel, I heard a voice behind me utter a greeting in Italian, and turning in surprise, found Olinto, dressed in his best suit of black, standing hat in hand.
10102{_}4998{_}In an instant I recollected what Jack had told me, and regarded him with some suspicion.
10102{_}4999{_}"Signor Commendatore," he said in a low voice, as though fearing to be overheard, "may I be permitted to speak in private with you?"
10102{_}5000{_}"Certainly," I said, and I took him in the lift up to my room.
10102{_}5001{_}"I have come to warn you, signore," he said, when I had given him a seat.
10102{_}5002{_}"Your enemies mean harm to you."
10102{_}5003{_}"And who are they, pray?"
10102{_}5004{_}I asked, biting my lips.
10102{_}5005{_}"The same, I suppose, who prepared that ingenious trap in Lambeth?"
10102{_}5006{_}"I am not here to reveal to you who they are, signore, only to warn you to have a care of yourself," was the Italian's reply.
10102{_}5007{_}"Look here, Olinto!"
10102{_}5008{_}I exclaimed determinedly, "I've had enough of this confounded mystery.
10102{_}5009{_}Tell me the truth regarding the assassination of your poor wife up in Scotland."
10102{_}5010{_}"Ah, signore!"
10102{_}5011{_}he answered sadly in a changed voice, "I do not know.
10102{_}5012{_}It was a plot.
10102{_}5013{_}Someone represented me--but he was killed also.
10102{_}5014{_}They believed they had struck me down," he added, with a bitter laugh.
10102{_}5015{_}"Poor Armida's body was found concealed behind a rock on the opposite side of the wood.
10102{_}5016{_}I saw it--ah!"
10102{_}5017{_}he cried shuddering.
10102{_}5018{_}"Then you are ignorant of the identity of your wife's assassin?"
10102{_}5019{_}"Entirely."
10102{_}5020{_}"Tell me one thing," I said.
10102{_}5021{_}"Did Armida possess any trinket in the form of a little enameled cross--like a miniature cross of cavaliere?"
10102{_}5022{_}"Yes; I gave it to her.
10102{_}5023{_}I found it on the floor at the Mansion House, where I was engaged as odd waiter for a banquet.
10102{_}5024{_}I know I ought to have given it up to the Lord Mayor's servants, but it was such a pretty little thing that I was tempted to keep it.
10102{_}5025{_}It probably had fallen from the coat of one of the diplomatists dining there."
10102{_}5026{_}I was silent.
10102{_}5027{_}The faint suspicion that Oberg had been at that spot was now entirely removed.
10102{_}5028{_}The only clue I had was satisfactorily accounted for.
10102{_}5029{_}"Why do you ask, Signor Commendatore?"
10102{_}5030{_}he added.
10102{_}5031{_}"Because the cross was found at the spot, and was believed to have been dropped by the assassin," I said.
10102{_}5032{_}The police had, it seemed, succeeded in discovering the unfortunate woman after all, and had found that she was his wife.
10102{_}5033{_}"You know a man named Leithcourt?"
10102{_}5034{_}I asked a few moments later.
10102{_}5035{_}"Now, tell the truth.
10102{_}5036{_}In this affair, Olinto, our interests are mutual, are they not?"
10102{_}5037{_}He nodded, after a moment's hesitation.
10102{_}5038{_}"And you know also a man named Archer--who is sometimes known as Hornby, or Woodroffe--as well as a friend of his called Chater."
10102{_}5039{_}"Si, signore," he said.
10102{_}5040{_}"I have met them all--to my regret."
10102{_}5041{_}"And have you ever met a Russian--a certain Baron Oberg--and his niece, Elma Heath?"
10102{_}5042{_}"His niece?
10102{_}5043{_}She isn't his niece."
10102{_}5044{_}"Then who is she?"
10102{_}5045{_}I demanded.
10102{_}5046{_}"How do I know?
10102{_}5047{_}I have seen her once or twice.
10102{_}5048{_}But she's dead, isn't she?
10102{_}5049{_}She knew the secret of those men, and they intended to kill her.
10102{_}5050{_}I tried to prevent them taking her away on the yacht, and I would have gone to the police--only I dare not."
10102{_}5051{_}"Why?"
10102{_}5052{_}"Well, because my own hands were not quite clean," he answered after a pause, his eyes fixed upon mine the while.
10102{_}5053{_}"I knew they intended to silence her, but I was powerless to save her, poor young lady.
10102{_}5054{_}They took her on board Leithcourt's yacht, the _Iris_, and they sailed for the Mediterranean, I believe."
10102{_}5055{_}"Then the name and appearance of the yacht was altered on the voyage, and it became the _Lola_," I said.
10102{_}5056{_}"No doubt," he smiled.
10102{_}5057{_}"The _Iris_ was a steamer of many names, and had, I believe, been painted nearly all the colors of the rainbow at various times.
10102{_}5058{_}It was a mysterious vessel, but she exists no more.
10102{_}5059{_}They scuttled her somewhere up in the Baltic, I've heard."
10102{_}5060{_}"And who is this Oberg?"
10102{_}5061{_}I inquired, urging him to reveal to me all he knew concerning him.
10102{_}5062{_}"He stands in great fear of the poor young lady, I believe, for it was at his instigation that Leithcourt and his friends took her on that fatal yachting cruise."
10102{_}5063{_}"And what was your connection with them?"
10102{_}5064{_}"Well, I was Leithcourt's servant," was his reply.
10102{_}5065{_}"I was steward on the _Iris_ for a year, until I suppose they thought that I began to see too much, and then I was placed in a position ashore."
10102{_}5066{_}"And what did you see?"
10102{_}5067{_}"More than I care to tell, signore.
10102{_}5068{_}If they were arrested I should be arrested, too, you see."
10102{_}5069{_}"But I mean to solve this mystery, Olinto," I said fiercely, for I was in no trifling mood.
10102{_}5070{_}"I'll fathom it if it costs me my life."
10102{_}5071{_}"If the signore solves it himself, then I cannot be charged with revealing the truth," was the man's diplomatic reply.
10102{_}5072{_}"But I fear that they are far too wary."
10102{_}5073{_}"Armida has lost her life.
10102{_}5074{_}Surely that is sufficient incentive for you to bring them all to justice?"
10102{_}5075{_}"Of course.
10102{_}5076{_}But if the law falls upon them, it will also fall upon me."
10102{_}5077{_}I explained the terrible affliction to which my love had been subjected by those heartless brutes, whereupon he cried enthusiastically:  "Then she is not dead!
10102{_}5078{_}She can tell us everything!"
10102{_}5079{_}"But cannot you tell us?"
10102{_}5080{_}"No; not all.
10102{_}5081{_}The secret she knows has never been revealed.
10102{_}5082{_}They feared she might be incautious, and for that reason Oberg made the villainous suggestion of the yachting trip.
10102{_}5083{_}She was to be drowned--accidentally, of course."
10102{_}5084{_}"She is in St. Petersburg now.
10102{_}5085{_}I left her a week ago."
10102{_}5086{_}"In Russia!
10102{_}5087{_}Ah, signore, for her sake, don't allow the young lady to remain there.
10102{_}5088{_}The Baron is all-powerful.
10102{_}5089{_}He does what he wishes in Russia, and the more merciless he is to the people he governs, the greater rewards he receives from the Czar.
10102{_}5090{_}I have never been in Russia, but surely it must be a strange country, signore!"
10102{_}5091{_}"Well," I said, sitting upon the edge of the bed and looking at him.
10102{_}5092{_}"Are you prepared to denounce them if I bring the Signorina Heath here, to England?"
10102{_}5093{_}"But what is the use, if we have no clear proof?"
10102{_}5094{_}was his evasive reply.
10102{_}5095{_}I could see plainly that he feared being himself implicated in some extraordinary plot, the exact nature of which he so steadfastly refused to reveal to me.
10102{_}5096{_}We talked on for fully half an hour, and from his conversation I gathered that he was well acquainted with Elma.
10102{_}5097{_}"Ah, signore, she was such a pleasant and kind-hearted young lady.
10102{_}5098{_}I always felt very sorry for her.
10102{_}5099{_}She was in deadly fear of them."
10102{_}5100{_}"Because they were thieves?"
10102{_}5101{_}I hazarded.
10102{_}5102{_}"Ah, worse!"
10102{_}5103{_}"But why did they induce you to entice me to that house in Lambeth?
10102{_}5104{_}Why did they so evidently desire that I should be killed?"
10102{_}5105{_}"By accident," he interrupted, correcting me.
10102{_}5106{_}"Always by accident," and he smiled grimly.
10102{_}5107{_}"Surely you know their secret motive?"
10102{_}5108{_}I remarked.
10102{_}5109{_}"At the time I did not," he declared.
10102{_}5110{_}"I acted on their instructions, being compelled to, for they hold my future in their hands.
10102{_}5111{_}Therefore I could not disobey.
10102{_}5112{_}You knew too much, therefore you were marked down for death--just as you are now."
10102{_}5113{_}"And who is it who is now seeking my life?"
10102{_}5114{_}I inquired gravely.
10102{_}5115{_}"I only returned from Russia yesterday."
10102{_}5116{_}"Your movements are well known," answered the young Italian.
10102{_}5117{_}"You cannot be too careful.
10102{_}5118{_}Woodroffe has been in Russia with you, has he not?"
10102{_}5119{_}I replied in the affirmative, whereupon he said:  "I thought so, but was not quite sure."
10102{_}5120{_}"And Chater?"
10102{_}5121{_}I inquired; "where is he?"
10102{_}5122{_}"In London."
10102{_}5123{_}"And the Leithcourts?"
10102{_}5124{_}He shrugged his shoulders with a gesture of ignorance, adding: "The Signorina Muriel returned to London from Eastbourne this morning."
10102{_}5125{_}"Where can I find her?"
10102{_}5126{_}I inquired eagerly.
10102{_}5127{_}"It is of the utmost importance that I should see her."
10102{_}5128{_}"She is with a relation, a cousin, I think, at Bassett Road, Notting Hill.
10102{_}5129{_}The house is called 'Holmwood.'"
10102{_}5130{_}"You have seen her?"
10102{_}5131{_}"No.
10102{_}5132{_}I heard she had returned."
10102{_}5133{_}"And her father is still in hiding from Chater?"
10102{_}5134{_}"He is still in hiding, but Chater is his best friend."
10102{_}5135{_}"That is curious," I remarked, recollecting the hurried departure from Rannoch.
10102{_}5136{_}"They've made it up, I suppose?"
10102{_}5137{_}"They never quarreled, to my knowledge."
10102{_}5138{_}"Then why did Leithcourt leave Scotland so hurriedly on Chater's arrival?
10102{_}5139{_}You know all about the affair, of course?"
10102{_}5140{_}He nodded, saying with a grim smile, "Yes; I know.
10102{_}5141{_}The party up there must have been a very interesting one.
10102{_}5142{_}If the police could have made a raid on the place they would have found among the guests certain persons long 'wanted.'
10102{_}5143{_}But the arrival of Chater and the flight of Leithcourt had an ulterior object.
10102{_}5144{_}Chater had never been Leithcourt's enemy."
10102{_}5145{_}"But I can't understand that," I said.
10102{_}5146{_}"Why should Leithcourt have attacked Chater, rendered him unconscious, and shut him up in the cupboard in the library?"
10102{_}5147{_}"Was it Leithcourt who did that?"
10102{_}5148{_}he asked dubiously.
10102{_}5149{_}"I think not.
10102{_}5150{_}It was another of the guests who was Chater's bitterest enemy.
10102{_}5151{_}But Philip Leithcourt took advantage of the fracas in order to make believe that he had fled because of Chater's arrival.
10102{_}5152{_}Ah!"
10102{_}5153{_}he added, "you haven't any idea of their ruses.
10102{_}5154{_}They are amazing!"
10102{_}5155{_}"So it seems," I said, nevertheless only half convinced that the Italian was telling me the truth.
10102{_}5156{_}If it was really, as he had said, that the arrival of Chater and the flight was merely a "blind," then the mystery was again deepened.
10102{_}5157{_}"Then who was the man who attacked Chater?"
10102{_}5158{_}I asked.
10102{_}5159{_}"Only Chater himself knows.
10102{_}5160{_}It was one of the guests, that is quite evident."
10102{_}5161{_}"And you say that the flight had been prearranged?"
10102{_}5162{_}I remarked.
10102{_}5163{_}"Yes, with a distinct motive," he said; then, after a pause, he added, with a strange, earnest look in his dark eyes, "Pardon me, Signor Commendatore, if I presume to suggest something, will you not?"
10102{_}5164{_}"Certainly.
10102{_}5165{_}What do you suggest?"
10102{_}5166{_}"That you should remain here, in this hotel, and not venture out."
10102{_}5167{_}"For fear of something unfortunate happening to me!"
10102{_}5168{_}I laughed.
10102{_}5169{_}"I'm really not afraid, Olinto," I added.
10102{_}5170{_}"You know I carry this," and I drew out my revolver from my hip-pocket.
10102{_}5171{_}"I know, signore," he said anxiously.
10102{_}5172{_}"But you might not be afforded opportunity for using it.
10102{_}5173{_}When they lay a trap they bait it well."
10102{_}5174{_}"I know.
10102{_}5175{_}They're a set of the most ingenious scoundrels in London, it is very evident.
10102{_}5176{_}Yet I don't fear them in the least," I declared.
10102{_}5177{_}"I must rescue the Signorina Heath."
10102{_}5178{_}"But, signore, have a care for yourself," cried the Italian, laying his hand upon my arm.
10102{_}5179{_}"You are a marked man.
10102{_}5180{_}Ah!
10102{_}5181{_}do I not know," he exclaimed breathlessly.
10102{_}5182{_}"If you go out you may run right into--well, the fatal accident."
10102{_}5183{_}"Never fear, Olinto," I said reassuringly.
10102{_}5184{_}"I shall keep my eyes well open.
10102{_}5185{_}Here, in London, one's life is safer than anywhere else in the world, perhaps--certainly safer than in some places I could name in your own country, eh?"
10102{_}5186{_}at which he grinned.
10102{_}5187{_}The next moment he grew serious again, and said:  "I only warn the signore that if he goes out it is at his own peril."
10102{_}5188{_}"Then let it be so," I laughed, feeling self-confident that no one could lead me into any trap.
10102{_}5189{_}I was neither a foreigner nor a country cousin.
10102{_}5190{_}I knew London too well.
10102{_}5191{_}He was silent and shook his head; then, after telling me that he was still at the same restaurant in Westbourne Grove, he took his departure, warning me once more not to go forth.
10102{_}5192{_}Half an hour later, disregarding his words, I strode out into the Strand, and again walked round to the "Junior."
10102{_}5193{_}The short wintry day had ended, the gas-lamps were lit, and the darkness of night was gradually creeping on.
10102{_}5194{_}Jack had not been to the club, and I began now to grow thoroughly uneasy.
10102{_}5195{_}He had parted from me at the corner of the Strand with only a five minutes' walk before him, and yet he had apparently disappeared.
10102{_}5196{_}My first impulse was to drive to Notting Hill to inquire of Muriel if she had news of him, but somehow the Italian's warning words made me wonder if he had met with foul play.
10102{_}5197{_}I suddenly recollected those two men who had passed by as we had talked, and how that the features of one had seemed strangely familiar.
10102{_}5198{_}Therefore I took a cab to the police-station down at Whitehall, and made inquiry of the inspector on duty in the big bare office with its flaring gas-jets in wire globes.
10102{_}5199{_}He heard me to the end, then turning back the book of "occurrences" before him, glanced through the ruled entries.
10102{_}5200{_}"I should think this is the gentleman, sir," he said.
10102{_}5201{_}And he read to me the entry as follows:  "P.C.
10102{_}5202{_}462A reports that at 2.07 a.m., while on duty outside the National Gallery, he heard a revolver shot, followed by a man's cry.
10102{_}5203{_}He ran to the corner of Suffolk Street, where he found a gentleman lying upon the pavement suffering from a serious shot-wound in the chest and quite unconscious.
10102{_}5204{_}He obtained the assistance of P.C.
10102{_}5205{_}'s 218A and 343A, and the gentleman, who was not identified, was taken to the Charing Cross Hospital, where the house-surgeon expressed a doubt whether he could live.
10102{_}5206{_}Neither P.C.
10102{_}5207{_}'s recollect having noticed any suspicious-looking person in the vicinity.
10102{_}5208{_}"JOHN PERCIVAL, _Inspector_."
10102{_}5209{_}I waited for no more, but rushed round to the hospital in the cab, and was, five minutes later, taken along the ward, where I identified poor Jack lying in bed, white-faced and unconscious.
10102{_}5210{_}"The doctor was here a quarter of an hour ago," whispered the sister.
10102{_}5211{_}"And he fears he is sinking."
10102{_}5212{_}"He has uttered no words?"
10102{_}5213{_}I asked anxiously.
10102{_}5214{_}"Made no statement?"
10102{_}5215{_}"None.
10102{_}5216{_}He has never regained consciousness, and I fear, sir, he never will.
10102{_}5217{_}It is a case of deliberate murder, the police told me early this morning."
10102{_}5218{_}I clenched my fists and swore a fierce revenge for that dastardly act.
10102{_}5219{_}And as I stood beside the narrow bed, I realized that what Olinto had said regarding my own peril was the actual truth.
10102{_}5220{_}I was a marked man.
10102{_}5221{_}Was I never to penetrate that inscrutable and ever-increasing mystery?
10102{_}5222{_}CHAPTER XVII  THE TRUTH ABOUT THE "LOLA"   Throughout the long night I called many times at the hospital, but the reply was always the same.
10102{_}5223{_}Jack had not regained consciousness, and the doctor regarded his case as hopeless.
10102{_}5224{_}In the morning I drove in hot haste to Bassett Road, Notting Hill, and at the address Olinto had given me found Muriel.
10102{_}5225{_}When she entered the room with folding doors into which I had been shown, I saw that she was pale and apprehensive, for we had not met since her flight, and she was, no doubt, at a loss for an explanation.
10102{_}5226{_}But I did not press her for one.
10102{_}5227{_}I merely told her that the Italian Santini had given me her address and that I came as bearer of unfortunate news.
10102{_}5228{_}"What is it?"
10102{_}5229{_}she gasped quickly.
10102{_}5230{_}"It concerns Captain Durnford," I replied.
10102{_}5231{_}"He has been injured in the street, and is in Charing Cross Hospital."
10102{_}5232{_}"Ah!"
10102{_}5233{_}she cried.
10102{_}5234{_}"I see.
10102{_}5235{_}You do not explain the truth.
10102{_}5236{_}By your face I can tell there is something more.
10102{_}5237{_}He's dead!
10102{_}5238{_}Tell me the worst."
10102{_}5239{_}"No, Miss Leithcourt," I said gravely, "not dead, but the doctors fear that he may not recover.
10102{_}5240{_}His wound is dangerous.
10102{_}5241{_}He has been shot by some unknown person."
10102{_}5242{_}"Shot!"
10102{_}5243{_}she echoed, bursting into tears.
10102{_}5244{_}"Then they have followed him, after all!
10102{_}5245{_}They have deceived me, and now, as they intend to take him from me, I will myself protect him.
10102{_}5246{_}You, Mr. Gregg, have been in peril of your life, that I know, but Jack's enemies are yours, and they shall not go unpunished.
10102{_}5247{_}May I see him?"
10102{_}5248{_}"I fear not, but we will ask at the hospital."
10102{_}5249{_}And after the exchange of some further explanations, we took a hansom back to Charing Cross.
10102{_}5250{_}At first the sister refused to allow Muriel to see the patient, but she implored so earnestly that at last she consented, and the distressed girl in the black coat and hat crept on tiptoe to the bedside.
10102{_}5251{_}"He was conscious for a quarter of an hour or so," whispered the nurse who sat there, "He asked after some lady named Muriel."
10102{_}5252{_}The girl at my side burst into low sobbing.
10102{_}5253{_}"Tell him," she said, "that Muriel is here--that she has seen him, and is waiting for him to recover."
10102{_}5254{_}We were not allowed to linger there, and on leaving the hospital I took her back again to Notting Hill, promising to keep her well informed of Jack's condition.
10102{_}5255{_}He had returned to consciousness, therefore there was now a faint hope for his recovery.
10102{_}5256{_}Day succeeded day, and although I was not allowed to visit my friend, I was told that he was very slowly progressing.
10102{_}5257{_}I idled at the Hotel Cecil longing daily for news of Elma.
10102{_}5258{_}Only once did a letter come from her, a brief, well-written note from which it appeared that she was quite well and happy, although she longed to be able to go out.
10102{_}5259{_}The Princess was very kind indeed to her, and, she added, was making secret arrangements for her escape across the Russian frontier into Germany.
10102{_}5260{_}I knew what that meant.
10102{_}5261{_}Use was to be made of certain Russian officials who were secretly allied with the Revolutionists in order to secure her safe conduct beyond the power of that order of exile of the tyrant de Plehve.
10102{_}5262{_}I wrote to her under cover to the Princess, but there had been no time yet for a reply.
10102{_}5263{_}I saw Muriel many times, but never once did she refer to Rannoch or their sudden departure.
10102{_}5264{_}Her only thought was of the man she loved.
10102{_}5265{_}"I always believed that you were engaged to Mr. Woodroffe," I said one day, when I called to tell her of Jack's latest bulletin.
10102{_}5266{_}"It is true that he asked me to marry him," she responded.
10102{_}5267{_}"But there were reasons why I did not accept."
10102{_}5268{_}"Reasons connected with his past, eh?"
10102{_}5269{_}She smiled, and then said:  "Ah, Mr. Gregg, it is all a strange and very tragic story.
10102{_}5270{_}I must see Jack.
10102{_}5271{_}When do you think they will allow me to go to him?"
10102{_}5272{_}I explained that the doctor feared to cause the patient any undue excitement, but that in two or three days there was hope of her being allowed to visit him.
10102{_}5273{_}Several times the police made inquiry of me, but I could tell them nothing.
10102{_}5274{_}I could not for the life of me recollect where I had before seen the face of that man who had passed in the darkness.
10102{_}5275{_}One afternoon, ten days after the attempt upon Jack, I was allowed to sit by his bedside and question him.
10102{_}5276{_}"Ah, Gordon, old fellow!"
10102{_}5277{_}he said faintly, "I've had a narrow escape--by Jove!
10102{_}5278{_}After I left you I walked quickly on towards the club, when, all of a sudden, two scoundrels sprang out of Suffolk Street, and one of them fired a revolver full at me.
10102{_}5279{_}Then I knew no more."
10102{_}5280{_}"But who were the men?
10102{_}5281{_}Did you recognize them?"
10102{_}5282{_}"No, not at all.
10102{_}5283{_}That's the worst of it."
10102{_}5284{_}"But Muriel knows who they were!"
10102{_}5285{_}I said.
10102{_}5286{_}"Ah, yes!
10102{_}5287{_}Bring her here, won't you?"
10102{_}5288{_}the poor fellow implored, "I'm dying to see her once again."
10102{_}5289{_}Then I told him how she had looked upon him while unconscious, and how I had taken the daily bulletin to her.
10102{_}5290{_}For an hour I talked with him, urging him to get well soon, so that we could unite in probing the mystery, and bringing to justice those responsible for the dastardly act.
10102{_}5291{_}"Muriel knows, and if she loves you she will no doubt assist us," I said.
10102{_}5292{_}"Oh, she does love me, Gordon, I know that," said the prostrate man, smiling contentedly, and when I left I promised to bring her there on the morrow.
10102{_}5293{_}This I did, but having conducted her to the bed at the end of the ward I discreetly withdrew.
10102{_}5294{_}What she said to him I am not, of course, aware.
10102{_}5295{_}All I know is that an hour later when I returned I found them the happiest pair possible to conceive, and I clearly saw that Jack's trust in her was not ill-placed.
10102{_}5296{_}But of Elma?
10102{_}5297{_}No further word had come from her, and I began to grow uneasy.
10102{_}5298{_}The days went on.
10102{_}5299{_}I wrote twice, but no reply was forthcoming.
10102{_}5300{_}At last I could bear the suspense no longer, and began to contemplate returning to Russia.
10102{_}5301{_}Jack, when at last discharged from the hospital, came across to the Cecil and lived with me in preference to the "Junior."
10102{_}5302{_}He was very weak at first, and I looked after him, while every day Muriel came and ate with us, brightening our lives by her smart and merry chatter.
10102{_}5303{_}She knew that I loved Elma and was also aware of the exciting events in Russia, Jack having told her of them during their long drives in hansoms when he went out with her to take the air.
10102{_}5304{_}One day I received a brief note from the Princess in Petersburg, urging me to remain patient and saying Elma was quite safe and well.
10102{_}5305{_}There were reasons, however, why she was unable to write, she added.
10102{_}5306{_}What were they, I wondered?
10102{_}5307{_}Yet I could only wait until I received word to travel back to Russia and fetch her home.
10102{_}5308{_}The Princess had promised to arrange everything.
10102{_}5309{_}December came, and we still remained on at the hotel.
10102{_}5310{_}Once Olinto had written me repeating his warning, but I did not heed it.
10102{_}5311{_}I somehow distrusted the fellow.
10102{_}5312{_}Jack, now thoroughly recovered, called almost daily at Bassett Road, and would often bring Muriel to the Cecil to tea or to luncheon.
10102{_}5313{_}Often I inquired the whereabouts of her father and of Hylton Chater, but she declared herself in entire ignorance, and believed they were abroad.
10102{_}5314{_}One afternoon, shortly before Christmas, as we were idling in the American bar of the hotel, my friend told me that Muriel had invited us to tea at her cousin's that afternoon, and accordingly we went there in company.
10102{_}5315{_}The drawing-room into which we were ushered was familiar to me as the apartment wherein I had told Muriel of the attempt upon her lover's life.
10102{_}5316{_}As we sat together Muriel, a smart figure in a pale blue gown, poured tea for us and chatted more merrily, I thought, than ever before.
10102{_}5317{_}She seemed quick and nervous and yet full of happiness, as she should indeed have been, for Jack Durnford was one of the best fellows in the world, and his restoration to health little short of miraculous.
10102{_}5318{_}"Gordon," he said to me with a sudden seriousness when tea had ended and we had placed down our cups.
10102{_}5319{_}"I want to tell you something--something I've been longing always to tell you, and now I have got dear Muriel's consent.
10102{_}5320{_}I want to tell you about her father and his friends."
10102{_}5321{_}"And about Elma, too?"
10102{_}5322{_}I said in quick eagerness.
10102{_}5323{_}"Yes, tell me everything."
10102{_}5324{_}"No, not everything, for I don't know it myself.
10102{_}5325{_}But what I know I will explain as briefly as I can, and leave you to form your own conclusions.
10102{_}5326{_}It is," he went on, "a strange--most amazing story.
10102{_}5327{_}When I myself became first cognizant of the mystery I was on board the flagship the _Renown_, under Admiral Sir John Fisher.
10102{_}5328{_}We were lying in Malta when there arrived the English yacht _Iris_, owned by Mr. Philip Leithcourt, and among those on board cruising for pleasure were Mr. Martin Woodroffe, Mr. Hylton Chater, and the owner's wife and daughter Muriel.
10102{_}5329{_}"Muriel and I met first at a tennis-party, and afterwards frequently at various houses in Malta, for anyone who goes there and entertains is soon entertained in return.
10102{_}5330{_}A mutual attachment sprang up between Muriel and myself," he said, placing his hand tenderly upon hers and smiling, "and we often met in secret and took long walks, until quite suddenly Leithcourt said that it was necessary to sail for Smyrna to pick up some friends who had been traveling in Palestine.
10102{_}5331{_}The night they sailed a great consternation was caused on the island by the news that the safe in the Admiral Superintendent's office had been opened by expert safe-breakers, and certain most important secret documents stolen."
10102{_}5332{_}"Well?"
10102{_}5333{_}I asked, much interested.
10102{_}5334{_}"Again, two months later, when the villa of the Prince of Montevachi, at Palmero, was broken into and the whole of the famous jewels of the Princess stolen, it was a very strange fact that the _Iris_ was at the moment in that port.
10102{_}5335{_}But it was not until the third occasion, when the yacht was at Villefranche, and our squadron being at Toulon I got four days' leave to go along the Riviera, that my suspicions were aroused, for at the very hour when I was dining at the London House at Nice with Muriel and a schoolfellow of hers, Elma Heath--who was spending the winter there with a lady who was Baron Oberg's cousin--that a great robbery was committed in one of the big hotels up at Cimiez, the wife of an American millionaire losing jewels valued at thirty thousand pounds.
10102{_}5336{_}Then the robberies, coincident with the visit of the yacht, aroused my strong suspicion.
10102{_}5337{_}I remarked the nature of those documents stolen from Malta, and recognized that they could only be of service to a foreign government.
10102{_}5338{_}Then came the Leghorn incident of which you told me.
10102{_}5339{_}The yacht's name had been changed to the _Lola_, and she had been repainted.
10102{_}5340{_}I made searching inquiry, and found that on the evening she was purposely run aground in order to strike up a friendship at the Consulate, a Russian gunboat was lying in the vicinity.
10102{_}5341{_}The Consul's safe was rifled, and the scheme certainly was to transfer anything obtained from it to the Russian gunboat."
10102{_}5342{_}"But what was in the safe?"
10102{_}5343{_}I asked.
10102{_}5344{_}"Fortunately nothing.
10102{_}5345{_}But you see they knew that our squadron was due in Leghorn, and that some extremely important despatches were on the way to the Admiral--secret orders based upon the decision of the British Cabinet as to the vexed question of Russian ships passing the Dardanelles--they expected that they would be lodged in the safe until the arrival of the squadron, as they always are.
10102{_}5346{_}They were, however, bitterly disappointed because the despatches had not arrived."
10102{_}5347{_}"And then?"
10102{_}5348{_}"Well, the only Russian who appeared to have any connection with them was Baron Oberg, the Governor-General of Finland, whose habit it was to spend part of the winter in the Mediterranean.
10102{_}5349{_}From Elma Heath's conversation at dinner that evening at Nice I gathered that she and her uncle had been guests on the _Iris_ on several occasions, although I must say that Muriel was extremely reticent regarding all that concerned the yacht."
10102{_}5350{_}"Of course," she said quickly.
10102{_}5351{_}"Now that I have told you the truth, Jack, don't you think it was only natural?"
10102{_}5352{_}"Most certainly, dear," he answered, still holding her hand.
10102{_}5353{_}"Yours was not a secret that you could very well tell to me until you could thoroughly trust me, especially as your father had been implicated in the theft of those documents from Malta.
10102{_}5354{_}The truth is," he said, turning to me, "Philip Leithcourt has all along been the catspaw of Baron Oberg.
10102{_}5355{_}A few years ago he was a well-known money-lender in the city, and in that capacity met the Baron, who, being in disgrace, required a loan.
10102{_}5356{_}He was also in the habit of having certain shady transactions with that daring gang of continental thieves of whom Dick Archer and Hylton Chater were leaders.
10102{_}5357{_}For this reason he purchased a yacht for their use, so that they might not only use it for the purpose of storing the stolen goods, but for the purpose of sailing from place to place under the guise of wealthy Englishmen traveling for pleasure.
10102{_}5358{_}Upon that vessel, indeed, was stored thousands and thousands of pounds' worth of jewels and objects of value, the proceeds of many great robberies in England, France and Belgium.
10102{_}5359{_}Sometimes they traveled for the purpose of disposing of the jewels in various inland towns where the gems, having been recut, were not recognized, while at other times, Chater and Archer, assisted by Mackintosh, the captain, and Olinto Santini, the steward, sailed for a port, landed, committed a robbery, and then sailed away again, quite unsuspected, as rich Englishmen."
10102{_}5360{_}"And the crew?"
10102{_}5361{_}I asked, after a pause.
10102{_}5362{_}"They were, of course, well paid, and were kept in ignorance of what the supposed owner and his friends did ashore."
10102{_}5363{_}"But Oberg's connection with it?"
10102{_}5364{_}I asked, surprised at those revelations.
10102{_}5365{_}"Ah!"
10102{_}5366{_}exclaimed Muriel.
10102{_}5367{_}"The ingenuity of that crafty villain is fiendish.
10102{_}5368{_}Before he got into the Czar's favor he owed my father a large sum, and then sought how to evade repayment.
10102{_}5369{_}By means of his spies he discovered the real purpose of the cruises of the _Iris_--for I was often taken on board with a maid in order to allay any suspicion that might arise if only men were cruising.
10102{_}5370{_}Then he not only compelled my father to cancel the debt, but he impressed the vessel and those who owned and navigated it into the secret service of Russia.
10102{_}5371{_}A dozen times did we make attempts to obtain secret papers from Italian, French and English dockyards, but only once in the case of Malta and once at Toulon did we succeed.
10102{_}5372{_}Ah!
10102{_}5373{_}Mr. Gregg," she added, "you do not know all the anxiety I suffered, how at every hour we were in danger of betrayal or capture, and of the hundred narrow escapes we have had of Custom House officers rummaging the yacht for contraband.
10102{_}5374{_}You will no doubt recollect the sensation caused by the theft of the jewels of the Princess Wilhelmine of Schaumbourg-Lippe from the lady's-maid in the rapide between Cannes and Les Arcs, the robbery from the Marseilles branch of the Credit Lyonnais, and the great haul of plate from the chateau of Bardon, the Paris millionaire, close to Arcachon."
10102{_}5375{_}"Yes," I said, for they were all robberies of which I had read in the newspapers a couple of years before.
10102{_}5376{_}"Well," she said, "they were all committed by Archer or Woodroffe and his gang--with accomplices ashore, of course--and never once did it seem that any suspicion fell upon us.
10102{_}5377{_}While the police were frantically searching hither and thither, we used to weigh anchor and calmly steam away with our booty on board.
10102{_}5378{_}We had with us an old Dutch lapidary, and one of the cabins was fitted as a workshop, where he altered the appearance of the stones, and prepared them ready for sale, while the gold was melted in a crucible and put ashore to be sent to agents in Hamburg."
10102{_}5379{_}"But that night in Leghorn?"
10102{_}5380{_}I said.
10102{_}5381{_}"What happened to poor Elma?"
10102{_}5382{_}"I do not know," was Muriel's reply.
10102{_}5383{_}"We were both on board together, and standing at the crack of the door watched you sitting at dinner that evening.
10102{_}5384{_}Elma told me that she believed that there was a plot against your life, but why she would not tell me.
10102{_}5385{_}She evidently knew of the proposed rifling of the safe at the Consulate.
10102{_}5386{_}Oberg himself was also on board, locked in his own cabin.
10102{_}5387{_}Elma must have overheard some conversation between the Baron and one of the others, for she was in great fear the whole time lest they might injure you.
10102{_}5388{_}Yet it seemed, after all, as though their idea was the same as always, to worm themselves into your confidence.
10102{_}5389{_}The instant, however, you went ashore, Chater, Woodroffe--whom you called Hornby--and Mackintosh, the captain--who, by the way, was an old ticket-of-leave man--went ashore, and, of course, broke into the Consulate.
10102{_}5390{_}Then, as soon as they returned, Elma came to my cabin, awoke me, and said that the Baron was taking her ashore, and that they were to travel overland back to London.
10102{_}5391{_}She was ready dressed to go, therefore I kissed her, and promising to meet her soon, we parted.
10102{_}5392{_}That was the last I saw of her.
10102{_}5393{_}What happened to her afterwards only she alone can tell us."
10102{_}5394{_}"But she is not the Baron's niece?"
10102{_}5395{_}I said.
10102{_}5396{_}"No.
10102{_}5397{_}There is some mystery," declared Muriel.
10102{_}5398{_}"She holds some secret which he fears she may divulge.
10102{_}5399{_}But of what nature, I am in ignorance."
10102{_}5400{_}"Then you say that your father has never taken any active part in the robberies?"
10102{_}5401{_}I remarked.
10102{_}5402{_}"No.
10102{_}5403{_}He commenced by lending money, and amassed a considerable fortune.
10102{_}5404{_}Then avarice seized him, as it does so many men, and coming into contact with Archer and his friends, he saw that the idea of the yacht was a safe and profitable one.
10102{_}5405{_}Therefore he purchased the vessel, and ran it at the disposition of the thieves, and subsequently under compulsion in the secret service of Russia, as I have already described to you.
10102{_}5406{_}The profits were colossal.
10102{_}5407{_}In one year my father's share was eighty thousand pounds."
10102{_}5408{_}"And where is your father now?"
10102{_}5409{_}I asked.
10102{_}5410{_}"Ah!"
10102{_}5411{_}she exclaimed sadly, her face pale and haggard.
10102{_}5412{_}"I have heard that the vessel was scuttled somewhere in the Baltic."
10102{_}5413{_}"That is true.
10102{_}5414{_}Oberg's purpose having been served, he demanded half the property on board, or he would give notice to the Russian naval authorities that the pirate yacht was afloat.
10102{_}5415{_}He attempted to blackmail my father, as he had already done so many times, but his scheme was frustrated.
10102{_}5416{_}My father, because of his inhuman treatment of poor Elma, defied him, when it appears that Oberg, who was in Helsingfors, telegraphed to the admiral of the Russian fleet in the Baltic.
10102{_}5417{_}The crew from the _Iris_ were at once landed at Riga, and only Mackintosh and my father put to sea again.
10102{_}5418{_}Ah!
10102{_}5419{_}my father was desperate, for he knew the merciless character of that man whose victim he had been for so long.
10102{_}5420{_}They watched a Russian cruiser bearing down upon them, when, just as it drew near, they got off in a boat and blew up the yacht, which sank in three minutes with its ill-obtained wealth on board."
10102{_}5421{_}"And your father?"
10102{_}5422{_}She was silent, and I saw tears standing in her eyes.
10102{_}5423{_}"There was a tragedy," Jack explained in a low, hoarse voice.
10102{_}5424{_}"He and the captain did not, unfortunately, get sufficiently far from the yacht when they blew her up, and they went down with her."
10102{_}5425{_}And I looked in silence at Muriel, who stood with her head bent and her white face covered with her hands.
10102{_}5426{_}Almost at the same moment there was a low tap at the door, and the servant-maid announced:  "Mr. Santini, miss."
10102{_}5427{_}"Ah!"
10102{_}5428{_}exclaimed Jack quickly, as Olinto entered the room.
10102{_}5429{_}"Then you had my note!
10102{_}5430{_}We have asked you here to reveal to us this dastardly plot which seemed to have been formed against Mr. Gregg and myself.
10102{_}5431{_}As you know, I've had a narrow escape."
10102{_}5432{_}"I know, signore.
10102{_}5433{_}And the Signor Commendatore is also threatened."
10102{_}5434{_}"By whom?"
10102{_}5435{_}"By those who killed my poor wife, and who intended also to silence me," was his answer.
10102{_}5436{_}"The same who compelled you take me to that house where the fatal chair was prepared, eh?"
10102{_}5437{_}"It was Archer, who, fearing that you came to London in search of them, devised that devilish contrivance," he said in his broken English.
10102{_}5438{_}Then continuing, he went on fiercely: "Now that I have discovered why my poor Armida was killed, I will tell the truth, and not spare them.
10102{_}5439{_}Since you left Scotland, signore, I have been up in Dumfries, and have discovered several facts which prove that for some reason known only to himself, Leithcourt, while at Rannoch, wrote to both Armida and myself separately, making an appointment to see us at the same time at that spot on the edge of the wood, as he had some secret commission to entrust to us.
10102{_}5440{_}The letter addressed to me apparently fell into someone else's hands--probably one of the secret agents of Baron Oberg, who were always watching Leithcourt's doings, and he, anxious to learn what was intended, made himself up to look like me, and kept the appointment in my place.
10102{_}5441{_}Armida, having received the letter unknown to me, went up to Scotland, and was also there at the appointed time.
10102{_}5442{_}What actually transpired can only be surmised, yet it seems that Leithcourt was in the habit of going up to that spot and loitering there in the evening in order to meet Chater in secret, as the latter was in hiding in a small hotel in Dumfries.
10102{_}5443{_}Therefore those who formed the plot must have endeavored to throw suspicion upon Leithcourt.
10102{_}5444{_}It is plain, however, as both myself and Armida knew the gang, it was to their interest to get rid of us, because the suspicions of the police had at last become aroused.
10102{_}5445{_}Poor Armida was therefore deliberately enticed there to her death, while the inquisitive man whom the assassin took to be myself was also struck down."
10102{_}5446{_}"By whom?"
10102{_}5447{_}"Not by Chater, for he was in London on that night."
10102{_}5448{_}"Then by Woodroffe?"
10102{_}5449{_}Durnford said.
10102{_}5450{_}"Without a doubt.
10102{_}5451{_}It was all most cleverly thought out.
10102{_}5452{_}It was to his advantage alone to close our lips, because in that same fatal chair in Lambeth old Jacob Moser, the Jew bullion-broker of Hatton Garden, met his death--a most dastardly crime, with which none of his friends were associated, and of which we alone held knowledge.
10102{_}5453{_}He therefore wrote to us as though from Leithcourt, calling us up to Rannoch, in order to strike the blows in the darkness," he added in his peculiar Italian manner.
10102{_}5454{_}"Besides, he feared we would tell the signore the truth."
10102{_}5455{_}"You have not told the police?"
10102{_}5456{_}"I dare not, signore.
10102{_}5457{_}Surely the less the police know about this matter the better, otherwise the Signorina Leithcourt must suffer for her father's avarice and evil-doing."
10102{_}5458{_}"Yes," cried Jack anxiously.
10102{_}5459{_}"That's right, Olinto.
10102{_}5460{_}The police must know nothing.
10102{_}5461{_}The reprisals we must make ourselves.
10102{_}5462{_}But who was it who shot me in Suffolk Street?"
10102{_}5463{_}"The same man, Martin Woodroffe."
10102{_}5464{_}"Then the assassin is back from Russia?"
10102{_}5465{_}"He followed closely behind the Signor Commendatore.
10102{_}5466{_}Markoff, a clever secret agent of Baron Oberg's, came with him."
10102{_}5467{_}Then for the first time I recollected that the man I had recognized in the Strand was a fellow I had seen lounging in the ante-room of the palace of the Governor-General of Finland.
10102{_}5468{_}The pair, fearing that I should reveal what I knew, were undoubtedly in London to take my life in secret.
10102{_}5469{_}Now that Leithcourt was dead, Woodroffe had united forces with Oberg, and intended to silence me because they feared that Elma, besides escaping them, had also revealed her secret.
10102{_}5470{_}"I trust that the Signorina Leithcourt has explained the story of the yacht and its crew," Olinto remarked.
10102{_}5471{_}"And has also shown you how I was implicated.
10102{_}5472{_}You will therefore discern the reason why I have hitherto feared to give you any explanation."
10102{_}5473{_}"Yes," I said, "Miss Leithcourt has told me a great deal, but not everything.
10102{_}5474{_}I cannot yet gather for what reason she and her father fled from Rannoch."
10102{_}5475{_}"Then I will tell you," said Muriel quickly.
10102{_}5476{_}"My father suspected Woodroffe of being the assassin in Rannoch Wood, for he knew that he had broken away from the original compact, and had now allied himself with Oberg.
10102{_}5477{_}Yet it was also my father's object to appear in fear of them, because he was only awaiting an opportunity to lay plans for poor Elma's rescue from Finland.
10102{_}5478{_}Therefore one evening Woodroffe called, and my father encountered him in the avenue, and admitted him with his own latchkey by one of the side doors of the castle, afterwards taking him up to the study.
10102{_}5479{_}He knew that he had come to try and make terms for Oberg, therefore he saw that he must fly at once to Newcastle, where the _Iris_ was lying, get on board, and sail away.
10102{_}5480{_}"With some excuse he left him in the study, and then warned my mother and myself to prepare to leave.
10102{_}5481{_}But while we were packing, it appeared that Chater, who had followed, was shown into the study by the butler, or rather he entered there himself, being well acquainted with the house.
10102{_}5482{_}Thus the two men, now bitter enemies, met.
10102{_}5483{_}A fierce quarrel must have ensued, and Chater was poisoned and concealed, Woodroffe, of course, believing he had killed him.
10102{_}5484{_}My father entered the study again, and seeing only Woodroffe there, did not know what had occurred.
10102{_}5485{_}Some words probably arose, when my father again turned and left.
10102{_}5486{_}Then we fled to Carlisle and on to Newcastle, and next morning were on board the yacht out in the North Sea, afterwards landing at Rotterdam.
10102{_}5487{_}Those," she added, "are briefly the facts, as my poor father related them to me."
10102{_}5488{_}"And what of poor Elma--and of her secret?
10102{_}5489{_}When, I wonder, shall I see her?"
10102{_}5490{_}I cried in despair.
10102{_}5491{_}"You will see her now, signore," answered Olinto.
10102{_}5492{_}"A servant of the Princess Zurloff brought her to London this afternoon, and I have just conveyed her from the station.
10102{_}5493{_}She is in the next room, in ignorance, however, that you are here."
10102{_}5494{_}And without another word I fled forward joyfully, and threw open the folding-doors which separated me from my silent love.
10102{_}5495{_}Silent, yes!
10102{_}5496{_}But she could, nevertheless, tell her story--surely the strangest that any woman has ever lived to tell.
10102{_}5497{_}CHAPTER XVIII  CONTAINS ELMA'S STORY   Before me stood my love, a slim, tragic, rather wan figure in a heavy dark traveling-coat and felt toque, her sweet lips parted and a look of bewildered amazement upon her countenance as I burst in so suddenly upon her.
10102{_}5498{_}In silence I grasped her tiny black-gloved hand, and then, also in silence, raised it passionately to my eager lips.
10102{_}5499{_}Her soft, dark eyes--those eyes that spoke although she was mute--met mine, and in them was a look that I had never seen there before--a look which as plainly as any words told me that my wild fevered passion was reciprocated.
10102{_}5500{_}She gazed beyond into the room where the others had assembled, and then looked at me inquiringly, whereupon I led her forward to where they were, and Muriel fell upon her and kissed her with tears streaming from her eyes.
10102{_}5501{_}"I prepared this surprise for you, Mr. Gregg," Muriel said, laughing through her tears of joy.
10102{_}5502{_}"Olinto learnt that she was on her way to London, and I sent him to meet her.
10102{_}5503{_}The Princess has managed magnificently, has she not?"
10102{_}5504{_}"Yes.
10102{_}5505{_}Thank God she is free!"
10102{_}5506{_}I exclaimed.
10102{_}5507{_}"But we must induce her to tell us everything."
10102{_}5508{_}Muriel was already helping my love out of her heavy Russian coat, a costly garment lined with sable, and when, after greeting Jack and Olinto, she was comfortably seated, I took some notepaper from the little writing-table by the window and scribbled in pencil the words:  "I need not write how delighted I am that you are safe--that the Almighty has heard my prayers for you.
10102{_}5509{_}Jack and Muriel have told me all about Leithcourt and his scoundrelly associates.
10102{_}5510{_}I know, too, dear--for I may call you that, may I not?--how terribly you must have suffered in silence through it all.
10102{_}5511{_}Leithcourt is dead.
10102{_}5512{_}He sank the yacht with all the stolen property on board, but by accident was himself engulfed."
10102{_}5513{_}Bending and watching intently as I wrote, she drew back in horror and surprise at the words.
10102{_}5514{_}Then I added: "We are all four determined that the guilty shall not go unpunished, and that the affliction placed upon you shall be adequately avenged.
10102{_}5515{_}You are my own love--I am bold enough to call you so.
10102{_}5516{_}Some strong but mysterious bond of affinity between us caused me to seek you out, and your pictured face seemed to call me to your side although I was unaware of your peril.
10102{_}5517{_}I was sent to you by the unseen power to extricate you from the hands of your enemies.
10102{_}5518{_}Therefore tell us everything--all that you know--without fear, for now that we are united no harm can assail us."
10102{_}5519{_}She took the pencil, and holding it in her white fingers sat staring first at us, and then looking hesitatingly at the white paper before her.
10102{_}5520{_}Her position, amid a hundred conflicting emotions, was one of extreme difficulty.
10102{_}5521{_}It seemed as though even now she was loth to reveal to us the absolute truth.
10102{_}5522{_}Muriel, standing behind her chair, tenderly stroked back the wealth of chestnut hair from her white brow.
10102{_}5523{_}Her complexion was perfect, even though her face was pale and jaded, and her eyes heavy, consequent upon her long, weary journey from the now frozen North.
10102{_}5524{_}Presently, when by signs both Jack and Olinto had urged her to write, she bent suddenly, and her pencil began to run swiftly over the paper.
10102{_}5525{_}All of us stood exchanging glances in silence, neither looking over her, but each determined to wait in patience until the end.
10102{_}5526{_}Once started, however, she did not pause.
10102{_}5527{_}Sheet after sheet she covered.
10102{_}5528{_}The silence for a long time was complete, broken only by the rapid running of the pencil over the rough surface of the paper.
10102{_}5529{_}She had apparently become seized by a sudden determination to explain everything, now that she saw we were in real, dead earnest.
10102{_}5530{_}I watched her sweet face bent so intently, and as the firelight fell across it found it incomparable.
10102{_}5531{_}Yes; she was afflicted by loss of speech, it was true, yet she was surely inexpressibly sweet and womanly, peerless above all others.
10102{_}5532{_}With a deep-drawn sigh she at last finished, and, her head still bowed in an attitude of humiliation, it seemed, she handed what she had written to me.
10102{_}5533{_}In breathless eagerness I read as follows:  "Is it true, dear love--for I call you so in return--that you were impelled towards me by the mysterious hand that directs all things?
10102{_}5534{_}You came in search of me, and you risked your life for mine at Kajana, therefore you have a right to know the truth.
10102{_}5535{_}You, as my champion, and the Princess as my friend, have contrived to effect my freedom.
10102{_}5536{_}Were it not for you, I should ere this have been on my way to Saghalien, to the tomb to which Oberg had so ingeniously contrived to consign me.
10102{_}5537{_}Ah!
10102{_}5538{_}you do not know--you never can know--all that I have suffered ever since I was a girl."
10102{_}5539{_}Here the statement broke off, and recommenced as follows:  "In order that you should understand the truth, I had better begin at the beginning.
10102{_}5540{_}My father was an English merchant in Petersburg, and my mother, Vera Bessanoff, who, before her marriage with my father, was celebrated at Court for her beauty, and was one of the maids-of-honor to the Czarina.
10102{_}5541{_}She was the only daughter of Count Paul Bessanoff, ex-Governor of Kharkoff, and before marrying my father she had, with her mother, been a well-known figure in society.
10102{_}5542{_}Immediately after her marriage her father died, leaving her in possession of an ample fortune, which, with my father's own wealth, placed them among the richest and most influential in Petersburg.
10102{_}5543{_}"Among my father's most intimate friends was Baron Xavier Oberg--who, at that time, held a very subordinate position in the Ministry of the Interior--and from my earliest recollections I can remember him coming frequently to our house and being invited to the brilliant entertainments which my mother gave.
10102{_}5544{_}When I was thirteen, however, my father died of a chill contracted while boar-hunting on his estate in Kiev, and within a few months a further disaster happened to us.
10102{_}5545{_}One night, while I was sitting alone reading aloud to my mother, two strangers were announced, and on being shown in they arrested my dear mother on a charge of complicity in a revolutionary plot against the Czar which had been discovered at Peterhof.
10102{_}5546{_}I stood defiant and indignant, for my mother was certainly no Nihilist, yet they said that the bomb had been introduced into the palace by the Countess Anna Shiproff, one of the ladies-in-waiting, who was an intimate friend of my mother's and often used to visit her.
